God is a woman

by NightsLikeThis

Summary

“It’s not the first time blue eyes do their best not to stare at tender lips, Rio’s bottom lip caught between her own teeth. A focus in brown eyes that never leave Agatha’s cheek.

She tries not to focus on how they’d gotten here, the way Rio had always helped her up to sit on the edge of the bathroom sink closest to the barred window, the way her nails bit into her hips just long enough to press her ass into cold porcelain.“

 

—-

Mostly inspired by Aubrey Plaza and Kathryn Hahn both going to all girls catholic high schools, but also by feeling nostalgic for my teenage years and missing home…

Notes

Disclaimer: this fic contains bible verses, heavy allegory to religion and commentary through the character’s interpretation of Catholicism. It is not my intention to degrade or disrespect anyone’s beliefs. There are also depictions of physical abuse.

See the end of the work for more notes

Chapter 1

1 Peter 5:8 - Be sober-minded; be watchful. Your adversary the devil prowls around like a roaring lion, seeking someone to devour.

Agatha can feel her own heart beat, a thrumming pulse against her spine, a disjointed pressure that betrays the pattern of her breathing.

It’s not the first time blue eyes do their best not to stare at tender lips, Rio’s bottom lip caught between her own teeth. A focus in brown eyes that never leave Agatha’s cheek.

She tries not to focus on how they’d gotten here, the way Rio had always helped her up to sit on the edge of the bathroom sink closest to the barred window, the way her nails bit into her hips just long enough to press her ass into cold porcelain.

She tries to regret the way her knees open so easily for Rio’s hips to fit between her thighs, enough room for Rio to be so close. The way the press of the beauty blender steadies her somehow, held so delicately between nimble fingers. Agatha tries not to think about the care in Rio’s movements, pressing the concealer in, firm enough to cover the red mark quickly on its way to purple, but gentle too, doing her best not to cause any added pain.

Agatha swallows, retracing all the other times they’d been like this, her standard uniform skirt wrinkled up just enough to expose her thighs to the chill of the petulant air conditioner, perhaps a means of freezing out every student who dared step out of line. The hem of her dark blue skirt is high enough now to get sent to the office for a dress code violation.

The goosebumps blooming along her thighs countering the heat climbing up her chest, one of Rio’s hands perched against her jaw to hold her in place, the other dutifully blending the full coverage makeup over her cheekbone tenderly.

It was startling still, as many times as they’d been here, in the third floor bathroom of their all girls catholic school, Agatha waiting patiently for Rio to finish her art, she’d never figured out what to do with her hands.

She settled on tilting back slightly, one hand palming at the side of her sink under her thigh, the other hesitantly clutching to the bottom of Rio’s blazer, a war in her mind at wanting to hold onto the other girl tighter but not wanting to scare her away.

Agatha wished that this could be enough for her, that Rio’s unwavering protection, the empathy and understanding that reporting Evanora wasn’t something she could do, even if her mother was spending more time bruising her daughter's face than playing her role as principal.

It felt sacred, the most holy she’d ever felt, watching Rio work on her like she was the art, not the scribbles and doodles in the margins of Rio’s notebooks.

Agatha winces at a particular press of the blender sponge under her eye, the edge where the mark met her eye socket. She doesn’t know whether to be grateful Evanora didn’t completely catch her eye with her fist this time, a black eye swollen shut harder to cover up.

“Sorry”, Rio stops as soon as she hears the small intake of breath, feels the micro movement of Agatha tilting away. She strokes her thumb over Agatha’s jaw, the reality settling in that she could definitely feel the hammering of Agatha’s pulse against her fingertips.

“You okay?” Brown eyes finally find blue ones, an echo of the screams that shrieked through the universe every time their eyes met, the flickering butterflies Agatha has been tamping down around her friend since they’d met freshman year.

The four years of truly knowing Rio only pressing dirt into the wounds of unreciprocated yearning.

Agatha only nods, not trusting her own voice, her eyelids falling closed as if to mirror the movement.

“I’m almost done,” Rio whispers like its regal, something practiced like sipping wine, receiving communion.

Rio holds death here, a precipice of falling in that always seems to be pushed off for later, because they’re lips are so close, Rio already perfectly slotted into Agatha’s personal space, but she never leans forward.

It’s not long before Rio is stepping back, putting the concealer back in her makeup bag, washing her hands in the sink next to the one Agatha is still sitting on, too far away for the brunette to pull her in now.

Agatha is too busy staring at her side profile, the delicate crook in her nose, the way she wets her own lips with her tongue, to track the movement of Rio’s eyes.

“What’s that from?” Rio motions downward with her eyebrows, her hands still under the stream of water.

“Huh?”

“This” Rio shifts closer again, not all the way into her bubble, but close enough to caress the outside of Agatha’s thigh. Her cold wet fingers sliding softly against a brown bruise a few inches away from her knee, the sensation causing the goosebumps to come back full force before they’d even had time to completely vanish.

“She usually aims for the face,” Rio offers, and Agatha would wince if it wasn’t true, Evanora always hell bent on attacking the most obvious places. Her mother wasn’t exactly picky with her targets, but more often than not, her cheeks and arms bore the worst of it.

“I don’t know what it’s from,” Agatha’s voice shakes, not liking how it sounds like she’s unsure, but in truth she’s only startled by how gentle Rio always is with her.

She almost wishes Rio would press her thumb into the brown and blue blob, shock some of that pain back to life, tired of feeling this numbness echo through her.

Rio searches her face, her fingers barely grazing the bruise, it almost tickles. She waits a beat, seemingly trying to find the lie in Agatha’s eyes.

“Okay”

—-

Agatha hates English class, hates the way Sister Hart seems to heavily rely on Spark notes to find any type of literary analysis, wishes there was more substance to their readings than redacted Shakespeare and the BIble. She hates Sister Hart’s lectures, the silent readings, the lack of opportunity for her to whisper to Rio across the foot of space between their desks.

Instead, she’s left to watch her, trace over the ridges of Rio’s face, the creases in her neck, the way she wished the collar of their uniforms fell just a bit lower against Rio’s collar bones.

She yearned for summer, Rio in tank tops and shorts, watching the night sky on a plush green blanket on Rio’s balcony. A sense of warmth when Rio could be completely herself. Agatha couldn’t believe this would be their last summer before college, before inevitable job searches and less time dedicated to each other.

As much as Agatha loves the warmer months away from school, less time spent in her mother’s clutches, a soaked in tranquility of wearing Rio’s crocs to grab the mail for Mr. Vidal while he worked over the grill, a bright smile from Rio’s mother who insisted Agatha call her Mama since they were 14, something more free in the way Rio allowed herself to hover closer somehow, let her eyes drift over her lips even if never spurred forward to connect them, Agatha wanted to savor their last few months of high school, feel the weight of childhood anchor her for just a little longer.

And for now, that felt kind of inescapable with Sister Hart’s current tangent about themes in Deuteronomy, free-will no longer on the table as the class sat with rapt attention, perfect posture.

Rio was doodling again, an expert at seeming completely engaged in the lecture, a facade of understanding nods, a show of taking notes that really consisted of small characters, attempts at calligraphy, webs of lines that morphed into sharp designs.

Agatha had always been amazed by how Rio could warp a page of loose leaf into a work of art, a balance of beauty and chaos mulled through Rio’s mind via a ball point pen. Chancing glances at Rio had always come first, but Agatha never failed to appreciate the scrawling doodles, had even wordlessly gifted Rio different color pens over the years for this exact purpose.

Chancing a look down toward Rio’s desk as their teacher is answering a question from a student on the other side of the room (Agatha is grateful for the distraction, but really what question could this girl possibly be asking right now), she traces over the top of the page, an intricate pattern one might think took a lot of forethought, and not something Rio had strung together on a whim. Below it is a tree, stoic and somehow moving, like Rio had drawn in the wind without explicit lines, the edges shaded with dark green ink. The image Rio is currently working on sits almost at the bottom of the page, about two inches from the border, the brunette’s hand hiding it from Agatha’s eyes, just from the natural way she’s holding the purple pen.

Agatha loves that Rio’s hands never work the same, sometimes making uncertain choppy lines, sketching out an echo of an object, trying to find the shape,or flowing smoothly across the page with intent. Right now, her movement more aligns with the latter approach, the pen held firm, the swirl of it slow and focused.

When Rio’s hand falls away, Agatha’s eyes settle on her own name, an elegant graffitied version that balances the humanity of Agatha with the chaotic abrasion she often wears (not towards Rio, never towards Rio).

Agatha can only blink at it, like a soft declaration that she might be held in the same regard as Rio’s art, the pages she saves securely in a folder and never lets anyone else touch.

Rio catches her of course, Agatha can feel Rio’s gaze on the side of her face, moves her own eyes to meet hers without a thought. She almost expects to find the other girl embarrassed, shrug off its meaning, remind Agatha without words that they are just friends, that they will only ever be friends.

What she finds instead is a soft smile, an almost smirk, a reassurance of something.

Agatha wishes she could question it.

”Ms. Harkness, can you tell the class your thoughts on last night's reading assignment of the book of Romans?”

Agatha hates English class.

“We’re all sinners,” Agatha almost huffs, wills herself to zone back into class without rolling her eyes, or saying something that would get back to her mother, “We don’t meet God’s standards which creates a need for salvation.”

”Good,” Sister Hart offers dejectedly after an unnecessary space of silence, as if she got off on the fear that curdled in its wake (could Agatha really take away those small wins from someone who’s a volunteer celibate?).

“Now who can tell me some examples of these sins that Paul writes about in Romans?”

Wanda is the only student to raise her hand, a red head too eager to be teacher’s pet, Agatha’s ears already ringing from all the times she’s winced at the sound of her voice. Rio always telling her to chill out, never understanding exactly why Wanda grated on her nerves in particular.

Maybe it was the favoritism, maybe it’s because the nuns liked her for her dedication, her photographic memory of just about every verse. Maybe it was because Agatha always got the fake, unearned version, a quiet pity of being the principal’s daughter but never living up to those expectations.

Sister Hart tilts her head just enough to spur Wanda to speak and Agatha has to shut her eyes to stop herself from groaning.

“Romans. Chapter 1, verse 27,” Wanda starts, no book in front of her, ready like she’s about to list the first 300 digits of pi. “For their women exchanged natural relations for those that are contrary to nature; and the men likewise gave up natural relations with women and were consumed with passion for one another, men committing shameless acts with men and receiving in themselves the due penalty for their error.”

Agatha grinds her teeth together, willing herself not to hurdle the 3 rows of desks between her and Wanda, because why the fuck was she choosing that particular verse.

”Okay, and what is Paul trying to say there?” Sister Hart asks, no change in her demeanor, unbothered by the ‘concrete truths’ Wanda had performed.

But there’s silence, no one daring to answer for the moment. Agatha isn’t sure what it is, if Wanda’s the only proud homophobe, if everyone else in the room gained nothing from four years of deep biblical analysis, or they’ve officially clocked out of the conversation.

Agatha is looking straight ahead, afraid to find the answers to long unasked questions in the features of Rio’s face, afraid her own eyes will give her away.

For all the close proximity, the charged glances, they’d never spoken about it. After many futile attempts of Rio asking Agatha about boys, somewhere in their friendship Rio had given up the topic altogether, and Agatha couldn’t say she was sad about that.

So when she hears that familiar voice, the one that had whispered good nights against her ear, reassured her through the bruises on her face, the weight of Evanora’s words, it felt odd. The pattern of Rio’s breathing a chorus it had never traced in front of Agatha before.

”Homosexuality,” Rio breaks the silence, maybe only pressed on by the awkwardness, “He’s talking about homosexuality” comes the clarification, a little more dull, a little slower.

Agatha still doesn’t look at her, suddenly very interested in her own pen.

“Correct, Ms. Vidal. Any other examples?” Sister Mary moves on.

Agatha was unsure if the lack of further discussion on that particular example came from indifference or perhaps the nun’s inability to even acknowledge sexuality outside the parameters set by the Bible.

She checks out of the group fully then, disassociating enough to free fall into a spiral of worry, fixated on the way Rio’s voice grated over the words, the shred of emotion in it that Agatha couldn’t pinpoint.

For all the yearning, Agatha was pessimistic at best, she knew that reality probably more closely aligned with Rio not reciprocating her feelings, that Rio liked boys, had spoken of first kisses with sweaty boys at summer camp, cut out pictures of Timothee Chalamet and Michael B Jordan on her bedroom walls. And as crushing as those thoughts were, Rio being homophobic would be so, so much worse.

She’s broken out of it when she catches movement in her peripheral, Rio’s arm outstretched towards her desk for a fleeting second.

When she finally looks down, a two inch scrap of paper sits on her notebook, the edges curling both from the rip and the way Rio must have scrunched it in her hand. Agatha usually found it endearing that Rio still passed notes like this, sticking to pen and paper when they could very easily conceal their phones under their desks. She appreciated the practicality of it even if they were more likely to get caught, it makes her feel like they have little secrets just for themselves, even if they were just Rio reminding her to pay attention half the time.

The split second before she reads it feels like it trails on too long, just a flash of time where she’s worried what Rio has to say to her so urgently.

‘Do u still have dinner w the devil tonight??? :(‘ is scrawled out in Rio’s unique handwriting, neat but something bouncy to it, the purple ink smeared a little from Rio’s inexplicably sweaty hands.

The note is referring to ‘family dinner’, standing tradition for Evanora and Agatha to have dinner together every Wednesday, a practice she never understood as Evanora couldn’t stand her and she’d never known her father. Agatha liked to think it was her mother’s way of keeping her on a tight leash, reminding her at least once a week that she was still in control, that Agatha was old enough to fight back now, but that doing so would somehow make it worse.

It had worked up to this point, Agatha having no other options, putting her trust into Rio that she wouldn’t say anything, waiting out another few months at least til she could get a job and save up enough to look for an apartment. Her mother’s crushing expectations just as much a factor in her good grades as her need to get a full scholarship so that she didn’t have to rely on Evanora to pay for college.

She’s already accepted the scholarship for Darkhold University, but had yet to secure a plan passed staying at home and commuting the 30 minutes everyday.

‘Unfortunately, why…’ Agatha writes back, her handwriting a lot less neat, folding the bit of paper a couple times before tossing it back onto Rio’s desk.

‘Wanted a hw buddy’ Rio writes back like they don’t always do homework together. Agatha had lost count of afternoons spent in the library or at Rio’s kitchen table, hours where they’d slip from working silently next to each other to gossiping about the nuns to talking about everything they’d dreamed of, teasing each other until a librarian had to remind them to be quiet, or Rio’s mother would chuckle at them and set them back to work.

Still, something pulls at Agatha, a desire to rebel, a new-found interest in actually seeing what consequences Evanora will lay at her feet. She’s already got bruises to cover, deep emotional baggage from years of being told she’ll never be enough. What else could she do? Maybe Agatha wanted to find out.

‘I can bail,’ she writes, hoping Rio will let her put herself at risk, but knowing her well enough that the brunette won’t agree.

She isn’t surprised by Rio’s face after reading her last addition to the note, a silent ‘are you serious?’ in her eyes that neither of them needs words for. It’s one of those things that makes Agatha’s heart hammer in her chest, the silent communication, the fierce protectiveness, Rio never afraid to tell her she’s being reckless for no reason.

The bell rings. Thank God.

“Dude,” Rio starts, written conversation definitely not over as they both move to grab their things and go to their next classes, “please go to dinner, we’ll hang out tomorrow” she shrugs like she isn’t actively trying to lessen Evanora’s wrath.

—-

Dinner with Evanora isn’t awful, a quiet back and forth of half pleasantries, or whatever Evanora considers passable as family bonding. Agatha sets the table, holds her breath, skates around the tense air like she always has, careful and quiet.

Maybe it's why Agatha is so loud and unapologetic in front of everyone else, why she can’t reel in all the emotions, a performance of sorts doing her best to curate the version of herself she thinks might have happened had her mother been supportive in any imagination of the word, a confidence, a desire to do something more than get away from this house.

Here, she wears a different mask, a solid coating of concrete that hardens over her eyes, stops the wrinkles of worry, but also never lets her smile.

“I see your face is looking better,” Evanora comments like she’s asking about something trivial, but Agatha hasn’t seen the woman meet her eyes, even look up from her plate since they’ve sat down.

Agatha is used to this game, the placating, the pushing down, talking about abuse like it’s nothing, like Agatha’s pain is nothing.

“Yes,” Agatha answers, knowing her mother expects a verbal answer, knowing Evanora is hoping she takes the bait, but Agatha has had years of practice, knows better than to question it.

”Where did you get the makeup?” Evanora asks, no heat to it, a simple demand.

Agatha isn’t allowed to wear makeup. Apparently not even to hide the evidence of her mother’s rage. Rio had been using her own makeup on her for years, Evanora never commenting on it. Agatha knows Evanora isn’t that stupid, to think that over the last 4 years Agatha’s healing abilities had become superhuman. And in the past she might have been confused as to why her mother was picking at something that was protecting her image, but Agatha almost took it as a compliment. If anything, it made it abundantly clear that Agatha had become extremely skilled at tucking in the loose edges of Evanora’s expectations, making it so the woman had to find more ridiculous things to fret over.

“Someone at school,” Agatha still does her best at honesty, wanting to tow the line between lying and keeping Rio’s name out of her mouth in hopes it might shield the girl from her mother’s wrath.

“That Vidal girl?” Evanora voices like a question, but Agatha knows she isn’t really asking.

“Yes”

”I don’t want you hanging around her, Agatha” the words ring like a curse, a declaration of prayer, something not meant to be fought against.

”Mother-“ Agatha tries anyway, her mind not even allowing herself to dream of a life where she wasn’t allowed to see Rio.

“She’s not a good influence on you.”

Agatha doesn’t know how to say that Rio makes her feel most like herself, brings out a smile in the soaring weight of pain, cares for her like she is sacred, propping her up in all the times she feels unable to stand.

“Agatha.” Evanora’s voice always feels so raw around the syllables of her name, a name she’d given her to mean ‘virtuous’, an expression of high moral standing, perhaps a reflection of all the virtue Evanora lacked. ”Tell me you understand, no more hanging around that girl.”

”I understand,” the words feel crushing, even if Agatha had no intention of pushing Rio away. It still stung. The fear that their friendship would be strained by operating under cover, how far Evanora might go to spy on them, separate them in class, punish Agatha for every text message, every glance.

It felt like a new low, an answer to Agatha’s earlier attempt at rebellion without even following through with skipping dinner. Her mother was so willing to rip away anything and anyone that brought her joy, a need to isolate her from the world, keep her ugly behind closed doors, break her down over and over for her own selfish pleasure.

Agatha pushed around her peas with her fork, Evanora had never been a good cook, but the bland food wasn’t the only reason for her lack of appetite. She poked at the pot roast, feeling the nausea lurch forward, praying her mother wasn’t paying close enough attention to how much she was actually swallowing.

“Are you not hungry?” Evanora asks, God evidently not hearing Agatha’s prayer. Evanora’s words almost rang close to the words of a mother who actually cares about the nourishment of her child. Only making dinner once a week, Agatha mostly got by on the tangerines Evanora kept in a bowl on the counter mostly for show, the extra empanadas Rio packed for her at lunch, church service refreshments of kool aid and cucumber sandwiches, and Saturday dinners courtesy of the Vidal family.

“I just have a lot of homework,” Agatha half lies, the essay she has due next week already half written.

”Well, don’t let me keep you,” Evanora waves her away vaguely and Agatha tries not to show her relief, “You’ve been looking quite bloated lately anyway.”

It’s one of those comments that sinks against her skin, makes her throat tremble, her knuckles feel ridged and locked, the type of line that had gotten a reaction so many times. But the bruise on her cheek still throbbed, she didn’t want to give Evanora another reason to lash out, feeling too unsteady from the thoughts of Rio, especially when her mother had given her a chance to walk away.

”Okay”

Agatha moves slowly, giving Evanora the opportunity to take back her permission if she saw fit, but she stands without another word from either of them, cleans her plate, places it in the dishwasher, before ascending up the stairs to her room.

Evanora doesn’t like when Agatha closes her bedroom door, so she doesn’t. No sanctuary of her bedroom walls, nothing more than an extension to the hell Evanora had crafted their home into.

—-

 

Ecclesiastes 4:9-10- Two are better than one, because they have a good reward for their labour. For if they fall, the one will lift up his fellow. But woe to him who is alone when he falls and hath not another to lift him up.

The sun is starting to set, Agatha’s window a portal to heaven, the sway of trees, the cotton candy blend of blue and pink horizons, fluffed expanses of white clouds.

She wishes she could touch it, play in the art God had made in the sky each night, find the strings of herself that still believed in Him despite her circumstances.

Rio once said that’s what she liked about Agatha most, the way she still hoped for things, ached to see the good in people despite her own reality. It didn’t feel like a test from up above, a series of hardships she could endure and still find the courage to be righteous.

It felt like a spell cast by an evil wizard, a damning curse she’d have to find a way to undo if she wanted to feel truly free. It was a battle, a storm of conflict fighting everything she’d ever been taught, cycling through Sunday service enough times to start to strain out the parts worth keeping from the words that brought on all this grief.

For all the ‘love thy neighbor’ and ‘I can do all things through God who strengthens me’, it was still the reality that empowered her mother to hit her, still the life that gave her no father, the world she couldn’t escape or recede from.

And still, this life gave her Rio. A force of love. A pillar in her life that had saved her from the crash right before impact every single time.

She was doing her best to focus on homework, wishing Rio was here to explain Standard Deviation to her for the 50th time at least. As naturally smart as Agatha was, she hated for anyone else to know she actually put in a lot of effort. Rio was the only person that made her feel proud of it, like it was out of drive and not fear.

Everyone else got the version of Agatha that presented as effortless, flawless, an ease to which she operated, which perhaps only reinforced the perception that she was only favored for the status of her mother and not for doing any real work.

Rio was like her sidekick in that regard, girls at school knowing them to be a package deal, not exactly popular, but also not unknown.

Agatha. The principal’s daughter.

Rio. The only one willing to be her friend.

Agatha’s phone buzzes halfway through reading a question about the median (a concept she very much understands), she knows it’s Rio without looking, a cosmic tell to the way her heart eases before even picking up the device from her bed.

‘wyd’

Agatha hates that such a low effort text earns a soft smile, that Rio thinking about her at all is some grand gesture.

‘HW’
’alone ofc’

Agatha answers, maybe too quickly, but she can’t chastise herself too long.

’open ur window’

’???’ Agatha responds, her thumb jamming the send with maybe too much might, but she hops out of bed all the same, walking the two steps to her window and lifting it open before peering down.

There stands Rio, one story down. She’s not in her school uniform anymore, a long sleeve gray shirt, gold letters on the front that read ‘St.Anthony Bible Camp 2022’, and straight fit joggers, held in her hand a white paper bag with the unmistakable orange of the Dunkin Donuts logo on the front.

Rio raises her eyebrows in silent question.

A part of Agatha wants to yell at her, call her an idiot for showing up unannounced when her mother is home, tell her to leave, save them both from whatever unknown outcome.

But she can’t deny the way her heart thumps in her ears, the way Rio’s brown eyes glow against the setting sun, the way her hair is down now, the put together look from earlier today at school softened now, that stupid grin she always wears. And more than that was her determination to see Agatha, this unasked for (but so desired) need to be around her, bring Agatha her favorite donut.

Agatha rolls her eyes, trying to quell away the tears, happy tears at the beauty of her friend caring for her so earnestly. But she can’t stop the wrinkle of the smile she returns despite her innate desire to want to come off as unaffected.

She holds up a hand, palm toward Rio, trying to tell her to wait a moment. She walks softly toward her open bedroom door, doing her best to avoid the creaking pressure points of the old wooden floor. She waits a moment in the threshold of it, listening intently. She can make out faint murmurs from the television in the living room, Dr. Phil reruns about wayward children no doubt. She closes her door inch by inch, slowly with both hands, concentrating on keeping it steady, until it clicks into the wall softly. She stands there another moment catching her breath, listening again for any shifts of movement or Evanora’s footsteps up the stairs.

After a moment of nothing, Agatha turns back towards the window, a push of desire to run back to Rio, but she treads across the wood panels delicately. She hatches a plan to throw down one of her bed sheets, hope Rio possesses the arm strength necessary to use it to climb up, but when she peers down once more, Rio is closer now, a lot closer.

The heathen had somehow scaled up the siding of the house, her nimble fingers apparently skilled at more than just blending concealer over bruises. The donut bag held securely between her lips, the look of concentration just as clear as when she’s working on a drawing.

Rio takes the hand Agatha offers her and somehow gracefully (and quietly, thank God) makes it through the window. Rio takes the rolled up edge of the bag out of her mouth, and Agatha winces at the saliva left behind, unable to rid her mind of the taste of thick brown paper.

Rio half chuckles at her reaction.

”Hey” she finally says, the word feeling heavy and light all at once, like it was casual for Rio to climb the side of a house to deliver a sweet treat.

But Agatha can’t risk the unpredictability of it.

She clamps a hand over Rio’s mouth, evading Rio’s personal space, their eyes locked in a desperate plea to please shut the fuck up. Agatha tries not to think of the softness of Rio’s lips under her touch, the way she doesn’t fight her off.

”She’s downstairs, you have to be quiet” Agatha whispers, but it strikes like a dagger.

Rio nods softly, her eyes boring into Agatha’s, a calculated measure of understanding. Still, it takes an extra moment for Agatha to move her hand, maybe finding the strength to trust Rio to keep this promise, maybe to commit Rio’s soft brown irises to memory.

“Sorry,” Rio whispers, “I just wanted to check on you”

Agatha doesn’t look at her, the uninterrupted care something she still can’t face head on sometimes. Instead, she focuses on the bag, easily pulling it from Rio’s grip. She opens it and looks inside.

”Boston Crème’s are usually reserved for when you think I’m about to spiral” Agatha chirps something slightly above a whisper, the bleak reality of it soft but telling.

Rio swallows harshly when Agatha’s eyes look up again, trying to combat Agatha’s assumptions. She hesitates, looking around the room, obviously trying to change the subject.

Rio had never been in Agatha’s room before. Mostly because Evanora never allowed company, especially if it was Agatha opening the door to them. She’d never been ballsy enough to sneak her in either, afraid Evanora had secret cameras posted by the door, in the kitchen, ways to monitor Agatha when she wasn’t home.

It was also the fact that Agatha was kind of embarrassed by it, her bedroom not a reflection of who she was or anything she liked. White walls almost clinical, never afforded the opportunity to pick what color her room would be, never given the freedom to decorate. Her twin bed in one corner, a tidy closet with the door closed. Two oak night stands, old and cracking. No TV. The only other additions were the cross above her bed and a gray alarm clock well past its prime.

It felt empty, an echo of what could be. Rio asks about homework maybe because there’s nothing else to ask about.

”Statistics?” Rio voices, still hushed.

“Yeah” Agatha sighs, not prodding any further about why Rio had turned up at her window with her SOS dessert of choice. She doesn’t have the mental energy to push. And while she doesn’t think they’d fight about it, she doesn’t want to risk the chance of their voices growing louder.

Rio sits on the edge of the bed, kicking off her sneakers quietly before settling further back to look at Agatha’s textbook.

“Do you need help with number 6?” Rio asks, not in a judgemental way, just noticing that Agatha had left it blank on her worksheet, that strong resolve of always being present, always trying to help. Rio was too good for her.

Agatha nods, sitting back in her original spot on the bed, letting their knees brush.

She hates how easy it is, how they effortlessly fall into working out the problem, Rio walking her through it, her voice remaining just above a whisper, their bodies close as they share the textbook. She hates how she rips the donut in two without a second thought, handing over the bigger half to Rio like she’d always be willing to take 49% if it meant giving Rio 51.

She hates that Rio is offensively polite, achingly gentle, tremendously thoughtful, doing her absolute best to save Agatha’s white bed sheets from any possible crumbs, that she can undo all of Agatha’s harsh edges just by being next to her.

On the last statistics question, Rio shifts, her head falling on Agatha’s shoulder, “I’m sorry” she whispers, somehow quieter than all her previous words, causing Agatha’s hand to stutter, her brain suddenly losing it’s sense of intent.

“For showing up unannounced,” Rio supplies the reason for her apology before Agatha can even ask for it, “I don’t wanna get you in trouble.”

”I know your intentions are good” Agatha’s voice trembles. She thinks to add ‘they always are’, a mark of the way Rio has only ever been this selfless, positive person. Another reason Agatha felt unworthy of the current of Rio’s friendship, a river so powerful she’d never been able to stop flowing with it.

“Let me put my books away,” Agatha almost whimpers, needing an excuse to put space between them, but not wanting Rio to feel like she’s pushing her away.

Rio lifts her head, but when Agatha leaves the bed entirely, she only snuggles further into the sheets, fully laying down now.

When she turns back to look at her, a dream Agatha’s had many times of Rio in her bed, holding her in a way that read as more than just friends, this felt like too much, like Agatha couldn’t have this, whatever it was without it spelling disaster.

Evanora convinced her a long time ago that she deserved nothing good.

And Rio was so good.

As much as she’d dreamt of Rio loving her that way, having Rio all to herself, caring for her, protecting her as fiercely right back, Agatha couldn’t bear the thought of taking her away from everyone else.

Rio was the sun, and Agatha was unwanted weeds. In all the growth, Agatha could never feel like she truly deserved her.

“Can you lay here with me for a few minutes?” Rio asks, a pressure to her voice like she’d been trying to find the nerve to ask.

Agatha can’t say ‘no’, cursing herself for how long she’d been taking to figure out how to ask Rio to leave.

Instead, she joins Rio, facing her, the twin bed not leaving much space between them, but Agatha does her best to keep from touching her.

But Rio is like an Agatha magnet, her fingers delicately tracing the outer edge of her wounded cheek bone, Agatha latches onto her wrist. She tells herself it’s a safety mechanism, security for the chance Rio presses too hard, but it feels more like an anchor.

“Does it still hurt?” the words bloom from Rio’s mouth into the small bubble between them.

”Mmmm” Agatha hums, not trusting her words, not wanting to break this spell.

Rio’s fingers dance higher, tucking stray hairs out of Agatha’s face, her eyes gliding over the angle of her nose, the plane of her eyebrows, before settling back into the oceans in Agatha’s irises.

Rio’s eyes get watery, its barely perceptible, but the collapse of her eyelids, the way she bites her lip. For the first time Agatha wonders if maybe Rio is the one on the verge of spiraling, this whole grand gesture a cry for help, a dazzling hope that Agatha would see through the facade and know.

Rio’s eyes are closed, her eyebrows slightly downturned, holding in, bracing for something. Her hand now settled on Agatha’s neck, her thumb stroking against her jaw.

“It’s okay to cry, Rio” Agatha doesn’t know what makes her say it, maybe this searing guilt in her gut that she’d made all her own problems Rio’s too, the bone crushing pain at seeing Rio hurt.

As Rio opens her eyes, tears fall. It isn’t wrecked sobs, just floating streams curved against the angles of her face, tendrils of a river flowing with the current.

Agatha can’t help the way her own thumb seeks to cover them, brush away the wet tears. She yearns to press kisses against the streaks, but she settles for her fingertips pressing away the trails.

Rio’s hand moves off her face then, giving Agatha more room to tend to her, instead it lands on Agatha’s hip, a touch that causes her to squirm slightly.

“Agatha” Rio always says her name like she is a saint. The saint that bears her name, St. Agatha, the patron saint of martyrs. Rio makes her feel like she can be good, like she can heal, like this suffering can lead to more than death.

Agatha can’t help the flicker of her eyes toward Rio’s lips, entranced by the way her lips wrap around the syllables of her name.

”Agatha,” Rio says her name again, trying to get her attention, bringing her blue eyes back to meet endless brown, almost black now that the sun has set, Rio’s fingers dig into her hip, something of a command to focus but it only makes her chest thrum harder, her eyes burning, her pulse ringing through her head.

“Rio” Agatha responds soft and asking, her eyes fall back down to her lips but this time her fingers follow, her thumb tracing the underside of Rio’s lower lip, it was charged, something close to a declaration. At the very least, Rio knew now that Agatha had thought about her lips in a way that didn’t exactly spell out ‘platonic friendship’.

Downstairs. There’s a thud. Sudden and loud.

”Fuck” is Rio’s next word, pushing up from the bed, almost knocking their heads together.

Agatha can’t speak, the ache of a chance lost doing its best to settle in. As many times as Agatha had convinced herself that nothing would ever happen between them, the sting of reality was something her brain was struggling to compute.

So she stands with Rio, paralleling the rigid speed, she fidgets with her hands, her hair, the seam of her shirt, as she watches Rio pull on her shoes, not caring that the tongues of her Vans are shoved into her toes, the laces undone.

“Rio” the whisper is gruff, an attempt at anger in the low volume, the fear coming out clearer than anything else.

Rio is already through the window, yet to climb down.

“It’s okay,”she whispers like it's the only thing she’s certain of, “I’ll see you tomorrow”

Agatha has no choice but to believe her.

Chapter 2

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Colossians 3:20- Children, obey your parents in everything, for this pleases the lord. 

 

Rio is already through the window, yet to climb down. 

 

“It’s okay,”she whispers like it's the only thing she’s certain of, “I’ll see you tomorrow”

 

Agatha has no choice but to believe her.

 

The next thing she hears is her mother’s voice calling her name, she tries to determine how distant it sounds, calculate the number of seconds she has before Evanora is looking into her eyes. 

 

“Agatha,” Evanora yells her name for the second time, “I’ve broken a glass, grab me the broom.”

 

Agatha whips around pushing away the raw feelings of Rio, this trepid ocean, a blister opening in the wake of being so close to that heat, but never finding the balm to cover it. She hops to her bedroom door, swinging it open against the worry that it would squeak, pleading that it will be back in its rightful position before Evanora could ever know it had been closed at all. 

 

She is half way through a sigh, relief at the way the hinges don’t creak from the movement, but the rest is swallowed. Evanora stands at the bottom of the stairs, her eyes boring up at Agatha as she stands in the threshold between her room and the staircase, hand tellingly still placed on the handle.

 

’Fuck’ Agatha curses in her head, her ability to swallow down her sailor mouth in front of her mother something she’d practiced for years. 

 

What helped too was the fire in Evanora’s eyes, that split into madness that rendered Agatha frozen. Five or seventeen, it was always the same. Agatha knew she’d fucked up and her mind had already started to shut down, remove herself from her brain to protect herself. 

 

Agatha had to give her credit, for a middle aged woman, Evanora sure could run up the stairs, maybe spurred on by rage, but spurred nonetheless. 

 

The warmth of Rio was suddenly vacant as everything fell into deceleration. Evanora was in front of her in an instant. At first it was a push, enough to knock her off her balance for a moment, the true intention for Evanora to see inside her room, find the reason Agatha had closed the door in the first place.

 

And Agatha lets her, takes the push without a word, without a groan, just stands by the door paralyzed, the weight of fear pressing her blood through her so intensely it stops her ability to move at all, to think at all. 

 

Evanora latches onto the now empty Dunkin bag, picking it up like it was utterly offensive. Perhaps an oversight they’d completely forgotten about when Rio was trying to leave as quickly as possible. It feels cruel now, the way this remnant of Rio’s care was being used as evidence against her. 

 

Evanora’s eyes find the open window, her steps launching her towards it, looking for more answers but only finding the darkness that had overtaken the night.

 

Agatha thanks God that Rio hadn’t decided to stick around for whatever reason, she didn’t want Rio mixed into this, she didn’t want Rio to see the way she’d crumbled under her mother’s wrath, wanting some sick curiosity never answered. Rio didn’t need to witness this, the sullen sadness, the frozen disgrace, no attempts made at fighting back. 

 

“Who was in here, Agatha?” Evanora is in her face now, the paper bag crumpled in her hand. 

 

She can see the way her mother’s knuckles are white, the veins in her neck that pop out as she speaks, the spit of her hatred, that empty rage that fills her eyes like a monster overtaken by the devil himself. 

 

“Mothe-“ Agatha isn’t allowed to finish her answer, only feels the hand slap across her face, the tears in her eyes, the wrecked intensity of it all not letting her process anything properly.

 

”You harlot”

 

It’s piercing, the words rattling around in her brain, doing their best to find a home next to all the things her mother ever called her. 

 

She can feel the wall behind her, the corner securing her. She can’t feel her hands, can’t remember how to move. She feels the heat on her cheek, the air pressing deep into the healing bruise that her mother’s hand had just pressed over. It’s unbearably hot, the sweat sudden and inescapable as Evanora holds her ground. Agatha’s face is wet with tears, a new realization that passes as she tries to focus back in on the actual words Evanora is screaming. 

 

It feels like a slow motion effect on a movie. Agatha tries to think about Rio forcing her to watch the Matrix, always surprised at how little media Evanora allowed her to consume. She tries to think of stale popcorn tucked between them on Rio’s couch, brown eyes and the way Rio could never shut up during a movie, the complaints about the plot being cheapened by the romance element. 

 

It helps for a fleeting moment, the press of her best friend in her mind soft enough to wick out the truth of the present. 

 

She sees Evanora raise her hand again and again but she can’t lift her own to impede the impact. It’s a crash of black and white, static as her body sinks to the floor, fights to keep her blurry eyes open. Eventually, the reflex follows through, her arms coming up, not to hit back, but to protect herself. 

 

It tickles her in some solemn way that the natural instinct to take cover, preserve her face and vital organs always takes an extra minute to follow through, like Evanora’s abuse, her disparaging words had cut deep enough that even her own brain believed she didn't deserve to be kept alive.

 

”please” she hears the echo of her own voice, a gentle plea for her mother to stop, her voice wrought and barely there, scared even now to speak out of turn, ask for something Evanora isn’t capable of providing. 

 

Agatha isn’t sure if her plea is heard, if her mother stops then or five minutes after.

 

The feeling in her face comes back first, red and throbbing, she knows without even looking in a mirror. Her hands feel papery and unattached, her feet are asleep, the prickly pain shocking up her calves at the awkward way she’d sunken to the floor. 

 

She’s breathing, the shudder taking her back into reality. She tries to focus. 

 

Evanora isn’t here anymore. At least not in the room. 

 

A startling relief. The pounding in her head a flurry of a pop song rolling through her head. She thinks of Rio humming to the radio, Agatha queuing songs on Rio’s phone so she can focus on driving. The old car still using an aux cord, the calm of being in Rio’s passenger seat and trusting her to take them where they needed to be. 

 

The thought trapezes through her mind as she finds sleep.

 

—-

 

 

As she walks towards Rio’s car, Agatha can’t help but pull the hoodie up around her face more securely, doing her best to hide the mess of bruises she had yet to fully access in the mirror. 

 

Hiding, as she often did. She couldn’t mask these wounds like she had her emotions. Maybe that’s why Evanora had chosen her face as the target, forcing Agatha to wear the hurt she’d been so good at hiding her whole life. 

 

Seven am was usually a happy time for Agatha. Not because she was naturally a morning person, and she obviously wasn’t the biggest fan of school, but because it meant at least 10 minutes in Rio’s old beat up sedan, the paint chipping off, the heater barely working, the brakes squeaking every time it rained. It meant Rio in her school issued pleated skirt, unfiltered by the outside world. The radio playing songs that felt like only theirs, a space to find solace and calm. 

 

Evanora always left home earlier than Agatha, leaving her daughter to walk the 30 minute distance rain, snow, or shine. But they’d always been overly cautious anyway, Rio parking four houses down, enough distance for Agatha to feel safe from prying eyes and the doorbell camera. 

 

The boiling embarrassment of it sank in her chest, the walk to Rio’s car feeling like rocks in her shoes, the thundering of each step as she tried to keep her expression jaded even though all she wanted to do was cry. As safe as Rio made her feel, this felt like too much, too overwhelming to face. 

 

Agatha gets into the passenger seat without a word, pressing away from any possible reactions from Rio. She does not look at her, only half registers the feeling of being watched, she can’t handle this, feeling like the tide is coming up over her lungs but never flowing back. 

 

She blinks, trying to will the pain from her right eye, the pulse of it hot and frantic. She can feel the purple of it without having to look, and for the moment she’s happier that it’s her right eye, blocked slightly from Rio’s view as long as Agatha doesn’t turn her head. 

 

On the verge of panic, Agatha tries to focus on the things that settle her back into the person she is without this pain. The smell of faded eucalyptus from the air freshener hanging from Rio’s rear view mirror, the dull buzz of the radio speakers since Rio had altered the settings, turning the bass all the way up when she first got the car and had never changed it back, the cold air inside the car refreshing and icy just the way Rio liked it. 

 

Agatha feels Rio’s hand on her thigh, her thumb brushing over the linty texture of old sweat pants. She hates how steadying it is, how much lighter it all feels just to be next to her. 

 

“You’re not in uniform” Rio chirps like it’s a surprise to Agatha too, like she’s informing them both. But Agatha can hear the pain in it too. She’s still not looking at her, but Agatha knows the hoodie isn’t covering it all, knows that Rio knows she’s hurt. 

 

Agatha hates how well Rio knows her, the way Agatha deflected from questions like ‘are you okay?’ and shut down in the wake of anyone fretting over her with pity. Agatha hates how Rio had carefully curated tactics with Agatha, how they’d worked against her stubbornness, her unwillingness to open up, had torn down the castle walls over and over.

 

She hated how Rio never got tired of fighting through it either, was annoyingly patient in hurdling the walls to Agatha’s heart, pulling at rare strings until Agatha’s resolve was untied. 

 

“I’m trying to get expelled” Agatha's voice is hollow, a strong attempt at sarcasm that would work on anyone else. 

 

“Mmmm” 

 

Agatha can’t take the warmth of Rio’s hand on her, but she doesn’t have the strength to push her away either. 

 

She picks up Rio’s hand, examining her fingers, tracing the edges of her blunt nails, picks at stained blue ink around her thumb. Rio lets her. Lets her have this crushed second of collapse, wrinkle the timeline just enough to grant Agatha a moment to breathe.

 

”Let me see,” comes from Rio’s mouth like a revenant whisper and Agatha knows she’s crying before she turns her head to look at her. 

 

Rio loosens her hand from Agatha’s grip to gently tug at Agatha’s chin, the fingers pulling her gently to look at her, giving her all the freedom to pull away, all the time for Agatha to tell her ‘no’. 

 

Brown eyes only darken as she traces them over Agatha’s face, there’s a weight of despair in her brown irises that Agatha can’t fully grasp onto. Silent tears slide down Rio’s cheeks, eyebrows furrowed, the creases of her face setting ridged against the burden of emotion. 

 

Agatha remembers when Rio’s grandfather died, how she held her hand the entire service, how she cried into her shoulder, how Rio was different for a long time after, how the grief had somehow morphed into who she was. This expression was reminiscent of that, the soaring pain mixed with something else. Agatha couldn’t exactly say what though.

 

”I’m so sorry”

 

Guilt, Rio felt guilty. 

 

Agatha’s heart shattered at the realization, the lurch in her stomach, the stale taste in her mouth, it felt like she was losing whatever hold she had left on consciousness, like this could only be a nightmare, that she’d have to shake herself awake. 

 

Rio was here, painting herself as the devil, when Rio was only ever a chorus of angels. Rio dreaming herself up as Judas. Rio could only ever be Simon, helping Jesus carry the cross. 

 

“Rio, you didn’t do this to me,” It’s firm and solid and it’s all the certainty she can offer.

 

Rio chuckles around her tears, dejected, a disappointment in herself, a disbelief.

 

”You shouldn’t be the one trying to comfort me right now”

 

But it’s all Agatha wants to do, hold Rio’s hands in hers, pull her closer, rest the full weight of her body into her until there is no place to run, let Rio cry for not being able to protect her, whisper reassurances in her ear, remind them both just how unfair all this was, that this was never Rio’s fault. 

 

She can’t. 

 

The burden of it swallowing her. Her refusal to let it swallow Rio too. Because there was no fixing this, just waiting and wishing, and hoping time passed quick enough for her to go to college, get the fuck out of that house alive. Evanora was only getting worse, and maybe she was right, maybe she shouldn’t see Rio, shouldn’t drag her into this unwinnable war.

 

”I can’t do this”

 

Agatha felt like a traitor as soon as the words came out, scared of how the world would keep turning without continuing their routine, the silent promise that Rio would always be there after the hurricanes of maternal rage, that Rio had been buying concealer way too pale for her own skin for years, the practiced truth of Rio holding her up like crutches, pressing care into her like bandaids over scrapes, looking at her like she was worth all the emotional turmoil if it meant there was a chance she’d be okay. But she couldn’t let Rio keep looking at her like she was broken, like Rio had let it happen under her watch. She opens the passenger door, determined to walk away. 

 

And she does.

 

She gets back to the side walk, a brisk walk of 4 steps or so before Rio is out of her car and following her. She hears the engine turn off, the slam of the driver’s side door, Rio’s gruff, an anger she’s never seen her wear. But she doesn’t turn back, knows the hurt in Rio’s eyes will be too much to bear. 

 

“Agatha please don’t do this”

 

She doesn’t expect Rio to sound so broken, her brain still convinced of her mother’s scathing words that she will never be good enough to love, that she’s never been worth chasing after. But the crack in Rio’s voice, the harsh footsteps that echo behind her, Agatha can feel the devastation.

 

Agatha turns back towards her abruptly, the anger, the fear, this deep seeded insecurity that she’ll let Rio in, love her with everything, and that Rio will still walk away in the end. It’s easier to end it now, before she knows what Rio’s lips feel like on hers, before she let’s herself sink so deep that she’ll never be able to swim back to the surface. She knows she won’t be able to handle the rejection, better to cut the red string of fate now. Save them both the trouble.

 

”Go the fuck to school, Rio” Agatha knows it’s harsh and she means it to be, needs to get the fuck away from here now. 

 

But Rio doesn’t stop coming towards her, the hurt and determination swirling in black irises, Agatha can she the way Rio is shaking, the way she’s still trying despite the fear, a bravery Agatha is jealous of. 

 

A coward, always a fucking coward. 

 

Rio grabs her, wraps her up into this bone crushing hug, bordering on tackle level strength, it almost knocks the wind out of her. The suddenness, the sharp shame at being so easily caught only whips out more frustration.

 

Agatha fights back and Rio would be stupid to assume anything less. Agatha tries to scratch at her, wiggle out of the grip, she pulls furiously at the back of Rio’s blazer, jostles her legs in an attempt to push them both into a nearby bush, her futile attempts only making her groan, the hot tears on her own cheeks pour out as her first sign of defeat.

 

”Stop, Agatha, just stop” 

 

Agatha hates how calming Rio’s voice is. Agatha hates that she listens, her body finally going slack against Rio, her hands tugging her closer now suddenly out of her control. 

 

Stop. Stop running from me. Stop trying to save me from you. You are not the monster. 

 

It sings in her brain without Rio having to say it, the way they slide together without thought, Agatha’s face buried into her neck, Rio’s hands securely supporting her weight. 

 

Rio presses a delicate kiss against Agatha’s hairline, it feels like a reinstatement of their promise. 

 

“Can we please get back in the car?” The anger in Rio’s voice is gone now, replaced by something fragile, something waning. 

 

“You should go to school,” Agatha’s voice is free of malice now too, the sentiment still stands that she doesn’t want to make Rio’s life any harder. 

 

“I’m not leaving you”

 

Agatha pulls away slightly, Rio loosening her grip enough to let the movement happen freely, seemingly trusting her enough to not make another escape attempt. Agatha takes a moment to look at Rio, the tears in her eyes no longer falling, but still so full of sorrow, the pink shade around her irises, the swollen eyelids. 

 

She thinks of last night. Before the storm. Rio in her bed, looking at her like more than just a friend, feeling safe in the unknown, this security blanket of Rio that still held her steady on the precipice of change. It made her feel brave. Like Rio gave her the strength to try and fail. 

 

Agatha couldn’t kiss her, not now. 

 

She gives a small nod, an indication that she wasn’t pushing Rio away. She was ready. 

 

Rio all but puts her back in the passenger seat, closes the door after she’s sure all her limbs are safely inside. It only takes Rio a second to be back in the driver’s seat but the empty air feels stale, a moment where all Agatha has is the throbbing of her eye and the hope that she’ll be okay. 

 

“Lemme just call my mom, tell her I’m not going to school,” Rio adds in as she pulls away from the curb. Agatha tries not to compare it, especially when the Vidals had been extremely good to her, but it still made her feel an echo of envy. Rio could tell her parents anything at any time and they’d always only been understanding. 

 

The explanation Rio might give her mother for skipping school doesn’t exactly cross Agatha’s mind until Mrs. Vidal’s voice comes through the phone after only ringing twice. 

 

“Are you alright, chispita?” 

 

Agatha held onto the care of it, the way Rio’s mother always spoke to her daughter like she was a gift. The nickname they’d given Rio as a child “little spark” still in use today, the fact that they cared not only because they were family, but loved Rio enough to be invested in her personality, in who she was to the world.

 

What Agatha doesn’t recognize is the hesitation in Rio’s voice, the way she looks to Agatha briefly, her eyes straying away before she moves to answer her mother’s question. 

 

“Yes, mama. Ummm…” 

 

“What is it, Rio?” Her mother asks, no bite in it, just looking for clarification, reading the stalling in her daughter’s tone with no difficulty. 

 

“Purple socks,” Rio says nervously, but her mother’s reaction only reaffirms that it’s not her mother she’s worried about.

 

”Okay, text me if you need anything”

 

It takes a minute for Agatha’s brain to catch up. 

 

Purple socks? What the fuck did that mean? A code word? For…?

 

She doesn’t process the last few seconds of the phone conversation, the blind rage settling back in. 

 

“What the fuck was that?” Are her words, but she doesn’t know how they’re coming out of her mouth, her fists winded tightly in her lap, finding the strength to not resort to violence before she has all the answers to her questions (also Rio’s driving and she’d never forgive herself for dying a virgin).

 

”Agath-“

 

”What the fuck does ‘purple socks’ mean, Rio?” 

 

There’s a partial imprint of a memory somewhere in the back of her mind, filed somewhere in the Rio stack, unorganized, unsure. A purple pair of socks Rio’s parents gifted her for Christmas the first year of their friendship.

 

She wants to believe that Rio had kept her promise, that she wouldn’t tell anyone about Evanora, about the abuse, but here she was explaining something to her mother in code, the meaning of it so implicitly understood.

 

”It just means you need me, I’m with you and we’re safe, that’s it Agatha,” Rio tries to explain like it's so simple, like the truth of Agatha’s life isn’t a secret tragedy, like the world knowing of her placated shame was worth a celebration. 

 

“You told them,” Agatha scoffs, not believing it fully, wishing she hadn’t put all of her into this intoxicating trust, hoping with everything that Rio was the only good she had. 

 

She hated this, hated how she couldn’t process the conflict of it, hated that she’d made Rio keep the secret in the first place. She hated her own anger, this crippling frustration that she knew Rio didn’t deserve to have to carry this reality all by herself, that her life had scared her enough to make a safe word with her parents if anything ever went wrong. It was endearing, if Agatha didn’t feel entirely betrayed. 

 

“Let me out of the car,” Agatha demands, her hand coming to unbuckle herself, reaching for the handle. 

 

“Dude, stop,” Rio takes her right hand off the wheel, trying to stop Agatha from opening the door, the vehicle still very much in motion. 

 

In the scramble of it, Rio ends up pulling over a moment later. As soon as the car comes to a stop, Agatha moves to get out, but Rio doesn’t let her get far, her arms circling around her waist from inside, tugging her back down into the seat. 

 

Rio keeps her in place, Agatha straining against her, she musters the strength to lean over the console (and Agatha) to pull the passenger down shut, recreate the barrier in hopes it’s one more thing Agatha has to get through to escape. 

 

“Are you done?” Rio remarks clearly annoyed that Agatha is still trying to break out of Rio’s hold. 

 

It would be funny in another life. Rio holding onto both of Agatha’s wrists as she tried to pull them from her grasp with no luck, the intense pout on her face never leaving as she heaved her body toward the door, Rio undeterred and unimpressed by her best efforts.

 

In another life. Where Agatha’s face wasn’t royally fucked up. Where Rio could kiss her without fear of her mother hearing them. Where Rio didn’t have to hold onto her heavy secrets at all. 

 

Agatha pouts up at her, halting her movements as their eyes meet again. 

 

Rio sighs, the edge of an explanation on her tongue and an Agatha who is half willing to listen. 

 

“I didn’t say anything to them,” there’s this urgent coating to the words, a reminder in the way she’d heard Rio lie before, to nuns, to peers, and this wasn’t it, “They kind of guessed, not exactly what was going on, but that something was off. We made a code word, just in case. They didn’t pry for anything else, okay?”

 

Agatha stares at her, trying to decide if this is the exact truth, trying to kill her own bias, weigh out whether she trusts Rio because it’s reality or because she’s already wrapped around her finger, entranced with this person to a degree that she can’t separate earnest logic from simply following what she wants to believe. 

 

It’s a pointless attempt, Rio looking at her like her heart is open on the table, outside of her body, a show of how far she’s willing to go to keep her safe. 

 

It bleeds her, breaks free a new library of self-hatred, the grief in Rio’s eyes that Agatha had pressed into them with her own trembling hands. 

 

Agatha wants to kiss her, apologize for the weapons she’s forged against Rio’s heart out of fear, sing of the gold Rio should be adorned with, replace the heavy armor she never needed to wear. 

 

For all the hard fought wars, Agatha would never believe she deserved to be saved.
