Chapter 3

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Proverbs 31:30-Charm is deceptive, and beauty is fleeting; but a woman who fears the LORD is to be praised.

 

Looking in the mirror had always felt like an act of rebellion, a calloused hand keeping her eyes open to stare at the truth of her face. Even when it wasn’t bruised and aching, Agatha had always been taught that she was nothing special, that flaunting things that weren’t her relationship with God were not only frowned upon, but strictly forbidden. The no makeup rule had come before Agatha really knew what it was, never had a chance to use it. 

 

She’d experiment in Rio’s stockpile, a collection consisting of several barely touched palettes of eye shadows and bronzer. She’d let Rio put eyeliner on her once or twice before deciding it didn’t suit her. 

 

Agatha liked having the space to try it out, had let Rio make her into art several times in a way that wasn’t just for covering up bruises. It felt powerful and delicate, the appeal of it not just being the way Rio had to be so close to apply lipstick on her. 

 

And she loved Rio’s eyes, maybe just a little bit more when they were framed with mascara, the “natural” look she’d wear to school most days to cover any pending pimples. 

 

It felt like an escape, an expression of the type of person she wanted other’s to see her as, something she could have full control over. 

 

Another thing Evanora had taken from her. 

 

Looking in the mirror now felt like an axe coated in honey, a slow moving ripple of anger, the urge to weep but the numb blocking out the chances of rain. 

 

Rio’s bathroom is small, a tiny square connected to her bedroom. The walls are blue gray, the towels, the shower curtain, the bath mat are all pale green. The soap dispenser is shaped like a dinosaur, something Rio’s had since childhood and refused to get rid of. The hairbrush on the sink, the water splatter on the mirror, the stray chunk of toothpaste by the drain. All evidence of existence, a place all Rio, tracks that Agatha was never allowed to leave in her own home. 

 

Agatha’s avoided this as long as possible, as she usually does, taking her time before having to access the damage. The bruise on her right eye isn’t the worst she’s ever seen, the purple of it sweeping under her eye, a streak of bruise along the bone there, tailing over the top of her eye lid. The swelling color something like eyeshadow. There’s dried blood just outside her nostril, something easy to miss, the dried stickiness a feeling she’d numbed out until now. Her cheekbone still stings, the redness pale against the swirl of harsher bruises. On her left brow, a split of skin, perhaps from the impact of skin pressing tight enough to break. 

 

“I don’t think you need stitches, so that’s good news,” Rio voices casually when she sees Agatha eyeing the wound in the mirror, she knows how to walk this line of commentary, not scaring Agatha away with too much at once, no pity, just attention. 

 

Rio’s just come back from the hall closet, she places the brown bottle of hydrogen peroxide on the sink, before opening a drawer underneath, finding a pack of round cotton pads.

 

Agatha doesn’t sit on the sink, their natural heights giving Rio the perfect vantage point to clean the cut above her eyebrow. They stand close, Agatha’s back pressed to the sink, Rio licking her lips, focusing on pressing an adequate amount of peroxide into the cotton. 

 

Her hand comes up to Agatha’s neck, the tips of her fingers brushing just behind her ear, an effort to hold her steady. Agatha knows this. Knows that Rio is holding on like always, that as easy as it would be to kiss her, she never does. 

 

Rio searches her eyes, a practiced gaze of neutrality that Agatha can see right through. There’s the hurt right there in brown irises, the barely there way they grow darker, the slight curve of her eyebrows. It feels like yearning, something like Agatha’s reflected back. 

 

Rio won’t kiss her, not now. 

 

“It’s gonna sting,” Rio warns, a gentle calm that Agatha can’t process, the explicit care she never received as a child.

 

”I know,” Agatha rolls her eyes, a deflection from the butterflies.

 

Rio smiles a little in reaction, happy at least to get some reaction out of Agatha, knowing she hit a nerve. 

 

But she presses forward, tilting Agatha’s head down slightly, pushing up on her tippy toes for just a second, settling back down half an inch closer before actually touching the cotton to Agatha’s skin. 

 

Agatha closes her eyes, the pain of it jumping back to life, almost as if the adrenaline had finally worn off. Rio’s fingers stroke the side of her neck, an instant attempt at comfort. 

 

Being this close to Rio sparks her heart beat, a magnetism of silver linings. A place under Rio’s hands that felt like an umbrella in a rainstorm, a place to rest when she’d only ever been running in fear. She sets her wrists against Rio’s hips without much thinking.

 

She blames it on the pain, the need to hold on to something. It is not because she’s dreamed of tracing every surface of Rio’s skin, it is not because Agatha could live in this moment forever. 

 

Still, she revels in the fact that Rio doesn’t seem to pull away, focused on cleaning away specks of dry blood and making sure it won’t get infected. Agatha opens her eyes to look at her again, hesitating for a breath, unsure if she could be this close and not combust. 

 

Rio finishes just as Agatha finds her eyes again, the stare of it so soft. Agatha feels Rio’s finger twitch against her neck, maybe involuntary, the thread of a desire to pull her closer, a droplet of fear pressed into her forehead. 

 

“Let me get a bandaid”

 

It’s hushed, a sentence just for the space between them, a loss as Rio pulls away.

 

Rio secures it without much fuss, sticking it over the cut, an ease in the way Rio put all her focus into things that mattered, clumsy everywhere else. She helps Agatha clean the blood from under her nose, a wet rag wiping it away. 

 

“We should ice your eye,” Rio paints their next direction, suddenly rushing out of the bathroom to put the hydrogen peroxide back. Agatha hates that Rio’s words portray it as a “them” problem, that Rio includes herself in the need to heal her. 

 

Agatha doesn’t know what she would do if Rio didn’t actively try to lessen her burden, even through small gestures like this, it felt like a weight they could carry together.

 

When Rio leaves the bathroom, she misses the proximity, the electricity of Rio’s hands. But the emptiness in her heart doesn’t settle back in, this room so Rio-coated, her energy still keeping Agatha up right as she walks away. 

 

“Let me change quick,” Rio chirps, her face toward the closet, clothes spilling out from the bottom, the door not being able to close for several years. 

 

Agatha busies herself trying to look away, her peripheral catching the way Rio tugs off her blazer, pulls down her skirt. She closes her eyes again, pressing away the thoughts of soft skin, the curve of thighs, the dull ridges of her rib cage. 

 

She only turns around at the sound of Rio stepping back towards her, the taller girl now in an old gray Paramore tshirt and basketball shorts she’s rolled up too high. She’s mid way through tying her hair up, an effortless little bun, the stray edges in the front purposely left out. 

 

Rio’s kitchen isn’t extravagant, the house itself smaller than Agatha’s but somehow always feeling so much fuller. There are always fresh flowers on the table, a gift from her father to her mother every time the last batch dies, a symbol of the continued effort to support a marriage. The table itself worn and scratched, the table legs wobbly on one side, evidence of years of shared meals. Dishes sit drying next to the sink, Rio’s favorite mug, a wide orange coffee cup covered in fall leaves that she uses year round, mostly to eat Froot Loops. Decorative towels with different Spanish words, a microwave with bits of splattered tomato sauce, magnets on the fridge, a birthday card from Rio to her father securely clipped to it’s metal surface. 

 

Rio bounds through the space like she’s unafraid, no tiptoeing, no slowing down around corners. And yes, her parents aren’t home, but Rio moves just as freely when they are. 

 

Agatha idly wonders what that’s like: existing in a home that felt comfortable enough to sail through, open drawers loudly, rummage through the pantry, leave dishes in the sink without worry. 

 

“You okay?” Rio asks like it’s not a loaded question, like they haven’t spent the last hour trying to piece Agatha back together, like her silence isn’t warranted.

 

And maybe it’s not with Rio, Agatha always willing to speak in front of her, the filter of her sliding away with Rio, a safety she’d been reaching to for the past four years.

 

Agatha hesitates, waits for Rio to put two Uncrustables in the air fryer (she swears they taste best that way), return her attention back to her. 

 

Agatha sits at the kitchen island, the marble counter enacting at least five feet between them, Rio on the other side, grabbing two water bottles from the fridge. It’s that seamless care that never makes its way into conversation, the immediate inclusion of her, like it was not a possibility to Rio that she wouldn’t automatically provide Agatha with a meal (even if it was just a childhood delicacy), more than she could say about her own mother. 

 

“Yeah, I just…”

 

But, Agatha trails off, unsure of her own thoughts, unsure of the truth. 

 

Rio looks at her, seeming to suddenly remember the black eye, maybe it's a good excuse to not push Agatha to speak when she isn’t ready, maybe it’s Rio changing the subject for them both. 

 

“Ice!” She turns back around, opening the freezer, “Corn okay? I don’t think we have an ice pack”

 

Agatha just reaches out her hand, a signal for Rio to pass it over, her eyes done with the whole situation, her heart beating harder at the way Rio seemed caught up in the worry of frozen corn doing an adequate job. 

 

Agatha basically slaps the bag to her face, the crunch of it making Rio wince. 

 

“Dude, be careful”

 

”It’s already fucked up, how much more damage could I really do?” Agatha shrugs. 

 

“I’d like both your eyes to stay functional, so chill out,” Rio answers without thought as she opens the air fryer, trying her best to keep up the conversation while grabbing the food out with her bare hands. 

 

“Says the one about to burn their fingers off” 

 

Rio just looks at her, offended, the Uncrustables still not moved. 

 

Agatha rolls her eyes for good measure, a reminder that she’s getting up to prove a point, not to be helpful. She drops the bag of frozen corn onto the island without any hesitation. 

 

She grabs a spatula from the drawer next to the stove, knowing where they were kept from watching Rio’s mother make them tostones as after school snacks hundreds of times. 

 

“Make yourself useful and get me something to put them on,” Agatha shoos Rio out of her way with the spatula wielding it like a hammer she’s about to do some serious masculine work with. Rio can’t help but smile at her, the way Agatha could transform herself into this intimidating figure even though Rio knew she possessed absolutely no upper body strength. 

 

Rio grabs two small plates, ones that might be used for birthday cake or as tea saucers, one is a little chipped, but Agatha is always charmed by the character of it, something well-used, a remnant of family.

 

She scoops the pocket sandwiches onto them with ease, a smug look meeting Rio’s soft smile. 

 

“You make it look so easy”

 

”it is easy”

 

—-

 

Agatha wouldn’t admit it, but her favorite room of Rio’s house was the sun room. The wide windows let in so much light, a glowing ambiance of dull orange from sunrise to sunset. There were too many plants to count, small cacti and winding vines, orchids and a hydrangea bush. She’d absolutely never admit that it was her favorite because of the way Rio always lit up in here, the way Rio could spend hours here taking care of the all the plants, would talk about each one and how it had been growing steadily, watered each one to a specification that Agatha had no clue how she remembered. 

 

It felt like an extra door to knowing all of Rio, a place where Rio could speak clearly, say the things she would never say anywhere else. 

 

Agatha remembers freshman year, mid January. She was fourteen and Evanora would never let her have sleepovers. The ever growing fear of life itself had cracked open just enough when her mother was away for a principal’s conference several states away. It was a weekend and Agatha thanked God Rio’s parents agreed without asking to speak to her mother. 

 

They’d decided to sleep in the sun room, sleeping bags and snacks, an idea from Rio when Agatha had told her she’d never been camping. Rio roasted marshmallows over the flame of the stove in the kitchen, Agatha watched with astonishment, envious of the way Rio seemed to take normal teenage risks, unafraid of the smoke alarm going off at 1 in the morning with her parents asleep upstairs. 

 

It was then that Agatha realized how safe she felt with Rio. There had always been this pull, the butterflies, the way Agatha would lose her thoughts the first few times they’d spoken. But it was then, 5 months into friendship, that Agatha knew this was home, Rio was the place to land when nothing else felt right. 

 

It was that night in their sleeping bags, Rio still had chocolate on the corner of her mouth, her eyes starting to close when Agatha started to speak. 

 

“Can I tell you something?” She turned on her side to face Rio. 

 

And the sleep in Rio’s eyes suddenly vanishes, replaced by something so open and delicate. 

 

“Of course”

 

Agatha relishes in the way there’s no fear in Rio’s words, but almost wishes there was, almost wishes she had better prepared her for impact. 

 

“Remember a few months ago, when my lip was busted open”

 

Rio’s eyebrows furrow, maybe confusion at why Agatha was bringing it up, the pain there as well, at the memory of her friend in pain. Rio’s eyes trace over her bottom lip, finding comfort in the way the skin had healed. 

 

“Yeah, you said you slipped and hit it on the bathroom counter”

 

”I lied” Agatha confesses, but doesn’t continue right away, she waits for Rio to be mad, to question it, to tell her to leave. She waits for God’s wrath, waits for all the unholy consequences. 

 

But Rio just waits for her, holding out for an explanation. It’s in this moment too, that Agatha decides Rio is too good for her.

 

”My mother,” Agatha breathes, sinking further into her sleeping bag minutely. “She hit me with a hanger” her eyes close, unable to look at Rio as the words spill out. It feels like pulling the trigger. “You can’t tell anyone” the words are so small, barely there as Agatha’s eyes no longer listen to her harsh pleas to not cry.

 

The first thing she feels is Rio shift closer, she isn’t holding her, but their sleeping bags are now close enough that Rio’s thighs push against her. 

 

“The bruise you had on your cheek the first day of school?” Rio’s voice is so soft, an attempt at a question, trying to put all the pieces together. 

 

Rio had once told her that the bruise was one of the reasons she approached her that day, that she’d thought maybe Agatha was the type to wrestle with boys or climb trees without fearing how to get back down, that the thought intrigued her. Another bit of shame that Rio had waltzed into her life because of Evanora. 

 

“The broken finger?” Rio asked another question when Agatha doesn’t answer the first one, Agatha’s eyes opening finally.

 

She just nods slowly, her eyes not meeting Rio’s, so afraid of the hurt that might be reflected there, unable to see her like that. Agatha was shaking, her arms wrapped around herself, the warmth of the room, of Rio beside her not enough to push away the adrenaline. 

 

“You can’t tell anyone”

 

Agatha finally finds her eyes in the dark when Rio doesn’t respond, finally realizes just how close they are. It’s shattering and comforting all at once, the way Rio looks at her like she doesn’t know what to do, what to say, the way Rio is bolted into her side, not running away. 

 

Rio’s arm comes out of her sleeping bag, she presses her hand over Agatha’s shoulder, a squeeze that morphs into a delicate stroke of her thumb. The touch alone is enough to settle some of her fraying nerves. 

 

She watches the conflict in Rio’s eyes, her care for Agatha eclipsed by the pain that her friend had suffered through this all alone. Rio bites her lip, trying her best to settle on the right decision. 

 

“I won’t tell anyone”

 

Sitting in the same room, four years later felt like a different lifetime with all the same themes. They were still those people, wrapped up in the same trauma, but time had made it feel eerily distant. 

 

Agatha was sat on the sofa with her legs crossed, the frozen bag of corn was half melted and put back in the freezer for now. Her face still felt hot and sore, a prickling itch from the cut on her brow bone. 

 

The TV was on, an old flat screen that turned on and off without prompting sometimes (Rio always blamed it on ghosts). It was an old rerun of an SVU episode, a show Rio had been exposed to way too young, and Agatha had only known about since being her friend. It was more background noise than anything as Agatha was currently using one of Rio’s coloring books, stealing her good markers to color in a picture of SpongeBob and Patrick jellyfishing. 

 

Rio was on the floor laying on her stomach, propped up on her elbows with her feet in the air, focused on her own image, a way more detailed color by number book of famous paintings. Agatha wasn’t sure how Rio possessed the core strength to lay like that for over an hour, how she possessed the patience to color such small spaces of Starry Night. 

 

Rio looks up at her, catching her staring, a game they no longer tease each other for. Rio had stopped calling her out on it a long time ago, Agatha didn’t know why. Maybe it was easier that way, Agatha never giving her an explanation for it anyway. 

 

“Can you stop hogging the blues?” Rio says instead of anything else. 

 

“I’m not hogging them,” Agatha throws two markers, both shades of blue, both bouncing off of Rio’s hip, definitely not one of the places Agatha was staring at, the way her t-shirt rode up just enough to expose skin. 

 

Rio turns her body enough to snatch them from the carpet where they landed, giving Agatha a glare as she turns. 

 

“Last time I checked SpongeBob is yellow, so you shouldn’t need these anyway” Rio continues, obviously not done with the banter. She uncaps her marker and focuses back on her book. 

 

“The water is blue, dork”

 

Rio flops onto her side suddenly, the task at hand seemingly forgotten for the moment. 

 

“Now Agatha, are those words truly fit for a woman of God to use?” Rio asks, doing her best impression of the most snobby nuns they’d encountered. 

 

“Well, lying is a sin, Rio. And you are definitely a dork.” Agatha hides her chuckle, secretly loving the way they could maintain this back and forth without hurting each other’s feelings. 

 

“Doesn’t mean you have to be rude,” Rio is sitting up now, the markers forgotten on the carpet, the pout on her face something both juvenile and alluring, lips that call out to Agatha like a sign from the heavens. 

 

“You shall not bear false witness against your neighbor,” Agatha quotes Exodus to make her point, not because she truly believes lying is the worst possible action to take, but more for the sake of disagreeing with Rio, more for the hope that it gets under Rio’s skin. 

 

“Okay, Wanda,” Rio teases, bringing up their classmate as a purposeful dig at her unending need to stitch scripture through everyday conversations.

 

It reminds Agatha of yesterday, of the way Rio seemed so thrown by the topic of homosexuality, she tries to push it away. 

 

”Okay, comparing me to Wanda is wild”

 

”Eh, I know you look up to her,” Rio shrugs, teasing a little further before laughing, unable to stay serious at the absurdity of her own words.

 

Agatha just squints at her, willing herself to not fall harder at the sight of Rio innocently laughing at her own joke, the quiet joy of it.

 

”Don’t make me throw the rest of the markers at you.”

 

—-

 

Luke 8:17- For nothing is hidden that will not be made manifest, and nothing concealed that will not be known and come to light.

 

The barrel of cheese balls is something Evanora would never allow inside her house. A gluttonous snack that offered absolutely no nutritional value. It sits on Agatha’s lap, sat in a lawn chair in Rio’s backyard. There’s a small garden to her right, a fence that surrounds the back half of the house, green grass kept manicured, a grill. 

 

There’s other chairs available around the table, but Rio is standing a few feet away trying to catch cheese balls in her mouth.

 

Agatha has pretty good aim, but it wouldn’t matter either way, Rio fully committed to diving to the floor if it means successfully catching the snack. 

 

“Slow down, I’m still chewing,” Rio speaks around the two she’d caught one after the other, Agatha’s hand already loaded with the next. 

 

Agatha snorts at the gross orange slime stuck to Rio’s teeth, she pops the cheese ball into her own mouth, shaking her head at the activities they considered fun. 

 

“I don’t know how you’re still alive with all the crap you ingest,” Agatha notes, seeing as how she’s at least 30 cheese balls in with no signs of stopping. 

 

“You’re just jealous my stomach is indestructible,” Rio flexes like she’s Superman, a definite power pose. Agatha tries her best not to look at the soft muscles of her biceps, the veins in her forearms. 

 

“Okay, super dork” Agatha throws another cheese ball, more like a fast ball than a lob.

 

Rio slaps it away instead of attempting a catch that she wasn’t ready for, the orange puff falling into the grass.

 

”Why you so mean to me?” Rio pouts again, but Agatha knows this is par for the course of their dynamic, Agatha only comfortable enough to be sarcastic with Rio, the only person she feels safe enough to joke with. 

 

“Don’t act like you don’t like it,” Agatha smirks.

 

”dONt aCt lIKE yOU DOnt liKE It,” Rio mocks her words, scurrying towards her, her hands already out in warning, Agatha knows what’s coming.

 

”If you tickle me, I will kill you,” She threatens Rio, a handful of cheese balls at the ready for ammo to protect her. 

 

“Fine,” Rio relents easily, “only cuz you asked nicely,” she winks before turning away, and Agatha has to swallow down the way her mouth waters. 

 

When she comes out of her moment of weakness, Rio has bent down to pick up the cheese ball she’d unceremoniously hit to the ground.

 

”Jesus, Rio please don’t eat that”

 

”I’m not,” Rio instantly defends herself, “Don’t want a squirrel to get it and get sick, his stomach ain’t as strong as mine,” she voices her explanation like a child trying to save a dying butterfly, placing it onto the table to discard later. 

 

“Okay, I’m ready,” Rio starts again a few moments later, stepping back, getting into position like she was next at bat and Agatha was the pitcher. 

 

“Hmmm, I think you need to earn it,” Agatha teases now, maybe a little annoyed at Rio having the upper hand, that wink doing more than she’d like to admit. 

 

“How do I earn it?” Rio chirps back almost too easily convinced to play along with whatever game Agatha had concocted. 

 

“I’ll ask you a question, a correct answer gets you a cheese ball,” Agatha shrugs, the rules clearly on the table.

 

”Fine, ask your questions,” Rio tries to appear annoyed by it, but Agatha can read the amusement there. 

 

“What’s my favorite color?” 

 

Rio looks at her like she’s crazy, like Agatha had given her a free pass, like Rio knew this was a soft ball question to catch her off guard for the hard balls to come. 

 

“Green,” Rio smirks, purposely answering wrong to see if the only consequence was no snacks being thrown her way. 

 

Agatha shakes her head.

 

”You’re only depriving yourself,” Agatha laughs, rewarding herself with two cheese balls, as if taking the one Rio would have earned with a correct answer, teasing Rio as if the sodium intake directly translated to her worth. 

 

“Next question” Rio pushes forward, hands on her hips, waiting impatiently, Agatha takes an extra moment to contemplate. 

 

“What’s my middle name?”

 

Rio huffs. 

 

“You won’t tell me!” Rio whines, “I’ve been begging you to tell me forever, this game isn’t fair”

 

”Not my fault you answered both questions wrong,” Agatha giggles. 

 

“I change my mind, I think I am gonna tickle you,” Rio threatens but doesn't move, knowing the words are enough to get a reaction.

 

Agatha throws her hands up in surrender.

 

”Wait, wait, wait. Let me ask another question.”

 

”Okay, go ahead,” Rio nods, thinking she’s finally got the upper hand again, waiting for a question akin to ‘what color is the sky?’ The color she’s always found in Agatha’s eyes, but no, her friend has other plans, feeling willing to take a risk. 

 

“Are you scared about going away for college?” Agatha asks, soft but certain, trying to focus on the orange powder coating her fingers and not the way Rio’s face falls. 

 

They’d had conversations like this before. Agatha had to convince Rio to dorm at a school several hours away for a better opportunity, a program more suited to her goals, even if it meant they’d be far away. She knew Rio was excited about studying botany, exploring a new city, but she could also sense the fear around it, that the independence would be a learning curve, not seeing her parents, not seeing Agatha would make everything feel empty. Rio hadn’t brought it up, especially after Agatha made it abundantly clear that she wouldn’t let Rio turn the opportunity down for her. 

 

“Agatha,” Rio’s stance changes, the gears in her mind skirting forward, the game pauses, Rio pulling out a chair and sitting in it to face Agatha, she perches herself over the edge, their knees touching, Rio looking at her like she’s about to tell a 6 year old their pet rabbit died, “I’m not going.”

 

Agatha’s mind takes a moment to compute the words, settle on them as a clear destination, her eyebrows furrow, “What?” Is all she can manage, shaking her head to shake away the confusion. 

 

“I’m going to Darkhold. With you.” Rio tries to explain gently, a severed confession that rings out like a hopeful whisper, wanting Agatha to find the relief of it more than the rage.

 

”Y- you can’t fucking do that,” Agatha pushes the barrel into Rio’s hands, not being able to stay still, to be this close to Rio when her friend was giving up her future for her. Rio was usually elated when Agatha cursed out loud, something special about the freedom of it, but right now, her eyes only read as contemplative, a truth that Agatha couldn’t fully read. 

 

She stands now, her arms crossed looking at Rio like she’d killed her first born.

 

”I told you to go, Rio. I saw the acceptance letter. Why would you stay here when you can fucking escape?”

 

And maybe that was the crux of it, Rio had nothing to run away from. Her family that loved and supported her was right here in West View, Darkhold University was giving her just as good of a scholarship without having to move (even if the school wasn’t as good), and Ag-

 

“I’m not leaving you here alone.” Rio voices like a prayer, a plea to Agatha to see her point of view, “You’re not ruining my life, Agatha. I made this decision.”

 

Agatha closes her eyes, the sting of surprise still jolting whenever Rio showed her how much she cared. A few tears leak out, she turns toward the sun still high in the sky, half wishing the rays would burn her into ash, rid her of all these heavy emotions. 

 

She feels Rio press into her from behind, her arms circling around her stomach and pulling her back into her chest, Rio’s chin settling against her shoulder. She tries to breathe, settle into Rio’s hold, commit the warmth to memory, be brave enough to not pull away when the feelings become overwhelming.

 

”I’m sorry I didn’t tell you sooner,” Rio apologizes into her hair, a whisper for just Agatha. In truth she knew she could never stay mad at Rio, especially when they both knew the way Agatha would react, would struggle with letting Rio stay for her. 

 

“I can handle Evanora, it’ll be fi-“ Agatha starts to lie, a final attempt at convincing Rio.

 

As much as she’d miss her, as scared as she was of being alone, of starting this new chapter without her best friend, she couldn’t clip Rio’s wings. 

 

“Agatha,” Rio cuts her off, a gentle warning, “I know you can, you are the strongest person I know, and I have no doubts about that. But, I won’t let you do this alone.”

 

Agatha can hear in her voice that she’s holding back tears of her own, she hates it, the flow of pain that leaks from Agatha into Rio she can’t ever find how to stop. 

 

She turns in Rio’s arms needing to see her face, this complex care resting in brown irises, a wrecked bliss, like this battle was worth it to keep Agatha safe. 

 

“I hate that I can’t protect you,” Rio whispers into the air between them, her arms still around Agatha’s waist, Agatha’s hands are on her face, silently wiping at fallen tears. 

 

The broken rift of Rio’s voice is too much, a reminder of all the pain she’s pressed into Rio’s heart without asking. Rio looks at her like she is holy, something to bow to, a twisted bar of nickel painted to look like gold and Rio is the only one gullible enough to see the value. 

 

Looking at her lips, wanting her this way, its electricity, a pulse of pressure, a balloon inflating, waiting for the pop. The devil on her shoulder telling her to lean in, press further into Rio’s space, kiss her for all the times she’s dreamt of them like this. The angel on her shoulder telling her that there was too much to lose, that Rio deserved better than this.

 

”Shimeath” she whispers back instead. The name of an ammonite woman in the Bible, a story of God’s judgement and revenge. 

 

Rio looks at her confused, wondering how she would be relevant, but doesn’t pull away, stays like she’d wait forever for Agatha to explain.

 

”My middle name,” she confesses.

 

”She who hears and obeys,” Rio recalls the meaning, perhaps her memory more closely aligned with Wanda than either of them would like to admit, “I don’t think that’s fitting,” Rio looks away as if contemplating the suitability of the name. 

 

Agatha laughs and it feels freeing, a press of air that makes her believe that happiness could find her somewhere, even if only in moments like this. 

 

“Look, not all of us can be the river of life,” Agatha teases, no bite behind it, secretly enamored by how her parents had named her something so powerful and beautiful without it feeling forced or odd. 

 

“Don’t be jealous that I have no middle name, Shimeath” Rio tests the new knowledge for the first time, knowing full well she’d be using the weapon Agatha had just willingly put into her hands. 

 

“Okay,” Agatha pushes out of the embrace, offended that her good-will had so quickly turned against her, “So what we’re not gonna do is- AHHH”

 

Agatha shrieks as Rio begins chasing her mid sentence, looking more than willing to tackle her to the ground. 

 

Rio catches her easily, falling to the ground less than gracefully and pulling Agatha down with her. They roll for a moment, Agatha giving up without much fight, hating how wide Rio smiled knowing she was stronger, settling facing each other, half tangled. 

 

“You are such a child,” Agatha looks at her grumpily, not happy to lay amongst the bugs.

 

“I think you owe me some cheese balls,” Rio ignores her words, her fingers busy pulling grass out of Agatha’s hair.

Chapter 4

Chapter Notes

John 15:13- Greater love has no one than this, that someone lay down his life for his friends.

 

Agatha knows better than to not come home, knows that her key turning in the door, the careful strides toward the stairs and up to her room would only breathe fire into Evanora’s eyes. 

 

She was meant to be seen and not heard, and as much as there were unspoken rules (staying home from school to conceal her wounds to protect Evanora’s image), the consequences to spending that time anywhere other than tucked into her bed, thinking about what she’d done to deserve it, were strictly prohibited. 

 

Even worse was the fact that Evanora had just established that she didn't want Agatha hanging out with Rio anymore, a truth that she hadn’t expressed to Rio for a number of reasons.

 

Agatha definitely didn’t plan on pushing Rio away simply because her mother was demanding it. Especially considering Rio was the only person who made her feel worth something. 

 

It’s a harsh contrast, stepping out of Rio’s car, safely parked a few houses down even if Evanora isn’t due home for another 30 minutes. She tries to push away the sinking feeling of ‘goodbye’, like her home wasn’t a war zone, like high school drama could be the worst of their worries. 

 

Rio squeezes her hand, the look in brown irises vowing all the unspoken promises. 

 

it feels like retreating to her cage, the day a moment of reprieve, almost as if her master had remembered her evil and was sending her back to hell.

 

Agatha sinks into her bed, the pain of her bruises mostly subsided now, the dull ache something she’d come to survive through easily, she closes her eyes, trying to focus on her breathing. 

 

The thought of Rio always a comfort, she felt desperate for wanting more, guilty that for all Rio had done for her, it was never enough to quiet the echo of desire in her chest.

 

The longing was embarrassing, this need to cross the boundaries of friendship, a tug in her heart that wanted to be entirely consumed by Rio, yet held back indefinitely by unparalleled fear. 

 

A plant that never grows past its stem, a bud that recedes into itself, no petals, no leaves. Agatha basks in the sunlight of Rio, taking in the heat of her touch, the warmth of her care, but too afraid to fully face it, a barrier of ozone keeping her from fully blooming. 

 

The contemplation only grows colder when she questions Rio’s stance, maybe Agatha had grown delusional over the years, half convinced herself that Rio must harbor some type of feelings, the way Rio was always so touchy with her, the quiet protective nature, the pained look of want, the things Agatha didn’t want to strictly file under the ‘friendship’ tab. 

 

But even if Rio shared these petulant feelings, she never acted on it either, perhaps wrapped up in her own fear. 

 

Fucking stupid. An edge they’d never leap off of for fear of leaving the other behind, caught in this tangle of unspoken words, unexplored realities, for the sake of keeping things stable. 

 

Agatha was tired. Tired of pressing over biting wounds, cycling through the catalog of places that had been marked by unpredictable rage, fighting to find her own self worth long enough to think she deserved a life that wasn’t this one. 

 

But breaking her own heart with an untimely confession would only make it worse. 

 

She bites the inside of her cheek, pushing away the sudden desire to weep.

 

She hears her mother’s key turn in the door, a quiet shuffle as she enters the house. 

 

Her heart slows, her breaths more even, the practiced tradition of listening to Evanora’s footsteps, trying to find the emotion in the way she carried herself. 

 

Agatha waits, catching the sounds with no signs of anger, the front door isn’t slammed when it closes, there doesn’t seem to be any haste in Evanora’s moments, an indication that the coast is clear for now. 

 

In truth, Agatha is never fully relaxed, a guarding wall pressed up in every moment, a coping mechanism that’s been in place for as long as she could remember, but there is still a press of relief that the upending doom remained lurking, not thundering full force. 

 

She tried to not let it sting, should have been used to the flippant disregard, the lack of mothering, but there was still this hollow feeling at the way Evanora never checked in on her, never apologized, like she truly had no care in whether Agatha lived or died. 

 

As much as she knew it would be just as toxic if her mother carried in fake ‘sorry’s or showered her in materialistic charms to win her favor, to keep her mouth shut about the abuse, a part of her still craved that attention. A part of her would always be that small girl wishing her mother would soothe her. 

 

The frustration of it swallowed her, the crushing pulse in her head lurching into a migraine. She couldn’t stomach that thought even now, that for all the harm Evanora caused her, she still wanted for the things she’d never have in this lifetime. 

 

Her phone buzzes underneath her. 

 

Rio. 

 

Always knowing the exact moment she needs her somehow. 

 

It’s an instagram notification, a post Rio shared with her.

 

An illustrated image of two frogs dressed as cowboys under the words ‘me and my bestie sharing one brain cell’.

 

Agatha will try to push it away, a small empty gesture of friendship. She hearts the message, trying not to mull over the perfect timing, set 5 minutes after Evanora gets home, from an art account Rio knew Agatha liked. 

 

Everything Rio did felt purposeful, intended and certain. It was difficult to untangle that from every instance, the ways Rio was different with Agatha, a definition of friendship or something more. Agatha could never be sure. 

 

She opens Rio’s story, a repost of a screenshotted tweet

 

’imagine someone trying to fix themselves so they can love you exactly how you deserve to be loved’

 

Agatha pushes away all the attempts of reading into it, letting it fester into a meaning she can’t make into something tangible. 

 

She’s exhausted of the almosts, looking at Rio’s lips as she dabs makeup over her bruises, being close, reveling under Rio’s touch, Rio’s attention, but never staking claim. The knot is starting to feel suffocating, a balloon ready to burst.

Forty five minutes of Rio next to her, the bench allowing them to be closer, Rio’s thigh pressed into hers from the proximity, something she didn’t question, they’re high school definitely over populated leaving few open spaces at lunch tables. 

 

It was hard to sit alone, be excluded from the mammoth of teenage girls, a feverish sea of dark blue pleated skirts, knee high socks, and pressed blazers. 

 

High school was a lot less clique-y when they all operated out of the same string of religious restrictions. Less little groups of specification and more like a spectrum from absolutely devout to girls forced here by their parents to the few stragglers who weren’t Catholic, drawn in by the status of paying an unnecessary amount in class dues. 

 

Agatha herself doesn’t fit in to those parameters that easily, forced here by her mother? Yep. But also floating through some sense of privilege, all the staff operating under the wrath of her mother. Something not exactly in the vein of teacher’s pet, but a taste of untouchable. Nuns weren’t exactly lining up to send her to the principal’s office.

Mark 11:25- And when you stand praying, if you hold anything against anyone, forgive them, so that your Father in heaven may forgive you your sins.

“So, are you done being fucking stupid?” 

 

Rio knows what she means, quieting all the dangerous whispers of doubt, brushing away the fear that Agatha would be upset, would push her away, would hate her for this. Rio knows it's Agatha’s way of saying she loves her, that nothing could break their bond. 

 

“Yeah,” Rio’s voice creaks, looking sheepish, but letting the solid relief hit her all the same. 

 

She reaches for some of the cheap brown paper towels, stepping towards Agatha. 

 

“Stop crying, idiot,” Rio chuckles, trying to nudge them back into practiced territory, “You’re ruining your makeup”, she adds, dabbing at Agatha’s face delicately. 

 

Agatha pushes down Rio’s arms, pulling her into a harsh embrace, wanting to be as close as possible, breathing in everything she could. 

 

Rio chuckles into her shoulder, sighing at the comfort of Agatha in her arms.

 

”We should probably make sure Billy isn’t having a heart attack,” Rio whispers into her after a moment. 

 

“One more minute”

 

Chapter End Notes

Ummm yeah, things are occurring….more things soon hopefully

Chapter 5

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Psalm 27:14- Wait on the Lord; be of good courage, and He shall strengthen your heart; Wait, I say, on the Lord.

 

Rio’s hair is down.

 

It’s obviously not the first time she’s worn it out like this to school, the sure waves of it coming over her shoulders, but everything feels different now. 

 

Now that Agatha knew Rio was interested in women, everything had a new lens. 

 

Like Agatha had permission to look, her stares not something she needed to be ashamed of, like Rio had rolled out the welcome mat just for Agatha to ogle at her.

 

And it’s not like Agatha didn’t love every other way Rio would wear her hair, the go-to bun a standard crowd pleaser, Agatha loved the way it exposed Rio’s neck, the flex of her throat, the soft skin on display like a vacant wall begging to be covered in graffiti. 

 

But there was something undeniably feminine at the way her hair framed her face, fell in thick curtains, played along her collar bones over her uniform. And it was making Agatha swoon every time she was near her. 

 

As infuriating as anatomy class was, Agatha was a lot more willing to push through her disgust at frog dissections if it meant she got to watch Rio engaged in something she found genuinely interesting.

 

Rio loved science, mostly the plant stuff, chlorophyll and photosynthesis and all that crap. But she also didn’t discriminate her sciences, still invested in learning all she could whether it be prehistoric theory, human biology, or even physics for fucks sake. 

 

Agatha could only get behind it for the sake of seeing Rio in her element, some of the only classes Rio wasn’t doodling for 45 minutes straight, giving her full attention to the lesson.

 

Until of course Sister Eunice spiraled out of questions about evolution and tracked back into the “God is our lone creator” bull shit. 

 

Still, Agatha wouldn’t be surprised if Rio was spending her free time reading their science textbooks front to back. 

 

Agatha could allow Rio’s attention to be somewhere other than her without being jealous if it was given to nerd shit. Rio had ranted to her on several occasions about how science only consisted of theories and how she couldn’t fathom that in some sense most of them couldn’t be absolutely proven given their specific limited perception and Agatha would have told anyone other than Rio to “please shut the fuck up”.

 

And maybe it wasn’t just the hair, or the rapt attention making her go all heart eyes for Rio (okay, more so than usual), maybe it was this shift of sorts, this feeling like Rio was different too now, more open, more clear.

 

”Do your parents know?” Agatha asks on the ride back after the diner.

 

Only secure in Rio’s passenger seat after Billy apologized to Rio so hard Agatha thought he might pass out, followed by Rio rubbing his shoulder and profusely telling him they were cool. 

 

“No,” Rio peaks at her for a moment, keeping her attention mostly on the road, “I don’t think they’d be mad, just surprised maybe,” she shrugs. 

 

“Did you think I’d be mad?”

 

Rio takes a moment to mull it over. 

 

“Maybe not mad, just different.”

 

Agatha hated that fear, but knew it well, this unending battle that changing anything between them would shatter her, losing this Rio would kill her. 

 

And now almost a week later, it had been different, maybe not in any of the ways Rio feared, but there was a change in undercurrent, the resounding energy an echo of a taste Agatha had never experienced before. 

 

It felt like a cliff, or maybe a mountain, a precipice of deciding whether to keep climbing or fall. Maybe it was just Rio feeling like she didn’t have to hide herself anymore, that quiet shame in touching Agatha without her knowing the truth. 

 

Agatha’s bruises were healing, the faint reminders of hazy discolored skin, the cut on her eyebrow sealed and fading. And usually this tide of healing pressed in new anxiety, the longer they’d go without an outburst from Evanora the more she put her guard up, prepared her mind for another release of trauma.

 

But this time, there was something settling against her differently, maybe it was hope, maybe it was this delusional tug toward the future, a place in her mind where she could see tomorrow and the edges of it weren’t dark. 

 

Rio and Agatha were always lab partners and now was no different. Rio in blue latex clothes, chunky protective goggles, holding a scalpel…

 

Okay, so what if Agatha was turned on by that image. 

 

But, today they weren’t doing any dissections, no gloves, or goggles, or scalpels. 

 

Instead, they were measuring each other’s heart rates, an experiment to understand the cardiovascular system that Agatha thought was a big fucking waste of time. Obviously, the heart beats faster after physical activity. 

 

And how does anyone expect her resting heart rate to be normal when Rio’s got two fingers up to the pulse point on the side of her neck tucked beneath her jaw, her brown eyes portraying something conflicted. Rio doesn’t look at her, but at the stopwatch, waiting for a minute to pass as she counts the amount of times Agatha’s artery bounces against her fingers. 

 

“Are you nervous?” Rio smirks at her as she records Agatha’s higher than average resting heart rate. 

 

“I never let my guard down around Sister Eunice,” Agatha deflects, happy to get the laugh out of Rio, helping her to steer away from the truth. 

 

That Rio makes her feel crazy, her heart pounding in her ears at their proximity, her blush curling up her neck. 

 

“Okay,” Rio slinks back toward their handout after coming out of her laughter, “now do 20 jumping jacks”

 

”Why am I the one who has to do the jumping jacks?” Agatha huffs, half rhetorical, the way Rio naturally took the lead on all of their labs. 

 

“I’m the scientist, you’re my guinea pig,” Rio supplies an answer swiftly, reaching forward to boop Agatha on the nose.

 

Agatha grimaces, “I’d rather be a rabbit”

 

”Lucky for you,” Rio offers without a misstep, never deterred by Agatha’s quips, “I’m also a magician,” Rio feigns the standard magic trick of pulling a coin from Agatha’s ear with her pencil as her prop of choice. 

 

Agatha just looks at her, unimpressed, her heart singing at how adorably goofy Rio is, how her flow of lighthearted comments met Agatha’s deadpan detached sense of humor so well.

 

”Get it, cause rabbits. Magician hats,” Rio tries to explain, a bit she’d play into often like Agatha simply didn’t understand the joke, because in no way could the lack of reaction stem from Rio not being funny. 

 

“I’m gonna do the jumping jacks now,” Agatha cracks her a smile, pushing them out of their back and forth for the time being. 

 

—-

 

“You seem different,” Jen says offhandedly as they walk from lunch to their next class, pre-calculus, one of the only classes Rio doesn’t have with her. 

 

Agatha doesn’t respond with a verbal answer, turns to look at Jen with a raised eyebrow, wondering when the fuck they crossed the boundary of commenting on each other’s perceived changes.

 

”Good different,” Jen clarifies.

 

And maybe if Jennifer Kale were anybody else, she’d think good of her commentary, but Agatha knew better, knew Jen was teetering close to unknown territory on purpose, doing her best to get a reaction without completely stepping over lines. 

 

“How so?” Agatha asks, too curious to stop herself, even if she wasn’t sure about trusting her classmate’s opinions in general. 

 

“You seem…brighter maybe, like you’re actually excited for something,” Jennifer scoffs to herself, “I've never seen you excited.”

 

“Oh” Agatha scowls, taking in the words, letting them bounce around her head.

 

Because how had Jennifer noticed the shift, this imperceptible movement that even Agatha couldn’t fully pin down. This perhaps tangible difference in the way she floated through existence, now some stroke of color in the sea of drab. 

 

She decidedly was not thinking about it anymore, caught in the purgatory of trying to assign meaning to every interaction with Rio, bit never growing the back bone to actually ask her about it. 

 

And Jen’s revelation didn’t change that, Jen only spoke of a change in Agatha. Not Rio. And in another timeline, Agatha would simply say something crude back, walk faster through the hall to get away from Jen, push away the thought that there might be any shred of hope for her. 

 

More evidence that something had changed in her. It felt embarrassing to be perceived in that way, all because Rio came out to her, a piece of information that changed exactly nothing about their friendship. Just because Rio liked girls, didn’t mean she liked Agatha.

 

The word ‘like’ felt empty and childish, when all of Agatha’s thoughts were consumed with Rio for the better part of their friendship, when Agatha had dreamt up any possible scenario of confessions over and over, and still bit her tongue, swallowed down any hope of it and existed in the numb of reality. 

 

It was paralyzing, she felt herself shrinking at the complicated emotion, shame, embarrassment that this new information had turned her into a giddy love struck weirdo, at least in her head, but enough that it had inspired Jennifer Kale to say something about it. 

 

If Jen saw it, did that mean Rio felt it too? 

 

Maybe it was time to direct her anger at Rio. For all the times Agatha felt her heart about to burst with longing, for all the time they’d spent together, Rio had never confessed, had never said anything in the realm of admitting romantic feelings, and maybe the only explanation for that was that Rio didn't have any for Agatha. 

 

“I didn’t mean to send you into a mental crisis,” Jen pipes up again when Agatha hasn’t said anything else, noticing the way Agatha seemed to shut down slightly, curl in on herself.

 

”Why are you being so nice to me?” And perhaps it wasn’t exactly nice, but considerate, not totally coated in the usual mocking or light-hearted insults, definitely nice by Agatha Harkness and Jennifer Kale standards. 

 

Jen looks at her like she’s crazy, wondering where Agatha’s opinions of her sat on the scale of friends to enemies. 

 

“Cause were friends”

 

”Yeah,” Agatha doesn’t know what to do with that, didn’t know Jennifer categorized them as such, didn’t know why she had put up her walls high enough to miss that, to push out any truths about people that had her back, maybe she was realizing now, “Friends”

 

”You okay?” Jen asks as they turn into their pre-calculus class room, genuine concern there. Had it been there before? Had Agatha missed it?

 

“Yeah”

 

—-

Agatha doesn’t usually subscribe to the Friday restlessness. The phenomenon of excitement for the impending weekend, trouble concentrating in class, waiting impatiently for the bell to ring. 

 

It means going home to Evanora. It means two days of studying, doom scrolling on tiktok, rotting in her bed with permission to go nowhere and do nothing. Sunday morning church is mandatory, perhaps a breath away from the static of her walls is better than nothing. It always felt like some well manicured trap, all the people her age rushing home to escape the torment of another mundane school week, a wave she let herself be swayed in from time to time. But she couldn’t make plans. 

 

There had been times where Evanora wasn’t home on a Saturday, times where she took the chance to sneak out the side door where there was no doorbell camera, pray to God that she made it home before her mother.

 

But now didn’t feel like a great time to test her luck, a count going in her head of how long she could go without a slap across the face. It swung like a pendulum sometimes, her urge to rebel swinging all the way back into this realm of only fear, where stepping out of line just didn’t feel worth it. 

 

She’s in the school library after school, an Evanora approved activity, even if 90% of the student body has already left the building giving in to the pull to get out of this place after a long week. 

 

Agatha is studying (waiting for Rio to get out of her Spanish Club meeting), tucked in a back corner chair, hidden behind bookshelves, a fleeting thought that a janitor could easily miss her back there, shut the lights, lock the door. The idea of being stuck in the library all weekend doesn’t exactly feel like the worst possible outcome. 

 

“Do I still have to whisper if we're the only two people in here?” Rio’s voice scares Agatha out of her thoughts as she strolls up to her creepily silent. 

 

“You scared the fuck out of me,” Agatha glares, her hand coming up to her chest, not hiding the rush of it from Rio. 

 

Rio looks regal, her dark hair falling so elegantly, still looking freshly styled after a full day of school, she’s wearing eyeliner that highlights the darkness of her eyes, her lips kissed with tinted chapstick. Agatha hates that as many times as she sees Rio in their school uniform, it still does things to her, the fitted blazer, the skirt. She felt like an old perv raking her eyes over her best friend, but Rio didn’t question it, never questioned it.

 

“Functions got you that on edge?” Rio jokes referencing the Math textbook sitting on the little table next to Agatha. 

 

“No, just my mother as usual,” Agatha complains shortly as she starts to pack up her books, not intending to start a whole conversation over it before she remembers-

 

“I forgot to tell you…” Agatha’s lips are moving before she fully consents to it, before she knows which way she wants to explain. 

 

Rio looks at her curious, waiting patiently. 

 

“Evanora doesn’t want me hanging out with you,” Agatha tries to push through it, give Rio little time to wonder when and why this came up with Agatha’s mother, skipping over any chances for Rio to blame herself for the fading bruises from the last attack, “So, we can’t be too obvious at church.”

 

”I can just sit with my parents if you want,” Rio offers as an immediate solution, breaking the way they’d always sat together during service, Evanora always front row, Rio’s parents casually somewhere in the middle section, Agatha and Rio tucked in any pew with space. 

 

“No,” Agatha refuses quickly, looking up at Rio after zipping closed her backpack, she can’t place the emotion in brown irises, this shaky uncertainty swirling in the unconditional care, “We’ll figure it out, but I’m still sitting with you. Lord knows the last time I made it through mass without you singing off key next to me.”

 

”I’m a natural performer and you know it,” Rio feigns offense, knowing full well the church hymns were not made for the singer to sound good. 

 

Agatha stands finally, tossing her bag over her shoulder, coming into Rio’s personal space maybe too eagerly. She’s squinting at her, a silent challenge. 

 

Rio just stares waiting for Agatha to give up on whatever fake beef she’s conjured up now, knowing that Agatha could never even stay fake mad at her for long. 

 

Rio’s eyes shift and soften, settling just below her left eye, Rio’s hand comes up without hesitation, her fingers sliding over the skin there, soft but purposeful, only a second or two it still takes Agatha’s breath away. 

 

“Eyelash” Rio explains, the single eyelash resting on the tip of her pointer finger.

 

Agatha is looking at Rio like a knight in shining armor and she is the damsel in distress, like Rio had just broken her out of her high tower.

 

And Rio has to do that stupid smirk, the one that makes her eyes squint slightly, the one that makes Agatha’s knees weak, like she sees the way Agatha is floored by her mere existence and can only toy with the fraying evidence, never coming close to changing their fate. 

 

“Make a wish,” Rio instructs like it’s sacred, pulled out of her prayer to God to be still in this moment, offer up her hand for Agatha to blow away the eyelash, search for answers from whatever cosmic energies are listening.

 

Agatha holds the eye contact as she exhales, the offending eyelash falling away from Rio’s fingertip. Caught up in the tender darkness of Rio’s eyes, close enough to feel her warmth, captured by the softness of the moment, she forgets to ask the universe for something.

 

—-

John 14:3- And if I go and prepare a place for you, I will come again and receive you to Myself; that where I am, there you may be also. 

 

Evanora is already sitting in the first row, already kneeling before mass begins, her hands tightly wound in prayer, her eyes closed.

 

In another life, the sight of it would be grounding, her mother called so securely to something bigger than herself, a path to follow, a belief system that as a child made Agatha feel less alone.

 

Now, it only felt incongruent. An image that didn’t match up with the truth of her world. Her mother, dedicated to a God who loves all his people, the same woman that had raised her hand to her for as long as she could remember.

 

Agatha still remembers when she realized it wasn’t normal, that the reprimands other children got for misbehaving were not the same, punished to a new degree where marks were always left behind, when she used it as a means of control, held Agatha to an unattainable standard.

 

Agatha hadn’t been an altar server for quite a while now, giving way to younger children when she was about 15. But she still knew them well, tried to serve as something of a mentor, a resource if any of them needed someone to speak to, perhaps things they didn’t think appropriate to tell the adults of the church.

 

It served as a good excuse to hang back, explore into the church basement to find the 3 boys and 2 girls that would assist Father Buchanan during the service. There is always a touch of nostalgia in watching them prepare, chatting idly among them, checking in. Agatha liked to believe a lot had changed in the last 2 years or so, but for the most part she still felt so stuck, entangled in this battle of understanding.

 

Faith had always felt untouchable, a pattern of knots that she could never fully untether herself from. It felt like an undoing, a world where she didn’t exist without her belief in God.

 

And maybe it was the only thing keeping her alive for a long time, a chance for salvation, a promise that as much as her mother hated her, Jesus loved her. The root of it so sunken into her past, most days she didn’t know how to walk into a future without it. Even if the truth of it didn’t serve her anymore, even if getting older had only exposed her to the darkness, the shame, the greed that lurked just behind the beaded veil. 

 

She makes her way back into the lobby, standing to the side as families pass through, smiling as best she can at faces she’s come across every Sunday for years, some greeting her with ‘hello’s and warm hugs. And perhaps it was this that kept her from completely severing ties, this feeling of community, no matter how shallow in some instances, the sharing in it, the support she never had the chance to experience elsewhere. Evanora had made church home for better or worse. 

 

Agatha spots Mrs. Vidal like Moses parting the Red Sea, the gentle confidence curling through the crowd like a wave. Agatha had always admired her assuredness, never bowing to the pressure to stew in the shame of sin, an aura that many in the church saw as disrespectful. Agatha thought it was beautiful, the way Rio’s mother was 100% herself in every room, could see the way Rio had taken after her, a refusal to be made to feel less than.

 

Mrs. Vidal pulls Agatha into a hug like it’s second nature, holding tight for maybe a second more than usual, clutching onto Agatha’s shoulders to look at her fully, as if to make sure she was truly okay.

 

”I haven’t seen you in forever, mija,” the words tumble out gracefully in lieu of asking any uncomfortable questions, never pushing Agatha to share anything she didn’t want to, “We’ve missed you.”

 

This unconditional warmth always makes Agatha want to cry, the ease with which Rio’s parents extended their care to Agatha without hesitation, the way her own mother had never come close to this level of nurturing. It made her feel pathetic, like an ounce of regard for her well being was enough to overwhelm her. 

 

“I miss you too,” Agatha tries to hold back the emotion of it, the way she didn’t just love the Vidals because they were Rio’s family, but because she actually enjoyed them as people, took the time to really know them the same way they had made an effort to really know Agatha, “I’ll try to come over for dinner this week,” she offers, knowing how much Rio’s mother loved to cook for the people she loved. 

 

Rio and her father stroll in a few moments later, probably lolly-gagging in the parking lot. 

 

Rio is in a yellow dress, her hips and torso framed elegantly, but still modest enough for church, the shape of it doing more to Agatha than any amount of showing skin. It makes her feel slightly underdressed, her brown dress pants, white shirt, and floral cardigan a few degrees simpler. 

 

Rio’s father greets her, a tight hug, a kiss to the side of her head, something gentle and paternal. 

 

“Muy bonita,” he sing-songs all smiles, turning Agatha by the hand as if spinning her in a romantic dance. In all the places Mrs. Vidal is confident and reassuring, Mr. Vidal is a jovial goofball, another clear side to Rio. Agatha can’t help the way it makes her smile, the way he can compliment her without it feeling like something she has to hide from.

 

”Papa,” Rio half-admonishes him, a playful warning that he was always being extra, especially if it meant he’d get the added consequence of annoying Rio.

 

”She needs to know she’s gorgeous, chispita” Is his grand explanation, earning a laugh from Agatha, and an eye roll from Rio. 

 

“Alright, mi corazón,” Mrs. Vidal steps in to save them, although clearly amused as well, “we should head in, before we're the last ones.” She directs, her hand on her husband's shoulder, pushing him toward the door to enter the main room of the church. 

 

“We’ll be in a second,” Rio catches Agatha’s wrist, holding her back from following them inside, offering her parents a smile.

 

They both nod, not questioning it, trusting Rio without question. 

 

—-

 

They shouldn’t have trusted Rio. 

 

Because they hadn’t followed in behind them a moment later. Or ever. 

 

Rio, instead, convincing Agatha to ditch Mass, take the short walk around the building to the old playground.

 

Rio’s on the rusted swing set, the chain creaking against the bar with every swing.

 

“I think you’re too big for that,” Agatha comments, standing to the side, admiring the way her dark hair, the skirt of her dress fluttered against the wind, noting the way Rio barely fit in the seat of it, her knees bent harshly at how close to the ground it was, these swings definitely intended for someone much smaller. 

 

“Hush, I’m living the last days of my youth,” Rio commands, a facade of annoyance that Agatha can only smile at as Rio doubles down on her attempt to make it off the ground. 

 

Agatha steps closer, grabbing one side of the chain in her hand, effectively stopping any chance of Rio gaining any momentum, looking down at her now.

 

Rio is blinking up at her, her eyelashes casting delicate shadows in the sunshine, Agatha hovering close enough to see the smooth of Rio’s skin, the wrinkles in her lips. 

 

“We’re not even old yet.”

 

”But we will be soon.” Rio says adamantly, feeling the pressure of impending change, the ripple of feeling like every little thing has world-altering consequences.

 

”Are you afraid of getting older?” Agatha asks, pressing something serious between them, Rio still looking up at her, the intricate details of her irises more prominent like this. 

 

“I think I’m just scared of everything changing,” Rio voices, honest, open.

 

Agatha scoffs, Rio’s eyes tracking the changes in her face, the delicate smile, the way her blue eyes crinkle slightly. 

 

“I think I’m scared of everything staying the same”

 

”Mmm,” is Rio’s response at first, a short sound of agreement, understanding where Agatha is coming from, “Maybe reality is somewhere in the middle, some things change, some things don’t, and we won’t have to be scared.”

 

Agatha nods looking down for a moment, not knowing where to steer them next, the air coated in vulnerability.

 

Rio’s thumb traces the edge of Agatha’s front pocket, the delicate touch almost tickling her, something electric in the way one of Rio’s hands could set her on fire without intention. Agatha pushes through the chill of it, needs to press forward. 

 

“What if,” she starts, trying to find the right way to frame it, “What if the wrong things change? What if the things I want to change stay the same?”

 

”That’s where the fear comes in,” Rio has moved into stroking against her hip, keeping her close with the soft ministrations, the curl of her thumb pressing into Agatha’s hip bone, something calm, something possessive, “We can’t predict the future.”

 

There’s something solemn in Rio’s voice, this reservation that perhaps she’d invest time and money into a Time Machine if it meant knowing if tomorrow is worth looking forward to. Maybe its the unpredictable, the unknown, the one thing that’s held Agatha back from facing her feelings for Rio for years. 

 

And here it was, starkly in her face that Rio was scared too, at least of what the world had to give them tomorrow, scared that change would be too much to handle, the loss of security, a place she would never willingly walk into. 

 

Believing in God used to make it all feel lighter, like the passage of time was dripping in His favor, the righteous path already laid out. Now it feels far away, something Agatha can’t grasp.

 

It feels like a crack in her armor, a small edge to pick at, enough room for the light to get in, claw at the folded insides that have sat dormant for so long, aching for any touch of movement. Agatha takes a breath, wishing goodbye to the shame, to the version of herself too afraid to give voice to the crushing spiral of love, to the despair of holding onto all of it for years and never being able to set it free. 

 

It’s not a surging climax, the reality that progress is not made in leaps and bounds, Agatha is ready to take a first step, even if it results in falling. She’ll deal with the consequences if it means not everything stays exactly the same, pulling at frayed wires if only to feel the charge. 

 

“Is that why you’ve never kissed me?”

 

Rio looks at her, her eyes slightly widened, the shock of it taking a moment to settle, the movement of her hand stopping, the grip on Agatha’s hip suddenly more harsh. There’s a battle in Rio’s eyes and Agatha can’t look away. A slight tremble she can’t tell if it’s stemming from her or Rio, an itching in her heart at what to do. A part of her wounded to see Rio’s overwhelm, wanting to apologize, tell her to forget she even asked. A crueler, more selfish part happy to see Rio suffer the way she has, content to watch her swim her way back to the surface on her own. 

 

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 6

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“Is that why you’ve never kissed me?”

 

Rio looks at her, her eyes slightly widened, the shock of it taking a moment to settle, the movement of her hand stopping, the grip on Agatha’s hip suddenly more harsh. There’s a battle in Rio’s eyes and Agatha can’t look away. A slight tremble she can’t tell if it’s stemming from her or Rio, an itching in her heart at what to do. A part of her wounded to see Rio’s overwhelm, wanting to apologize, tell her to forget she even asked. A crueler, more selfish part happy to see Rio suffer the way she has, content to watch her swim her way back to the surface on her own. 

 

Rio opens her mouth to speak, her breath a tilted sigh, but she closes her lips again trying to find the right words. 

 

“Do you want me to kiss you?” Are what she finally settles on after another moment of silence, the creases of each word shaky and unsure. 

 

Agatha is surprised they’re even still here, that she was able to ask such a question without instantly exploding, floored that Rio hadn’t run in the aftermath, that she was asking this of Agatha like it was a simple question, like she needed more answers. 

 

Of course, the question isn't exactly fair, leaving Agatha to press in puzzle pieces when she had asked first, done all the heavy lifting. She can feel the physical effects of it, the sweat on the back of her neck making her nauseous, the ache in her chest swirling like a flash of heart-burn.

 

“Rio,” Agatha warns, an attempt at refusal, “I’m asking you. Have you stopped… out of fear?” She’s never felt so in control, so confident to push forward through the difficulty, they had come this far, and Agatha was tired of waiting, tired of yearning for something just out of reach. 

 

Watching Rio struggle with it feels validating and sad at the same time, giving her reason to believe she hasn’t suffered alone in a pool of unreciprocated longing, but also a new realization that they had waited all this time for nothing. 

 

Still, she needed Rio to say it. 

 

Rio breaks the eye contact, removes her hand from Agatha’s hip, pushes herself off the swing to stand with a steadying breath, puts space between them.

 

And the fear surges back, Agatha wishing she had super powers to keep Rio here until she speaks all her truth, glue her to the swing set if it means understanding each other. Agatha wipes her sweaty palms on the front of her pants, sucks in her own bottom lip, prepares herself for the impending fallout. 

 

“I don’t want to hurt you,” Rio faces her again, a couple feet of space between them, but the look in her eyes is vulnerable, honest. “I don’t want to ruin us.”

 

It feels like a mirror, watching Rio fight herself, press away her desires in favor of saving them both. It’s painful, it’s liberating. She’s not sure if she’s listening to the devil or the angel on her shoulder, but she has to know the truth. 

 

”Answer the question, Rio.” Agatha is practically begging her now, her hands bunched into fists at her sides, pushing away the need to cry, trying her best to keep it together. 

 

Rio doesn’t answer with words.

 

Instead she steps forward, invading Agatha’s space.

 

She forgets how to breathe, her mind snapping into this limited existence where she can only feel Rio, her brown eyes filled with tears and determination, her lips open slightly, the warmth of her breath on Agatha’s face, her palms come to rest against Agatha’s jaw line cradling her face. And they stay there for what feels like eternity, breathing the same air, waiting for the ground to open up and swallow them whole.

 

It’s dizzying, a state of existence that had for so long felt like a dream, but now Rio was close enough to kiss, close enough to forget all the consequences.

 

Agatha’s phone chimes.

 

The specific tone assigned to a text message from the devil. 

 

“Fuck,” Agatha says, breathless.

 

Rio let’s go without another second passing. 

 

Agatha fishes her phone from her pocket in an instant, reading the message in record time. She tries her best to steady her breath in the aftermath of the proximity, tries to compartmentalize the soaring emotion she needed to push down. 

 

“Let’s go,” she demands quietly, not mean, but no room for questioning, “Evanora is asking where I am.”

 

”Okay,” Rio follows behind her without another word.

 

—-

Acts 3:19- Repent therefore, and turn back, that your sins may be blotted out. 

 

“A disgrace, Agatha. You are a disgrace to my name.” Evanora is only halfway through her tirade with no signs of stopping, certain by the way Mass isn’t even halfway over and her mother doesn’t have to worry about any eavesdropping on her ridicule for at least another 30 minutes. Her words are hushed yet crisp, her lips fitting over each syllable violently. 

 

They are outside of the church, just past the front steps as Evanora details her short-comings, how she had failed Evanora, how she had failed the Lord.

 

”Leaving church during prayer is something I will not tolerate, do you hear me?” 

 

Agatha is crying, unable to hold in the rush of tears, the whiplash of the last 10 minutes, the stress hitting her body without warning. The fact that Rio was hiding in a bush 10 feet away hearing this, only made it worse. 

 

“Stop your crying,” Evanora pushes her, just enough to throw her off balance, but not enough to leave any evidence, “You brought this on yourself.”  

 

“Yes, mother.” Agatha wipes her tears, trying to seem as normal as possible, not wanting to continue this scene out in public, not wanting to give Rio any more ammunition.

She guides them into a row towards the back, sitting next to her in an effort to keep a close eye on her, stop her from escaping once more. Evanora snaps back into her pattern of praise, listening to the gospel intently, seemingly secure again in the fact that she knew where her daughter was, rightfully extending her relationship with God.
