Rio’s jaw is set tight, her eyes downcast, a shift that only Agatha would notice. To everyone else Rio was still playing her role, the respectful daughter quietly making her way into her seat. Even here, Agatha knew the expectations were different for them.

 

Evanora was extremely devout, her role as principal of a Catholic School didn’t leave much room for anything less. And of course, those implications fell on her daughter, to never step out of line, to strive for perfection, that anything less was not good enough.

 

Rio’s parents were already sort of viewed as outsiders. Agatha wasn’t blind to the racial undertones of it all, that even if both of Rio’s parents were citizens, even if they were lawful taxpayers, the world would always villainize them, blame them for things outside of their control. And even in a house of worship, where the main teaching was loving thy neighbor, was not casting judgement, the people in these pews held bias against the churchgoers that had darker skin tones, that spoke different languages. 

 

It felt horrifying to be envious of that in some ways, like the expectation bar for them was set a little lower, the desire to be perfect cemented a little less if she knew perfection was impossible in their eyes. 

 

It just felt like another reason to run from here, flee from the ugly that sang hymns and preached of love in an effort to hide the hatred, the bigotry. 

 

She tries to focus on her breathing, push the panic away, resolve herself to find the silver linings, that Agatha saw the text and came back, that Evanora didn’t come looking, that she hadn’t found her with Rio. 

 

The words of the priest bring her back in, the story of a woman from the Gospel of Mark, how she had bled for years, her belief in Jesus ultimately healing her from simply touching his robe. 

 

“Jesus said ‘Daughter, you are well because you dared to believe. Go in peace, and stay well.”

 

Agatha had soaked herself in faith, pressed all of her mind into the hope that her belief in Him would be enough to break her from the wretched curse of her existence. And for a long time, it felt like an escape, a world she could breathe in, where everything would turn out okay if she prayed, if she was gracious, if she did as her mother told her. 

 

But now it all felt like a scam, a dream she’d woken up from. She found it admirable, the dedication of the people around her, the community it brought, the hope in the eyes of the children, a place of safety to come back to when the world felt uninhabitable. But it couldn’t be that for her anymore, couldn’t hold all the pain in these wooden walls anymore, not enough candles to be set ablaze to quiet the fire in her soul that raged to run. 

 

But she can’t run.

 

Stuck to the cold surface of the pew, quietly imploding she holds back her tears, numbing herself to reality, pushing away the sound of the priest’s voice, forgetting how close her mother is, she focuses on the back of Rio’s head, contemplates a life that isn’t all consumed by fear, by repression, by all the things expected of her and none of her actual desires. 

 

—-

 

Matthew 11:28- Come to me, all you who are weary and burdened, and I will give you rest.

 

Agatha stood inside the bathroom stall, her forehead pressed into the wall, one hand steadying her there as she took deep breaths, needing a moment to hide herself away from everyone else, seal herself in the confines of the small space to keep her from the judgement of her mother even if it meant facing the claustrophobia.

 

Mass had ended, Evanora probably speaking to as many people as she could as they made their way out of the church, wearing her usual fake smile and projecting joy in a way Agatha had never been on the receiving end of.

 

”Agatha,” her name is called, the voice splitting yet cautious. 

 

Rio.

 

The pounding in her head was too intense to find full clarity immediately, unsure if the voice was real or she’d imagined it. 

 

“Agatha, open the door,” Rio’s voice comes again, now just outside the stall door, the words much clearer now, still Agatha tilts her head to peek through the bottom opening of the stall, confirm it’s Rio’s feet planted on the other side before moving to unlock the door. 

 

The bathroom is in the church basement, not a common stop for the average church goer, most using the one adjacent to the lobby if at all. Coming here at the end of mass had been strategic, Agatha knowing that it would be rare for anyone else to be down here, but also knowing it was a place that Rio would probably go looking for her. 

 

The look in Rio’s eyes is a dark abyss, a fear Agatha has never seen planted there, the echo of what will one day be forehead wrinkles, the worry in the delicate creases of her innocent face. 

 

Agatha doesn’t give her the time to say anything, can’t give Rio the opportunity to take in her shivering form, the way her eyes were surely red, the etch of fresh tears still falling. She launches forward towards her instead, needing to feel the comfort of Rio in her arms, the solidity of her pressed into her.

 

Rio doesn’t hesitate to hug her back, Agatha’s arms wrapping around her shoulders as Rio’s latch around her waist, the searing warmth like a fire pit, the flames licking close to her skin, the pain of the crash pressing out the discomfort, giving way to relief. Agatha sighs into her neck, unashamed of the tears that continue to fall, the ragged breaths pressed against Rio’s pulse. She smells like sea salt and cedar, a coarse coating of escape, a masculine edge to the lotions Rio had always chosen, a sense of something familiar and secure. 

 

“It’s okay,” Rio tries, an attempt at convincing them both, “You’re safe,” it feels shaky and from a place of frustration and pain, but Agatha soaks it in, needing the words even if they are hushed and soggy. 

 

They stay wrapped in each other for a harsh moment, crushing bones together, heart pressed to heart. Agatha pulls away first, the hold Rio has on her feeling steady and unyielding, a position Rio would stay in for as long as Agatha needed. 

 

Rio only looks her in the eye for a moment, perhaps shaken by the broken expression Agatha wears, her face red and blotchy from her own tremendous emotions, not the evidence of her mother’s physical violence for once, just the emotional effects of her callous rage. There’s something fiercely tangled there, a choice Agatha is getting closer to making. 

 

Not yet. 

 

Rio turns around briefly, ripping off a piece of scratchy brown paper towel to hand Agatha. She takes the offensive material, wiping it under her nose, knowing the snot was probably the worst part of the liquid leaking from her face, the tears would dry without much interference. 

 

Still, Rio turns around again, grabbing more paper towel, before putting herself to work, seemingly changing her mind from whatever had stopped her from doing so originally.

 

Rio brushes any stray hairs clung to Agatha’s cheeks, strokes the tears away gently, undeterred by the girl in front of her actively blowing her nose. Rio’s expression is more delicate now, her features settling slightly, focused on clearing Agatha’s face, seemingly calmed by Agatha’s presence, the way they’d done this before, had been this close in the name of covering bruises and cuts. 

 

“I was really struggling to not beat the fuck out of her,” Rio voices, her words echoing in the tight space, a soft aura surrounding them as she wipes the last of Agatha’s tears.

 

Agatha can’t help, but scoff at the abrupt honesty, knowing Rio’s physical strength, but also the way she’d never seen Rio use it against someone maliciously, knowing that she’d only ever wield it to protect herself or the people she loves. 

 

“I’ll have to imagine you hiding in a bush the next time I’m mid spiral,” Agatha answers, trying to find some of the light Rio had pushed in, easing her way into the calm territory Rio always stirred around them, even in the wake of disaster. 

 

Agatha really looks at her, her fingers combing through the ends of her hair, playing with the strands idly, her fingers gliding over her neck, her collarbone, it felt freeing, a delicate landing strip for all the hurt, freshly painted over with a smile, an attempt at pushing through the pain. 

 

Rio had always felt like moments of escape, a fairytale land that Rio had furnished and kept clean just for the two of them, a safety net, a home. 

 

Rio’s hands were on her hips now, stroking over her belt loops, waiting patiently for whatever Agatha would push towards next. A lot of the time Agatha felt trapped in these spaces of ‘almosts’ and ‘so close’, hoping for Rio to jolt forward and finally kiss her, confess all the tragic love that sat on her tongue. 

 

Maybe it fully dawned on Agatha that she held that power too, that despite all the paralyzing fear, she could be the one to jump the bridge, steer them forward instead of always sitting in park with the engine on.

 

What a waste of fucking gas.

 

Agatha steps forward, an effort to be closer, feel Rio’s breath against her face again, but of course the brunette is taken off guard, her step falling backward as Agatha surges forward. 

 

For a moment, her heart takes the movement as rejection, letting the shift in Rio’s eyes settle into confusion rather than an attempt at pushing her away. Agatha was tired of taking a backseat in her own life, tired of letting other people steer. 

 

She pushes forward again, holding onto Rio’s shoulders, steering the woman backwards until her lower back presses into the outer edge of the sink, the sound of Rio’s pelvis hitting the porcelain louder than Agatha intended. 

 

Still, Rio grabs onto her, her arms clinging around Agatha’s mid section, as she comes to stand in Rio’s personal space, one hand wrapped around the back of Rio’s neck, her fingers tangled under her hair, fingertips pressed into her scalp, the other hand molded against her jaw, keeping them close, but not connecting their lips. 

 

Rio’s eyes are so brown, the reflection of light casting little white dots from the overhead lighting stuck into dark irises. There’s a fountain of emotion in her eyes, fear, desire, a yin and yang of all the desperate attempts at looking into the future and always coming back with empty answers. 

 

Rio’s hair and skin are so soft, a plane of exploration Agatha dreams of often, her thumb stroking over the jaw line, the way Rio seems to melt slightly at the touch, Agatha can’t imagine how intense anything else could feel if this was already overwhelming, holding Rio on the precipice of a cliff, but never crossing the caution tape. 

 

She looks down at Rio’s lips, unable to stop her eyes from shifting, hypnotized by the pink softness awaiting her, the glare a mix of saliva and chapstick. 

 

“Agatha,” comes the wrecked whisper, the sight of Rio’s tongue adding fuel to the fire.

 

Agatha tilts forward, but not to connect their lips, a traitorous thud as their foreheads press together instead. Rio breathes hot against her, both of their eyes screwing shut, bracing themselves. 

 

“I’m not gonna kiss you right now,” Agatha decides, the words brushed into the small space between their faces. 

 

Rio whines, it's quiet and barely there, and Agatha knows the sound isn’t voluntary, but it's almost enough to make her change her mind. 

 

“I don’t want the memory to be stashed right next to another installment of Hurricane Evanora,” Agatha explains, hoping to peel away any feelings of rejection Rio might be toying with. 

 

Agatha wanted Rio, and now Rio knew it. It felt like a volcano set to erupt for hundreds of years that had now laid dormant, allowing life to thrive around it. It wasn’t an explosion, instead they’d found a new island to explore, a new planet to understand. But, she could be patient a little while longer, give herself the opportunity to really choose when and where the tides would change between them. 

 

Rio nods minutely, just enough for Agatha to feel, her cue to pull away. 

 

It felt strange looking at her now, like the ease of a confession that was never explicitly spoken, but now understood. Rio seemed shaken too, pulling Agatha back for a second into a full hug, seemingly needing to hold her for another moment, make sure she was whole before stepping back. 

 

“Do you need anything?” Rio asks, the words singing for all things she doesn’t say.

 

Agatha shakes her head, soaking in the calm, relishing in the way Rio had taken her off the edge of a panic attack, sent her swirling back into her own hope.

 

Rio brushes hair out of Agatha’s face, strokes her cheek for a moment, like she really needs Agatha to hear her. 

 

“If anything happens tonight, please call me and I’ll pick you up, Mami already said you could stay the night,” Rio urges like it’s a promise, knowing Agatha had hard lines on the ways she would allow Rio to protect her, allow her to get involved to calculated extents. 

 

Agatha’s hand comes up to cover the one Rio has on her face, stroking at the back of her knuckles, wanting Rio to know just how much she felt her never-waning care. 

 

“I’ll text you,” Agatha promises, “I’ll be okay.”

 

Rio swallows, not sure if she fully agrees with the words, but she accepts it for now, pulling Agatha forward to place a delicate kiss to her hairline. 

 

“Go,” Agatha giggles at the contact, playfully pushing away from Rio’s hold, “Before someone comes looking for us.” The words are dismissive but she’s smiling at Rio, a soft glint of happiness in her eye, one step closer to really being with Rio the way she’d dreamt of for so long, the baby steps alone making her feel the butterflies erupt all over again. 

 

“The Lord is always watching,” Rio chastises like it’s a harsh truth, a sin they’d already been caught for. 

 

“Surprised you haven’t burst into flames in all of your years of perfect Sunday service attendance,” Agatha jokes, poking Rio in the ribs, knowing exactly where she’s ticklish. 

 

Rio swats at her hands. 

 

“Guess I could say the same about you,” Rio laughs, testing the territory of the new information.

 

Agatha squints her eyes at her, fake-insulted, she moves to jab at Rio’s ribs again, but is stopped easily, Rio grabbing hold of both wrists, and holding onto them securely, Agatha hates how she loses her breath at the show of strength, hates how easily Rio melts her insides. 

 

“Don’t worry, sweetheart. You wouldn’t be the first to have their queer awakening in the basement of a Catholic Church.”

 

—-

 

The car ride home is quiet. Quieter than Agatha thought it would be.

 

Evanora often held in her rage just long enough for them to be sealed inside her SUV, the pristine leather, the unused cup holders, the stark newness a safe place to berate her daughter. 

 

But, right now her mother is solely focused on the road, seemingly unmoved to spill her rage, the gospel music at a hushed volume streaming from the radio, Evanora contemplating her own thoughts more than listening. 

 

Agatha can’t complain even if she knows the words will come eventually, knows it won’t be quiet forever. She lets the anticipation curl into her stomach, holds the fear in her chest alongside the festering doom. 

 

“You are a reflection on me. You are a reflection of God.” Evanora finally speaks.

 

If Agatha wasn’t so shaken by the start of a new tirade, she would roll her eyes at the way her mother always tried to string words together like she was giving a sermon, like they were somehow meant to inspire change for the better, not overwhelm her in pain. 

 

“Yes, mother.” Agatha answers, knowing the practiced pattern, a call and answer like they’re still stuck in those pews.

 

Peace be with you.

 

and also with you. 

 

Agatha knows that Evanora needs to hear it, a clear message that she understands, that her words are landing squarely in Agatha’s brain.

 

”You understand me. Yet you go against my words. You go against His teachings.”

 

It’s a statement, not a question, no room for Agatha to defend herself. 

 

Agatha isn’t breathing, holding it in in hopes that perhaps she sinks into the seat, disappears from the world if it means she doesn’t have to find an answer to that. 

 

“I knew you were evil the day you were born,” It’s not the first time Evanora has said it, a statement she’s always deemed true out loud, perhaps the first sentence Agatha can truly remember as a child, something taught, something embedded in her reflection, an ultimate truth she can’t erase, “but I have always had hope for you Agatha. You just need to follow Him the way I’ve shown you.” 

 

It feels too akin to a pep talk, like Evanora was truly trying to be helpful. And Agatha knew that Evanora truly believed she was being helpful. The sting of it whips across her like a slap, shattering words that have her reeling just the same, the red in her cheeks, the unfocused expression. She needs to inhale, needs to find the will to push through. 

 

“Yes, mother.” it’s an echo, her lips moving on autopilot, the most basic part of her brain still intact, a rhythm of protecting herself unconsciously. 

 

It presses out some of the hope, flattens out the willingness to fight back. But a new bloom of need surges right behind it, the desire to exist without all of the solemn shaky hurt, a desire to run from this, to plant seeds in new grass, create a home without any traces of this one. 

 

Agatha keeps her face neutral, sealing away the new found faith, faith in a future that doesn’t feel as cloudy, faith in herself. She knows those are things she can’t show her mother, she knows she must protect the fragile peaks, give it time to root itself, let it fester under her skin until she’s strong enough to face her and really walk away. 

 

Agatha knows that as soon as she breathes clean air, she’ll never be able to turn back. 

 

—-

Isaiah 65:17- Behold, I will create new heavens and a new Earth. The former things will not be remembered, nor will they come to mind.

 

Agatha takes it as a win when she makes it to her room without any new emotional or physical wounds. She takes a deep breath, the reflex to thank God for that fact presses hard against her chest. But even more than that, It’s a little surprising how easily it seemed Evanora was moving on.

 

Maybe, her mother was above marking new bruises into her so soon after being in the Lord’s house. 

 

Maybe she was better off not questioning it, her brain already tracing the pattern of damage, trying to find the cause, filtering through her mother’s rationale was never an easy task. 

 

‘Made it to my room unscathed somehow…’ Agatha texts Rio as soon as she’s sat up in her bed, her head resting against the headboard, too emotionally drained to think about changing out of her church clothes just yet. 

 

’the demon is tired from cosplaying as an angel’ Rio answers a moment later.

 

Agatha rolls her eyes even if Rio can’t see it, always amused by the other girl’s refusal to refer to Evanora as anything in the realm of motherly. She’s not wrong. It used to tug in all the wrong places, reminding Agatha of the weight it held. Now it rang as validation, a voice that told her this wasn’t normal, that Rio understood.

 

’back to rotting in my bed ig’ Agatha types back without much thought, resigning herself to the impending doom scrolling, the stomach growls that would eventually pull her from the mattress, a trip downstairs to stare at the nothing in the fridge, probably resorting to crackers before the inevitable return to her bed. 

 

‘Your bed you say??? 👀’

 

The reply sort of takes Agatha off guard, a hint of jovial teasing, coated in something else, a new plane they’d never explored before. 

 

‘Is that your poor attempt at flirting ?’ Agatha types back, unable to stop the soft smile on her lips, the way the butterflies flung free in her stomach, the hollow fluttering a calming chaos. She tries her best to stop the way her brain tracks down new pathways, jumping to a universe where they exchange tasteful nudes (a blissful, unyielding thought that presses heat against her skin) and Evanora finding out before promptly disowning her (okay, Evanora does not belong anywhere near her horny thoughts, but thinking about never speaking to her mother again isn’t the worst possible outcome). 

 

‘Depends’

’am i allowed to flirt????’

 

It’s a good question, Agatha supposes, wondering where they stand in all this, figuring out what’s fair game, perhaps the new normal, exploring them post almost-kissing, post knowing there’s something there. 

 

The relief of it settles then, not this perfect moment of love confessions, but a softer transition, less pressure, less expectation. 

 

It clicked something in her heart back into place, this soft feeling that made her ache in a whole different way. 

 

Rio cared. Maybe too much. Enough to push down her own feelings if it meant giving Agatha the space to choose for them, steer them at her own pace.

 

In hindsight, Agatha wished they’d talked about it sooner, that Rio had let Agatha know she was letting her drive, waiting for her to hit the gas. It would have saved a lot of time. 

 

Still, she’s grateful the car’s moving, even if at a snail's pace. 

 

‘…tread lightly’ Agatha starts, ‘I’ll hit the breaks if I have to’

 

’soooo what are you wearing? (Flirting)’ is Rio’s response because she’s an idiot. 

 

‘Well ik ur wearing ur clown makeup’ Agatha shakes her head, amused at her own  stupidity. 

 

‘Yk i never leave the house out of uniform 🫡’

 

God, Rio is such a dork. 

 

She’s definitely not swooning over it. 

 

‘Btw i didnt have my gay awakening in a church basement’ Agatha starts at something new, finding herself steering them more easily. 

 

‘English class? Sister Hart gets you goin too?’

 

Agatha snorts, she should have expected this shit from Rio by now. She hates how easy this feels, how the smile on her face feels permanent, the press of it etched into her long term memories, she wants to savor every minute. 

 

‘I was trying to be serious 🥺’

 

’my bad. The first time you’ve ever been serious’

’tell me shawty, what enlightened you?’

 

God, she’s going to throw Rio’s phone out of her moving vehicle tomorrow morning, she can’t handle this, the way her hands ache to murder her for being such an insufferable dumbass (the way her hands ache to feel the soft of her skin, press kisses into any where she’s allowed, explore all the freedoms Rio is willing to give).

 

‘Ehhh probably the telephone music video…the sexual tension was crazy’ Agatha answers, not entirely sure when the gay realization hit, just knowing that Lady Gaga wrapped in caution tape had been an earlier memory of feeling hot over women and then feeling shame about it. 

 

‘Can I be Beyoncé in this scenario?’ 

 

‘You just want a honey bun 😡’ Agatha jokes, even if she knows Rio would probably be easily swayed by the fact that Beyoncé eats a Honey Bun in the music video and Rio has been known to be motivated by sugar. 

 

‘Just tryna eat ur honey bun 😝’ Rio answers because she’s absolutely unhinged. 

 

Agatha swallows, would never admit the way it made her imagine Rio in places she never allowed her mind to explore, would take years of torture to get her to confess that Rio’s joke had gotten her head spinning. 

 

‘Alright…ur officially in time out’

Chapter 7

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Hebrews 11:1- Now faith is the assurance of things hoped for, the conviction of things not seen.

 

”Agatha”, she hears her mother call her name from downstairs, but the tone of it isn’t as darkly commanding, “Dinner’s ready”

 

Dinner? 

 

It wasn’t like it never happened, Evanora making dinner, but it was usually reserved for Wednesday’s and their standard ritual of sharing one meal a week, keeping Agatha from completely forgetting the talons she existed under. 

 

Agatha tried to push down the feeling that this was a trap, wanting to believe that the light feel of her mother’s voice wasn’t another clever veil, an extended olive branch she’d use the thorns of later.

 

Instead, she moves her feet, knowing that the consequences were inevitable and refusing her mother’s requests only ever made the punishments worse. 

 

It’s meatloaf, not exactly Agatha’s favorite, but it didn’t look like poison, and Agatha could fuck up some mashed potatoes even if they were instant from a box. She finds it hard to complain as she sits in her designated seat, just left of her mother who always sat at the head of the table, a throne to symbolize her power. This was at least more substantial than crackers, maybe her stomach wouldn’t growl as hard as usual tomorrow.

 

Agatha knows better than to dive right in, leading them in prayer before every shared meal since she could speak. She looks at Evanora to make sure she’s ready before clasping her hands together, closing her eyes, bowing her head. 

 

“Dear Heavenly Father, We thank you for this nourishment and for the hands that prepared it. May this food give us the strength to serve You well. In Jesus’ name we pray. Amen.” Agatha’s voice is even, something so certain in the words, a practiced lullaby that had brought her comfort for a long time. It feels stale on her tongue, a whisper of denial, a breath that gives her the room to wonder why she so often went without food.

 

“Amen”, always comes Evanora’s soft echo. Agatha looks to her again, a gentle smile on Evanora’s lips, the only time it’s ever directed at her daughter, a completion of their ritual.  

 

Agatha always picks up her fork with a pit in her stomach. A conflict in the way she desperately wants to cling to that second of maternal affection casted over her, but knowing in her bones that this is not love, this is something twisted and evil, a droplet of love enough to keep her from wilting into nothing, keeping her misted enough to stay alive, but never grow. 

 

She let’s Evanora take a bite first, always. A small gesture that makes her feel less likely to die at the hands of antifreeze or arsenic mixed into green beans. 

 

And she hates that she has to think like that, hates that the motives of a home cooked meal have to come into question. It felt like a carrot dangling within her reach, a reward for good behavior when Agatha had done nothing but embarrass her, enrage her. She wrestles with the perplexity of it, Evanora treating her kindly after she’d been caught skipping Sunday service. It doesn’t make any sense. 

 

It hits her the hardest in these quiet moments that this is not normal. It’s easier to disassociate when the physical abuse is actively happening, easier to pretend this isn’t reality when the bruises are healing and Evanora is far away. But, now they’re close, pretending this is what they do, have cozy dinners, are pleasant to each other when no one else is around, that Evanora does anything without a scheme brewing. 

 

“I was thinking I’d give you my credit card.” Evanora states like it doesn’t warrant any follow up questions.

 

Agatha half-stunned by the words, waits for an explanation without asking. 

 

“I figured you might want to go to the mall and start looking for a prom dress.”

 

Agatha almost chokes on her mashed potatoes.

 

”I thought I wasn’t allow-“ Agatha starts tentatively, recounting their past conversations about how school dances were for ‘sluts’ and how Evanora would get rid of them entirely if it wouldn’t cause ‘student outrage’.

 

“I’ve decided you need a little more freedom.” Her mother cuts her off, but it doesn’t ring in her ears harshly, the words finding a home on a plane of understanding.

 

Agatha’s confused. 

 

Is Evanora trying?

 

It’s a trap. It must be a trap.

 

Evanora must see the hesitation there. She continues.

 

”You’re getting older, dear.” The term of endearment feels foreign, but Agatha can’t think too much about it before she keeps explaining, her voice vulnerable, but solid, “Soon, you’ll be looking for a husband, settling down, starting a family. Perhaps, I haven’t given you the room to grow into that role.”

 

Agatha’s still confused. She knows the expectation, a path to her future that has been drilled into her since the womb. The people to love and cherish a short list of God, her husband, and her children. In that order. But, she’s not sure what a prom dress has to do with this. 

 

“Prom is going to prepare me to be a wife?” Agatha speaks slowly, no contempt in her voice, knowing speaking out of turn has resulted in hair brushes whacked into  the back of the head, pinches to her arms. She truly wants to understand.

 

”No,” Evanora is looking down at her plate again, not giving Agatha the eye contact she wants, a play she isn’t ready to show, “Not exactly.”

 

”But, the event is hosted with St. Vincent’s, as you know,” Evanora continues, mentioning the all-boys Catholic school they planned all co-ed festivities with, “It will give you the opportunity to socialize and get some understanding of how to orient yourself.”

 

”Okay.” Agatha agrees, mostly because she’s unsure how else to respond. But she tries not to seem too eager, still holding fear that this was a carefully planned trap, an episode of Punk’d except there were no cameras, just the pitiful sting of her mother’s hands on her.

 

”Very good.” Evanora nods her approval, seemingly done with the conversation.

 

Agatha doesn’t know what to feel. She’s honestly confused Evanora seems so willing to give her away, not for any misplaced notion that Evanora wanted her around, but because she didn't know if her mother could fully relinquish control. She’d always thought her husband would be hand picked, someone just as cruel, or at the very least blind enough to let her mother continue to exist as a dictator, keep her tightly wound in her bloodied ribbon. 

 

But, Evanora was encouraging her to fraternize? Get comfy with boys? at a party? 

 

Okay, a chaperoned, no-alcohol-allowed school event, but a party nonetheless.

 

When Evanora hands over her credit card after dinner, Agatha’s still edging on the side of caution. Her mother marks the exchange with a single word.

 

”Modesty” A warning.

 

And maybe that’s the crux of it. A test. A test to see if Agatha can pick out a dress that doesn’t discount her mother’s devotion to God, to see if Agatha can follow directions. 

 

It still feels like a set up. A prank. A joke. A dream. Anything other than reality.

 

But with it comes a searing curdle of something else, a bubble in her stomach that runs along the highway of her nerves. 

 

This warmth at her mother being…nice.

 

And after all the harm, Agatha wishes it took more than a single meal without an insult to make her feel something, but Evanora had set the bar extremely low.

 

She tries to swallow down the quiet string of hope, that there was something human and redeemable inside her mother, that perhaps she could change even if molecule by molecule into something less demon-shaped.

 

It felt like plucking one hair at a time, the pinch of pain releasing into a dull itch. The pain of the thick pill to swallow, less harrowing than the headache she takes it for. 

 

—-

Ephesians 4:22-24 - You were taught, with regard to your former way of life, to put off your old self, which is being corrupted by its deceitful desires; to be made new in the attitude of your minds; and to put on the new self, created to be like God in true righteousness and holiness. 

 

“I just think it’s weird,” Rio laments, trying to air on the side of caution without striking down all the hope in Agatha’s expression, “She has to have some other motive.”

 

They’re in the hallway in between classes, Agatha rummaging through her locker trying to find her History textbook buried under loose worksheets and unused binders. Keeping her locker organized would be a lot easier if she hadn’t allowed Rio to use it, the assortment of candy wrappers amongst the chaos definitely from the taller girl.

 

Agatha huffs, finally finding the book wedged into the bottom, standing up straight again to close her locker, doing her best to find the words to explain.

 

”Maybe I’m stupid for it, but a part of me wants to believe she’s turning a new leaf.” Agatha shrugs, finally meeting Rio’s eyes.

 

They’d been talking about Evanora all day in small moments, in Rio’s car this morning, a note passed during English class, walking through hallways in between class, a conversation they kept coming back to.

 

It seemed like they were both trying to grapple with it, puzzle out exactly why Agatha’s mother, who had been hellbent on traumatizing her for the past almost 18 years, was suddenly acting …understanding? Cool? Like she cared?

 

And the worst part was that it had an unclear direction, stood in common ground enough that it wasn’t automatically a definite ploy. Because Evanora wanting Agatha to get married and have kids had always been part of the calculated plan God had laid out for her, but the direct encouragement towards it was new. The way she’d been calm and undemanding about it was new too. 

 

”If the new leaf is finding you a husband, I guess that’s not the biggest leap,” Rio scoffs through her own reasoning, “Like that part makes sense.”

 

”It’s strange,” Agatha ponders as they walk away from her locker, the fullness of the hallway effectively shielding their conversation from pesky eavesdropping, the blend of voices hard to untangle from each other, “She’s still giving me bare minimum, less than bare minimum,” she corrects herself. 

 

“It’s still different than usual, you said she was actually kind of nice?” 

 

“She looked at me like I wasn’t the ugliest thing she’s ever seen,” Agatha laughs like it’s funny, not an insecurity her mother had clawed into her identity.

 

”Calling you ugly is crazy,” Rio chirps like it’s second nature, like this wasn’t still so new, the clarity that there were feelings between them, a journey they still had yet to explore… life, Evanora, getting in the way. “That demon needs her eyes checked.”

 

”Alright, simp.” Agatha tries to hide the slight blush that coats her cheeks, “My knight in shining armor isn’t on the clock right now.”

 

”First of all, I’d look great in armor.” Rio turns to her, raising an eyebrow, daring Agatha to disagree, she doesn’t. “Secondly, I’m a proud simp, so you’re not insulting me. And thirdly, I better be getting paid for this”.

 

Agatha rolls her eyes playfully, letting the cheesy stupidity of it settle against her chest.

 

The simplicity of it felt almost nauseating, the slow pedaling of Rio’s attempts at flirting shifted seamlessly into their existing friendship. Like a testament to all the time they’d spent holding back, the way Agatha wouldn’t allow the pipe to burst now, giving time for the faucet to leak slowly for a while, offer them a chance to find their sea legs before blasting them with the entire ocean.

 

It felt like a welcome trickle, just enough to quench her thirst, breathe through the moments of astonishment that Rio was really looking at her like that, saying these things to her, meaning them. It felt like another universe, an existence where happiness didn’t have to feel like somewhere she’d never reach, where joy could effortlessly be sewn into the spaces they got to create together. 

 

“So, what’s the move, simp?” Agatha reigns back the butterflies in her stomach, breathes in for the sake of steadying her thoughts, willing herself to stay patient, build the bricks of their relationship with care. Now that she knew of feelings, it changed nothing about the way she refused to let it ruin them, their connection would always be something to be cherished, and if doing this right meant pushing through the desire to push Rio into the lockers in front of everyone and kiss her like their lives depended on it, she’d settle for knocking their shoulders together for now. 

 

“I guess we find you a prom dress.”

 

Agatha sighs. Dejected. Wondering if she’d ever have clarity on her mother’s chess moves, wondering where truth and manipulation intersected. 

 

“You have something to wear yet?” Agatha asks, purposely trying to sway the subject a little, tired of trying to understand Evanora’s potential scheme. 

 

“No,” Rio sighs, “I was thinking a suit at first, but I think a nun might faint at the sight and I don’t want to be liable for any holy deaths.”

 

”So, no suit,” Agatha chimes in, almost cementing it, but also inserting it to air it out once more, loving the idea of a fitted tux on Rio, the thought of pulling her closer by her suspenders, the clean silhouette of her shoulders and hips. Agatha shook her head, pressing away the thoughts, coating herself in the sympathy that Rio didn’t have the full freedom to express the dichotomy of her masculine and feminine sides in their very strict Catholic school.

 

“I’m not that bummed,” Rio seems to read Agatha’s mind, “I wear a tie to school like everyday,” her hand comes up, subconsciously tugging at the knot of it at the front of her throat.

 

”A dress will be nice too.” Agatha says, an attempt at a compliment, still piecing together exactly how forward she wanted to be, not sure what she was willing to confess out loud, afraid of what her words might indirectly confess. Maybe Rio didn’t need to know the exact parameters of her intense yearning just yet.

 

Here, Agatha was, stuck in her own insecurity, walking a tightrope of too much or too little, when Rio had just been adamant about being a ‘proud simp’. 

 

Just give her time. She’s figuring it out. 

 

“Do you think it’s less fucked up if a nun faints from me in a dress?” Rio asks, her eyes actually curious. 

 

“How much skin are we trying to show?” Agatha laughs as they finally make it to their classroom, finding their usual seats towards the middle, the cover of the first few rows a safe place for Rio to doodle all class long and for Agatha to pretend to pay attention. 

 

“How much is faint worthy?” Rio asks with a smirk, and Agatha’s glad they’re sitting down, her brain tracing over every instance that she’s thought about Rio’s soft skin, all the places she’d only dreamt of touching. 

 

Agatha blushes, doesn’t try to hide it, revels in the way Rio smiles at her, the way it reaches her eyes. 

 

The classroom starts filling up, an indication that this conversation was coming to an end for now, a sign they were never good at following.

 

“At this school, a dry elbow would be scandalous,” Agatha whispers, moving forward with a safe answer.

 

Rio gasps, fake-offended.

 

”You think I don’t moisturize? I’m not a monster.” Rio is whisper yelling, and Agatha hates how endearing she is.

 

”Shut up,” Agatha laughs at her, “Class is starting.” She throws her pencil the short distance between them, hitting Rio in the chin.

 

”Dude, you could have taken my eye out,” Rio says, her voice taking on a more serious tone, still quiet but more of a grumble than a whisper. 

 

“Shhhhhhh,” comes the shrill sound from a few desks over as Sister Edith enters the room. 

 

Agatha lifts her head, tearing her eyes away from Rio and the adorable mark of graphite now adorning her face, just above her left laugh line. She finds Wanda looking towards them, mostly at Rio as she was the last of them to make noise, her eyebrows raised as if questioning them, wondering where they found the audacity to speak to each other in a class that hadn't even started.

 

And Agatha wishes she could say that Wanda might be joking, but she knew the girl was completely serious, borderline offended that her and Rio weren’t experts at falling in line with the rest of the class. 

 

Rio makes a funny face at Wanda, crossing her eyes and sticking out her tongue. 

 

Wanda huffs, still clearly annoyed, disgusted by Rio’s lack of seriousness, a point of contention that had long existed between them as classmates, less intense than enemies, but never clicking as anything close to friends.

 

Rio had even come to Wanda’s defense in the past, when Agatha’s anger ran too hot, saving them all the headache of making something into a fight that was never serious enough to get that far.

 

But in all the ways Rio was free spirited, Wanda was tightly wound. 

 

Either way, it gets Wanda to look away, face forward at her desk, dissolve back into the mechanics of obedient woman of God, diligent student. 

 

As Sister Edith starts her opening remarks, Agatha finds herself doing the doodling for once, tearing off the corner of her loose leaf before drawing her best rendition of a clown, big round nose, wide smile and Wanda’s name written below it, perhaps some of her best work.

 

She folds it, sliding it to Rio while the teacher’s writing on the board. 

 

The ease of Rio’s smile feels like a blooming flower, a patch of mended clothing, a warmth of hot chocolate in her brown eyes that surges Agatha’s heart at the fact that she’d brought it out, she’d bow if given a stage to gloat. 

 

Rio rips up the small bit of paper without any hesitance, effectively silencing Agatha’s masterpiece. Agatha can’t help the way her own face morphs, her eyes widen, surprised by the action.

 

But, brown eyes find her again, an air of amusement mixed with something else.

 

’ur such a bully’ a new slip of paper says, balled up and tossed to Agatha.

 

Agatha rolls her eyes, because Rio was too nice, a reminder of all the sappy good in her heart, pushing Agatha to do the right thing, be a better person, even if no one else was watching. It was infuriating. It was charming. 

 

She flattens the paper before starting a new doodle. Another clown, an even bigger smile. Rio’s name scrawled underneath, a firm arrow pointing from her name to the image so that no mistaken identity could take place. 

 

Rio has to visibly hold in her laugh, shaking her head at the paper. 

 

It sort of felt like Agatha’s own version of flirting, a twisted expression of care, trying to give Rio the joy she effortlessly carried for everyone else. Agatha wanted to be that safety net for her too, show her that she could be good enough. She’d spend forever trying to prove that to herself. 

 

Like they were kids on a playground and Agatha was pushing Rio into the mud because she couldn’t express her big feelings any other way. She at least hoped it landed that way for Rio. 

 

‘lucky ur pretty’ the note says when it comes back to Agatha. Rio smiles goofily as she stares toward the front of the classroom, not giving Agatha the satisfaction of finding her eyes. 

 

It’s then that Agatha wishes the chunk of paper had more room, wishes that she had walls to fill with all the bewitching fortune she’s thought about her best friend, paint murals with all the flawless beauty she saw in Rio, paint the night sky with stars that burst alongside the pulse of her heart, fill word documents with clumsy poems, describe the brown of Rio’s eyes, the mysterious glint of emotion that Agatha was always trying to capture, take up clotheslines with pinned Polaroids of her smile, the one she pulls out in true laughter, not the one she’d practiced for school pictures. 

 

It’s scary. Trying to stir away the desire to claim it all out loud at once, the spill of emotions that have been building for years. She’s not sure if she’s ready for the damn to break, the routine of holding back stamped into every interaction even with the permission to push past the old limits. 

 

She toys with all the possibilities, hunting in her mind for the perfect thing to to write, the one word or phrase that will tell Rio what she needs to tell her, something true, something grounding yet clear. Anything. Anything to tell her of all the comfort she tracks into Agatha’s tragic world, the angel that steers her thoughts back to Rio when she’s drowning in pain, the beauty she sees on the surface and underneath that she wields so easily. 

 

Something to say, ‘I like you’ in the way Rio had with all her flirty quips, without it feeling extremely juvenile, a far cry from the weight she was putting on this. 

 

Agatha crumples the paper back into a ball, lets it sit on the edge of her desk, pushes away the desire for now. She doesn’t look at Rio, can’t explain it to her right now, can’t stomach the retreat. 

 

—-

 

“So, I don’t think I know how to flirt.” Agatha blurts as soon as they’re settled into Rio’s car, not enough time to buckle up or plug her phone into the aux. 

 

“What are you talking about?” Rio sort of scoffs, a mixture of amused and confused, wondering why the sudden confession had felt necessary. 

 

“I just, I don’t know, it seems so easy for you, and I don’t know how to like say…that stuff,” Agatha feels overwhelmed by how much she feels for Rio, how long she’s tucked it all into a safe and threw away the key. Now that Rio was opening that door without fear, it felt like a day she had never prepared for. The words feel flimsy as they leave her mouth, trying to be vulnerable, trying to be honest for the sake of this ever working. She knows she wouldn’t have even brought it up in front of anyone that wasn’t Rio, this safety something specific to them. 

 

“That you like me?” Rio’s smug, because of course. Rio knows exactly how to meet Agatha’s openness, never making her feel uncomfortable, opting to tease her rather than pity her, never drawing attention to the way this version of Agatha was hard to encounter. 

 

“Rio” Agatha warns her, staring at her like this isn’t their usual dance, like she isn’t grateful for the way they seem to always understand exactly what the other needs. 

 

“So you’re telling me when you drew me as a clown earlier, that wasn’t flirting?” Rio asks, somewhat serious, the edge of it still light. 

 

“It was. I just- that’s different than saying the actual words.”

 

Rio is momentarily distracted, finally putting the car in reverse and driving them out of the parking lot. Agatha takes the moment to recollect herself, try to gather the words she wants to say. 

 

“I think your flirting is fine,” Rio comments, hoping it quells the insecurity, not trying to make a big deal out of it.

 

”Fine? Just fine? I’m trying to wow you here,” Agatha jokes, letting the big feelings leak out a little, under the mask of making fun of herself. 

 

Rio giggles, offering her a side glance, focused on the road. 

 

“Okay, for real though,” Agatha puts them back on task, not ready to let the conversation go, “How do you flirt?”

 

Rio shrugs, searching her brain for the answer, seemingly dedicating actual thought to the question.

 

”I don’t think about how I flirt, it kinda comes naturally, maybe it’s the way my parents are with each other”

 

”I really don’t want to think about your parents right now,” Agatha gripes, a little grossed out at the thought of the Vidal’s getting freaky. Rio only laughs at her response, almost like she knew the thoughts it would conjure up.

 

”I mean they had to have sex at least once for me to exist,” Rio offers factually, not disturbed by it, very comfortable with how in love her parents always were, the differences of their childhoods coming to the forefront. Maybe familial affection wouldn’t seem so weird to Agatha if she’d experienced it in any sense. 

 

”I love your parents, but please never say those words again,” Agatha grimaces, thinking she’s at least successfully gotten them off of that topic. 

 

“You’re flirting with me right now,” Rio comments like it’s nothing. 

 

“I’m telling you how I don’t want to hear about your mother and father fucking, how is that flirting?” 

 

“First of all, they don’t fuck. They make love.” Rio voices, only half a joke, enough to make Agatha roll her eyes, and jump in before she can continue.

 

”If you weren’t driving right now, I’d punch you.” Agatha warns her. 

 

“See! There you are flirting again.”

 

Rio stops at a red light, finally giving them time to look at each other for more than a fleeting second. 

 

“Stop messing with me,” Agatha lifts her hand, flicking Rio in the arm as punishment.

 

”I’m not messing with you,” Rio promises, grabbing onto Agatha’s extended hand before it can fully retreat back to her side of the car, she takes it gently, pulling it up to her mouth, pressing a delicate kiss to Agatha’s knuckles as the light turns green and she puts her foot back on the gas.

 

Agatha swoons, her heart collapsing in on itself, the instant warmth of the action buzzing through her. Rio, this perfect motherfucker, and her super powers tugging away all the cold fear, curse this woman and her unyielding calm, the firm paintbrush coating Agatha in tranquility, in certainty, in love. 

 

“Please explain” is all she can conjure as a response, her brain unable to find logic with her hand being held like she deserves to be cradled and protected. 

 

Rio interlaces their fingers, cautiously thinking the way she often does before saying something she truly means, the musings that Agatha had always found meaningful and profound. She does her best to focus on anticipating the words and not how hot Rio looks steering with one hand, the flex of her forearm, as her other hand stays occupied holding onto hers.

 

”You pretending to be annoyed with me, or threatening to hit me, maybe to someone else, it’s just you being violent. But I know how you communicate, I know if you truly didn’t care, you wouldn’t even respond. You wouldn’t give me the energy if it didn’t matter to you.”

 

”You think I’m pretending to be annoyed with you?” Agatha answers, calling her logic into question instead of being serious, pushing away the sharp jolt of tenderness that comes as a result of Rio’s words, the way Rio had understood her, saw her for all the ways she was different and sought to love those parts of her just as fiercely. 

 

Rio smiles, knowing the words landed when Agatha squeezes her hand, even if the other girl can’t verbalize what they mean to her.

 

”You can never be serious,” Rio laughs, not mad at it, more of an observation.

 

”Sorry, sorry, I’ll be serious” 

 

“Do I actually annoy you?” Rio asks as she turns the corner onto Agatha’s block.

 

“Sometimes,” Agatha answers honestly, causing Rio to gasp theatrically before she can even get an explanation out, “but only when you’re being adorable or being really protective and I get annoyed because it makes me freak out cause I like you so much.”

 

Rio smiles bright at that, the glint in her eye, the little gap in her teeth shown without hesitation, it all flies back towards Agatha like a slingshot, the joy of it plastered on them both. 

 

”Agatha Harkness! Was that a flirting attempt?” 

 

“Oh my god! Shut up!” Agatha blushes, pulling her hand out of Rio’s grip to cover her face, wondering when she had jumped from repressed crush to absolute bumbling mess from her own words about Rio. 

 

“Oh, now I’m never shutting up. Who else is going to annoy you by being too adorable?” Rio teases as she puts the car in park a few houses down from Agatha’s. 

 

“You’re the worst.” Agatha peaks out from her hands, not fully pulling them away from her face yet. 

 

“I don’t think you believe that.” 

 

Agatha groans, replanting her hands over her face as Rio fully turns to her in her seat, hoping the sad scratched leather decides to open up and swallow her whole. One day of flirting and she was already crumbling. Pathetic. 

 

“Lemme see your pretty face.” Rio mumbles, pulling Agatha’s hands away, holding onto both hands, she lets them settle into this new territory where they’re deciding how they fit together without the strict boundaries.

 

One of Agatha’s hands grazes up her forearm, finds a home in tracing the inner side of her her elbow, exploring soft skin under fingertips, memorizing the birthmark there, but also knowing its a place she’ll have time to revisit, safety in the way time never felt limited with Rio. The calm in quiet that fills the space of the car, Rio never starting her playlist after Agatha’s impromptu conversation. 

 

Agatha looks up from where her hand has landed after a few moments, finally finding the courage to face this reality, giving herself the chance to breathe in the truth of it, learn how to exist here. She finds Rio’s eyes, the delicate brown meeting her with this kind patience, the open heart Rio held up for her without a second thought. 

 

“I like how you flirt,” Rio breaks the silence, it's firm but quiet, Agatha knows she isn’t joking, “keeps me on my toes.”

 

Agatha nods, a gentle smile returning to her face, letting the words soak through the jagged exterior, letting it feel true. 

 

“And the threat of violence is kinda hot.” Rio adds.

 

Agatha swats at her instantly, tapping against the forearm she’d just been rubbing against soothingly.

 

”See! Exactly! You get it!” Rio answers, fueled by the way Agatha fell right into her trap, proving her point. 

 

She just shakes her head, but still smiles, feeling at ease in all the change, the slow pace of it lulling her like the sway of a hammock.

 

She thinks of cuddling Rio fully, being close enough to hold her, tangle their limbs without overthinking anything, settling in the warmth of her, sleeping next to her, finding her dreams as more than an escape, waking up without being disappointed with reality. For once, Agatha finds comfort in all the things they have yet to explore, all the new mountains they’ll get to climb, a part of her can’t wait, but she tries to quiet that raging desire, savoring each breath. 

 

Rio takes her other hand, playing with her fingers, allowing Agatha to breeze through the journey of her thoughts, never rushing her to speak. 

 

Agatha looks up at her again, emboldened to push them forward even if only an inch.

 

She moves forward, her hand coming up to the side of Rio’s neck, wanting them both to know her intentions before stepping over a new line she wasn’t ready to cross, angling her enough to press a kiss into her cheek, linger in the closeness, seal it somewhere in the truth that she wanted this, wanted Rio to know that she wanted this. 

Chapter End Notes

Sorry it’s been a hot minute since last chapter..i think this one took me a while to wrap my head around because I felt like I was pushing on the hard stuff so intensely and I don’t want that to be the whole narrative…Rio is sort of the happy moments between Agatha’s roughest moments and I want to give that time to exist on it’s own too…that being said I think I’ve found the refocus and really evaluated how I want the plot to progress…I’ve found myself really caring about this story and how these characters end up and it means so much to me that other people seem to care about it too.

Hope you enjoyed this lighter chapter and maybe a little bit of a breather from Evanora being super evil…but brace yourself for future chapters lol

As always any feedback means so much to be so thank you for all your comments

Chapter 8

Chapter Notes

This chapter was buried deep in the recesses of my mind and I liberated her from the abyss via typing furiously with no plan at 3 am over the course of two nights…but I kind of love this chapter as rough as it felt to write (kind of like I was being possessed by a higher power (the lord using me as a vessel to write lesbian angst is crazy but not impossible))

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Jeremiah 29:11- ‘For I know the plans I have for you,’ declares the Lord. ‘Plans to prosper you and not to harm you, plans to give you hope and a future’. 

 

“This has to be considered cruel and unusual punishment,” Alice laughs as Agatha grumbles towards the ground even if she didn’t mean it as a joke. 

 

“Rio seems to be having fun,” Alice comments, nodding a few feet in front of them to direct Agatha’s attention towards her, like reminding her of the girl’s presence changes the current task, as if Agatha hadn’t been chancing a pattern of glances towards the brunette every few seconds, something grounding about having the other girl in her line of sight. 

 

They’re doing their monthly community service, a school requirement for St. Elizabeth students, a planned event that can range from handing out fliers with Jesus hanging from the cross on them (blood and guts printed in full color) to picking up trash from the side of the highway. Maybe the current predicament wasn’t the worst possible option, but working in a community garden wasn’t exactly Agatha’s definition of fun. 

 

Alice and Agatha were relegated to the job of pulling weeds, even given the proper tool (and an enthusiastic demonstration from Rio), Agatha didn’t have the patience or upper-body strength to complete the task without complaining the entire way through. 

 

“Yeah,” Agatha answers, looking up towards Rio as if she hadn’t been tracking her through the crowd of classmates the entire time they were here, “Cuz she’s a nerd.”

 

”I didn’t realize she was so into gardening,” Alice muses, not meeting Agatha’s snark, as she holds open the industrial sized trash bag for Agatha to drop another clump of weeds into.

 

In another time, Agatha might have been jealous of the way Alice seemed to be invested in Rio specifically right now, but the last week or so of clarity had cleared some of that charged delusion. Alice and Jen were their friends. Or at least they were friendly. She knew Alice well enough to read it as well-intentioned curiosity, not some violent ploy that she needed to read into. 

 

Not to mention, Rio played the role of garden fairy a little too well. More than Rio being a natural leader, she simply adapted to different roles easily. It reminded Agatha of how they swam around each other, the push and the pull, Rio always being the support in places Agatha couldn’t hold herself up, but also giving her the freedom to pedal her own bike. Agatha had not been given the power to see into the future, but she could feel in her bones that Rio would do something big, would dream far past anything Agatha had the ambition for and make those dreams reality. 

 

It was evident in the way she held herself now, the way their classmates seemed magnetized to her instruction, asking her for clarification on how much to water different plants, if they were digging deep enough into the soil, the way she guided gently, but firmly, the kindness in allowing others to learn through trial and error. 

 

Rio and Jen were planting hydrangeas, a pattern of bushes along the edge of a bed of soil, she made it look simple, something therapeutic in the way the dirt ran through her hands, found home underneath her fingernails. 

 

“She really likes plants, I’m pretty sure Earth day is her favorite holiday,” Agatha answers, amused by her own revelation. 

 

Alice smiles softly, thinking to herself for a moment, looking like she has something to say, but not knowing how to say it. Agatha sort of holds her breath for a second, an anxious thought of hoping Alice keeps her mouth shut.

 

”You two are cute together.” It isn’t a question, something certain in the way Alice offers her the words without room for argument, like Alice means them in whatever capacity it might hold. 

 

Agatha’s face scrunches, but maybe more out of surprise than confusion, she feels the wrinkle in her nose before she can stop it (a facial expression that made Rio’s eyes soften everytime it came out involuntarily). She doesn’t know exactly how to process it, how to let it be true, how to handle the reality that whatever is between her and Rio is tangible, something Alice can grasp without the confirmation of words, even if Alice is just talking about friendship, it’s still an energy that radiates, a sharp taste of something she can’t name. 

 

“You don’t have to say anything,” Alice qualifies her own statement, willing the possible worry out of Agatha before she can cement it out loud. Something a friend would do.

Amen.

Revelations 21:4- He will wipe every tear from their eyes. There will be no more death’ or mourning or crying or pain, for the old order of things has passed away.

Agatha allows her feet to carry her forward, a sense of auto-pilot, her brain carrying her towards safety without coherent thought. She finds the nearest bathroom, not the same one that got her into this mess, but the same stale odor of cleaning fluid, the same pattern of stalls and sinks. 

 

She’s not surprised by her own appearance, the mix of sweat and tears causing her hair to stick around her neck and against her cheeks, the biting red blob roughly the size of Evanora’s palm on the left side of her face, the way her eyes look far away, an absence of spark. 

 

Little spark. Mi chispita. Rio. 

 

Agatha reaches into her bag for her phone, hovers over their text thread, before locking it, dropping it back in. She couldn’t bring herself to text Rio, rip her out of class, she didn’t know how to explain, how she could drop the shriveled burden onto Rio when she could barely register it herself.

 

She knew. Fuck. Evanora knew about them. Wanda had told her. That fucking bitch ran to the principal without hesitation to out the resident sinners. Of course. 

 

Maybe that’s why her earlier apology was only aimed at Rio, Wanda couldn't even look her in the eye, couldn’t confront the damage she was about to cause. Still, the impact was immediate, the hurried volcano torching over the life Agatha was trying to rebuild. 

 

She splashes her face with water, trying to breathe, fixing her hair into some semblance of normalcy, she pulls at the knots forming in the back of her head from the way she’d been thrust against the chair. 

 

She checks her phone again for the time. 

 

Twenty more minutes of pre-calculus. 

 

Agatha wasn’t going back to that classroom right now, couldn’t handle the guarded perception, would rather her classmates assume that she earned the privilege as a nepo baby to miss out on a full lesson of calculator functions. 

 

After that was Spanish. A class Rio forced her to keep taking with her for the past 2 years that it was no longer a requirement. Agatha allowed it, would never admit to the way Rio speaking Spanish to her made her melt a little, or that she enjoyed it to a point, liked being able to understand most of the Vidal’s jokes without waiting for an explanation. 

 

Another class she wasn’t sure she’d be attending. Rio would question her absence, but she wasn’t sure she could face her yet.

 

Fuck. She needs to get out of this bathroom. Stop tripping over her own thoughts, find somewhere to sit, somewhere to breathe. 

 

Agatha’s mind races for a place to go, contemplating how full the library might be with 2 periods left in the day, wondering if she should go outside and soak in some vitamin D, if she should just walk home, curl into her bed and depression-sleep until tomorrow. 

 

She takes the staircase closest to her up to the second floor as the pattern of thoughts continue to stir, makes a path towards her locker, having a crumb of sanity left in remembering that she needs her History textbook for tonight’s homework. 

 

She holds onto that thought, trying to grasp at things that are less intense, the grayed-out green on the lockers, the rustle of students in an English classroom, she can hear them debating Julius Caesar, the crack of adolescent voices trying to make their point. 

 

She hears a piano.

 

A faint flurry of music closed behind a solid door.

 

The notes floating are certain but far away, a trained hand brushing against the keys with practiced ease. 

 

Agatha follows it, knowing where the noise must be coming from. Trusting the safety of it.

 

She turns the knob and pushes open the door, peeking her head in just enough to find the piano and the person playing it on the other side.

 

”I’m not available right now, you can come ba-“ Sister Calderu starts to say, her fingers stuttering against the keys, her words abruptly ending when she finally looks up at the intruder. 

 

“Agatha,” Lilia says her name like a pleasant surprise, holding it up like something to admire, it flitting through the air with all the adoration Evanora never assigns to it.

 

”Sorry,” Agatha apologizes, her hand still on the door knob, yet to cross the threshold, ready to close it and walk away, “I didn’t mean to bother you.”

 

”No,” Lilia gets up from the piano in a drastic flourish, a commanding caress of keeping Agatha from leaving, “please, come in.”

 

Agatha listens, caution in the way she pushes the door open, waits for the choir teacher to change her mind. She’s thinking about the way she’d so willfully obeyed Evanora’s violent demands, but always hesitated in the wake of anyone offering her something soft. 

 

She places her bag on the floor, sits in the front row of seats closest to the piano, gives Lilia the time to settle back in front of it. 

 

The nun takes a moment to look at her, showing something careful and wistful in her eyes, like she’s remembering the past, like she has a question to ask, but she’s not ready to ask it. 

 

It reminds Agatha of her one required year of Choir, of singing hymns as a freshman with a sense of pride, the dull lessening of her faith still not as apparent at the time. She remembers how Sister Calderu looked at her sometimes, a careful consideration like she could solve the changing puzzle in Agatha’s eyes. It reminds her of Evanora telling her to keep her distance from the nun, how her mother wouldn’t allow her to take the class another year, told her she could sing at church if she wanted to. It confused her then, how her Aunt Lilia had morphed into a monster made by her mother’s vague stories of ‘that woman is no good’ and ‘she is not like us, Agatha’. Whatever the full story was, Agatha was not in a position to question it. 

 

She knew the truth. Well, most of the truth. 

 

Lilia was a friend. A good friend. A good person.

 

And Evanora would never allow Agatha a friend.

 

Not then, when Lilia was the only person to value her opinion. 

 

Not now, when Rio empowered her to find her own strength for the first time in her life. 

 

Agatha lapses over the shifting memory, a vague sense of being 8 or 9. She remembers the voices more than what she could see. Lilia asking Evanora about the bruises, she doesn’t remember the exact mode of deflection, just that Lilia had been adamant that the severity was worse than childhood clumsiness, that the conversation ended with Evanora forcing her out of their house. 

 

“What were you playing?” Agatha asks to fill the newly threatened silence, but also to hold off on coursing further down memory lane. 

 

Lilia’s fingers find the keys again, trapezing over them like a professional ballet dancer, the notes ring out again, clearer without the wall separating Agatha from them, she listens closely, knows Lilia is waiting for her to pick up the melody.

 

Landslide by Fleetwood Mac, Agatha recognizes it as it glides into the chorus. One of Lilia’s hands playing as the piano version of the guitar, the other striking the melody of Stevie Nicks’ voice.

 

”Secular music? Really Sister Calderu?” Agatha jokes, breaking the tension of the solemn beauty of the song, faking a surprised gasp.

 

She wonders where it’s coming from, that gentle push back into joking, wonders whether it’s a coping mechanism or a sign that her body still feels safe with Lilia. 

 

The nun chuckles, appreciating the barb, not as uptight or strict as some of the other nuns, especially with students she felt protective of. Agatha had always seen her display a humanity that most of their other teachers hadn’t, an example of a confident personality that she hadn’t compromised in her relationship with God. 

 

“I can only listen to ‘I Am The Bread of Life’ so many times before my ears beg for something different.” Lilia sort of whines thinking of that particular hymn, like the truth of her words weighs heavy.

 

”Isn’t Stevie Nicks a witch?” Agatha asks, pushing on it a little harder, wanting Sister Calderu to keep the light banter going. 

 

The nun sort of scoffs, pushing the thought away with a gesture of her hands like the sentiment was pure bullshit.

 

“Just a rumor started by men who couldn’t comprehend a successful woman.”

 

”I’ll take your word for it, Sister Calderu.”

 

”Lilia,” the older woman chimes in to correct the name this time, almost like a deep breath she’s taking like Agatha calling her that in this space grated on something that went way beyond teacher and student. “You can still call me Lilia.”

 

Agatha nods. Smiles at her own trembling thoughts.

 

”Calling you Lilia makes me feel like we’re colleagues or something”, it’s a touch of jest, but the grounding pain of it feels like a loss. 

 

“Aunt Lilia, then?”

 

It feels like a careful offer, an apology for not trying harder to stay all those years ago, like a cave that sat in Agatha’s chest wondering how life would have been if Evanora gave Lilia just one more second to really see her, gave her just enough space to really know the truth, to get Agatha out of there. 

 

Agatha wasn’t mad at her. She knew her mother’s power and influence better than anyone, knew that Lilia had always been on her side, even if it was a part of her life that collapsed and faded. 

 

“okay”

 

The silence returns, but it hangs like a protective blanket, a step in the direction of reconciliation. 

 

“Are you alright, dear?” Lilia asks.

 

Agatha isn’t sure where the curiosity comes from. Maybe the way her eyes had still shown the after effects of crying, slightly puffy, the whites of her eyes more pink. Maybe it was the fading red of her cheek, none of Rio’s makeup to soften the coloring. Maybe it was the fact that she’d strolled into this classroom for the first time in years without an indicated reason.

 

Agatha shakes her head, the honesty of it pushing against her throat, her eyes threatening to spill tears again. She breathes, shuts her eyes for a few seconds, just long enough for the swell of it to pass, the vulnerability pressing into her like something she can’t show.

 

”I don’t really want to talk about it.” She doesn’t meet Lilia’s eyes, can’t let her see all of it. 

 

“Okay.” Lilia answers like it isn’t a burden, like she was ready to listen, but not willing to push, giving Agatha the freedom to choose. A choice that didn’t feel like a trap.

 

Lilia turns around, awkwardly reaching over desk for something instead of getting up to walk to the other side. Agatha can’t make out what she’s grabbing.

 

”Here,” The nun offers as she tosses the item across the 3 feet between them, “Chocolate cures everything.”

 

Agatha catches it, her face showing confusion as she reads the label on the red packaging.

 

”Milk Chocolate Candy Wafers Bar?” She questions the off-brand version of a Kit Kat now sitting in her hands. 

 

“Just eat it, it tastes the same,” Lilia grumbles, biting into a not-snickers bar. 

 

Agatha opens the plastic just enough to break off a corner and give it a fair taste. Lilia raises her eyebrows, a silent question of Agatha’s final verdict on the chocolate bar, while still chewing her own mess of chocolate, caramel, and peanuts.

 

She shrugs. “It’s fine, I guess.”

 

Lilia gets up from her chair, putting her hand out for Agatha to hand her back the candy. She breaks off her own piece tasting it for herself as if to confirm or deny Agatha’s opinion. 

 

She chews, contemplating. 

 

“It's missing something.” 

 

“Corporate greed.” Agatha supplies without missing a beat. 

 

Lilia laughs, a pleased smile settling and not leaving, the wave of nostalgia clear on her features. 

 

“I missed you, kid.” Lilia touches her shoulder, a delicate support, the certainty of it hanging between them. 

 

“Where do you even buy these?” Agatha asks, reading the label again when Lilia hands it back to her. 

 

Lilia shrugs like she’s got an off-brand candy dealer who she isn’t quite ready to sell out.

 

”Can’t afford a real almond joy,” She scoffs at herself, “I wasn't really thinking about my candy intake when I became a nun and took a vow of poverty.”

 

”The amount they pay you guys is bullshit,” Agatha munches on another piece of the bar, something to keep her busy, her stomach still not completely settled from earlier. “Sorry,” she adds, realizing her own curse word too late. “Bull…” she tries to correct it, find a Catholic approved alternative, “What’s an acceptable substitute?”

 

Lilia laughs, never seeming offended by it, clearly agreeing with the teenager. 

 

“I think the words you’re looking for are ‘fucking terrible’”

 

Agatha smiles, gives the words the strength to rip through the last of her lingering anxiety.

 

”Sounds right to me.”
