See the end of the chapter for more notes

1 Timothy 4:15-16- Be diligent in these matters; give yourself wholly to them, so that everyone may see your progress. Watch your life and doctrine closely. Persevere in them, because if you do, you will save both yourself and your hearers.

 

Lilia doesn’t force Agatha out of her classroom when the bell rings. She has a class to teach; freshman choir, a group of noisy pubescent teenagers that fill almost every seat in the room. But she’d squared Agatha with a firm look, something that said ‘hear me when I speak’, and said “You can stay here if you need to.”

 

The invitation hit her like a promise, like a safety net extended over any possible landing spots. Still, she doesn’t know how to say ‘thank you’, doesn’t know how to take the offer, allow herself to be seen as vulnerable, taking help without even asking for it. She hates that it’s visible, that Lilia knew something was wrong without having to voice it.

 

Maybe Rio had made her soft, especially lately, dulling the harsh edges into someone less intense, the cutting words she used to protect herself often slipping towards something a little less violent, a playful push in place of a full on stabbing. 

 

It felt strange, but good. The conflict of falling into herself, cutting away the parts of her identity that existed in favor of survival, trying to recognize the things about her that hadn’t been shaped out of external expectations, or the strict rules set out by her mother. 

 

That leap of progress had surged like a pet spider, something tangible she could hold, and nourish, but also still tickled as it walked across her skin, still had her fearful of the scurrying legs and potential bites. In all the growth, there was still caution, but still not enough.

 

The slap to the face felt just as symbolic too, the rug pulled from beneath her feet just as she started to gain her footing. It served as a reminder that Evanora would always have the upper hand, that in all the glimpses of joy, she’d always be designed to return here where spiders died and daughters listened. 

 

An attempt at an escape crawls out of her plans, her feet tracing the careful pattern of one step in front of the other, guiding her towards her Spanish classroom. She pulls out her phone, looking at herself in the front facing camera, not wanting to give Rio the evidence to start an interrogation. Her cheeks are dry now, the whisper of red in her eyes less noticeable, the sting of red on her cheek faded. She realizes that the slap graced her left cheek and Rio’s desk was on her right, the epiphany offering some relief. But her blue eyes have lost their glow, the growing spark that sang of profacsized returns, sat as a shrinking ache, a pain that stomped out the brightness. 

 

And maybe that was what kept her walking. Rio. Her torch. A crippling need to return to that scorching light. 

 

Agatha takes her seat with a steadying breath, pushes away the shuddering attempt at her impenetrable walls jolting back up, she closes her eyes, forces them back down, a careful truce made with the person she was and the person she wants to be. 

 

Evanora had made a mistake in giving her an inch, in showing her what life could be like without the weight of perfection, the constant lurking eyes of callous fear, the doubtful thunder that stormed like rage in her gut over every move she dared to make. She’d gotten a taste of freedom, a small shuddering lick of something warm and full. Like chocolate cake, a chance at sugar for the first time, richer than she’d allowed herself to imagine. 

 

Rio was her chocolate cake, the start of a new beginning, a place to celebrate, blow out candles, stability in the layers, the chance to indulge herself, show her the world and what it had to offer without the solemn cloud of constantly having to check over her shoulder. It was the wiggle room she needed to kiss Rio for the first time, to find safety in brown eyes and her cocky smile, to dream up the possibility of a life that wasn’t always darkness.

 

Agatha meditates on it for a moment, tries to elongate the dwindling time she has where her classmates shuffle into their seats, the shifting truth that Rio will be next to her within seconds. 

 

She doesn’t know how to process it, maybe that’s why it feels akin to suffocating, maybe it's not the same warped anxiety, but there’s still something unfamiliar in the way Rio’s energy seems to caress her, hold her up like she is weightless, give her the strength to take on the uncertainty, carries her trauma for her. Maybe it isn’t anxiety at all. Maybe it's excitement. Something she hadn’t felt for a long time. An eager enthusiasm to see the person who has loved her without question for so long, the person dedicated to her growth when Agatha could only focus on staying alive, the person who had protected her fiercely, was gentle with her in the wake of all her mess, was still patient with her, allowed her the time to let the unfamiliarity wash into comfort. 

 

It feels similar to the way her chest aches in fear, but the negative connotation melts away. Thinking of Rio, even at the chance of her anger, even with a tough conversation looming, standing in the reality of her pain and letting Rio see it, Agatha still felt a sense of peace. Rio’s voice ringing in her head like a church bell, a reminder that everything is going to be okay. 

 

Agatha feels her before she sees her, the shuffling beside her, Rio’s book bag hung loose on the back of her chair, her shoes shifting against the tile. She keeps her eyes closed a second longer, let’s the security of it wash over her. 

 

“Hola, hermosa,” falls from Rio’s mouth like a blessing, the Spanish wrapping around her tongue more easily than Agatha’s attempt at an accent. “Para ti.” Rio adds as Agatha opens her eyes to find the taller girl standing beside her desk, her hand outstretched. 

 

A part of Agatha is annoyed at the way Rio had swung easily into speaking Spanish, the calm switch as if she felt obligated to communicate that way in this classroom, a joke that edged closely to an added layer of comfort.

 

Agatha remembers Mr. Vidal explaining to her that they’d only spoken Spanish in their household until Rio turned 5, wanting to still give her the foundations of their first language before going to school and learning English, even if both parents spoke it well, they still wanted their daughter to follow the tradition, to be able to hold her own amongst her older extended family. 

 

She’s remembers Mrs. Vidal’s loud laughter as she recounted the story of how Rio didn’t answer to her own name on her first day of Kindergarten when her teacher took attendance, how Rio really thought her name was Chispita. She remembers Rio’s face in response to the story, a touch of embarrassment at sharing it with Agatha before she’d seen the way it made her smile, thinking of little Rio clumsy and unaware.

 

Agatha still rolls her eyes, not wanting Rio to think she’s gone completely soft, always amused by Rio's commitment to the bit. She finally looks down at the offered object, she takes it in her hands inspecting it closer. 

 

It’s a round-flat rock, about two inches in diameter. A soft grain against her fingers. On the face of it sits a painted design, a spiraled maze of lines, a swirling star at the center, the lines skillfully painted in black and gold. 

 

Agatha grazes her fingertips over it, flipping it over in her palm to find ‘RV’ carved in the back, before flipping it back, finding Rio’s eyes again, a silent question, waiting for an explanation,

 

”It was a little art project,” Rio is sort of perched over Agatha’s desk, palms holding herself up against the surface of it, sinking closer, making a space for just their voices amongst the chatter around them. She shrugs like it isn’t a big deal, letting her voice trade back to English, something more nonchalant. “Finally got a grade back for it, so I could give it to you.”

 

Agatha looks at it again, searching for the divine power of the symbol, wonders briefly how Rio had effortlessly crafted things with Agatha in mind, like she was never an afterthought, like she was the whole goddamn reason. 

 

“I obviously got an A,” Rio laughs to herself, smug, as she pushes off Agatha’s desk to finally sit at her own. To any onlookers, it seemed like a breezy shift, like the movement wasn’t charged, but Agatha followed the retreat, knew Rio was withdrawing in the swell of her own emotion, suddenly shy to explain it. 

 

“What does it mean?” Agatha asks, quiet, thoughtful, wanting to know the weight of it, especially if it was causing Rio to hesitate. 

 

“It’s Hecate’s wheel.” Rio starts, flipping open her binder to a fresh page of loose leaf, not meeting Agatha’s eyes, “The goddess of magic, and crossroads,” she adds like it wasn’t the driving force, knowing Agatha’s life had always felt like a battle of choice, which path to take; the one that had been violently paved by her mother’s commands or the one she’d have to find for herself. 

 

“It’s a shield,” Rio finally looks up at her, brown eyes soft, a crisp understanding, “It’s a symbol of protection.”

 

Agatha nods, shifting her glances between the rock and Rio, trying to find the composure to respond, trying to comprehend the tidal wave of care Rio sprung onto her with practiced ease, it didn’t feel like drowning in the current anymore, it felt like learning to float. She wasn’t swimming on her own yet, but it felt like a step in the right direction, keeping her head above water long enough to figure out how to paddle. 

 

“It’s beautiful.”

 

Rio’s eyes shine brighter then, like Agatha’s acceptance means everything, the delicate reverence she holds the stone with, the careful contemplation of its meaning, the grace with which Agatha is allowing her to love her steadily, it makes the pressure of her heartbeat hard to ignore. 

 

The bell rings, signaling the official start of class cutting off any chance at furthering the exchange. Brother Morales enters the room in a flurry, one of the only male teachers brave enough to deal with the quaking dramatics of girls in their teens. He’s young, probably in his twenties still, a hellstorm of crushes flung at him as one of the only consistent targets for their straight peers. 

 

One time he’d printed the answer sheet to the test on the last page and didn’t realize until 30 minutes later, when some teacher’s pet had to point it out to him, citing ‘academic integrity’ and ‘following God’. His aloof nature is enough to distract her out of the deep swirl of emotions. 

 

She does her best to follow along with the 500th explanation of conjugating ‘ser’ vs ‘estar’ like they haven’t been doing this since freshman year. She looks over at Rio, who on top of being a fucking nerd, had been unknowingly doing this in conversation her entire life before she even knew what verbs were. She doesn’t look bored, but definitely not fully immersed, none of the lesson landing as new information. But there’s definitely a stream of unfolding thoughts behind brown eyes, something more than the usual air of quiet confidence. 

 

Agatha pulls her phone out from under her thigh, the same place she kept it through most of her classes, pressed between her seat and the fabric of her skirt, skillfully hidden from the prying eyes of strict nuns, but ready to be used at a moment's notice. 

 

Sitting pretty far from the front of the classroom, it’s easy to slide it onto her desk, navigate to her text thread with Rio with one hand, crafting the outer perception that ‘vosotros’ was a very interesting part of Brother Morales’ lesson. 

 

‘r u ok???’ Agatha types out, hitting send before she even thinks to question if Rio’s phone is on silent. Maybe she’s projecting, reading into the quiet resolve of the girl next to her, because she hasn’t processed her own thoughts, hasn’t fully recovered from the mayhem in her mother’s office. 

 

For a fleeting moment, Agatha thinks that if Rio had given her that rock an hour earlier, Evanora’s rage wouldn’t have been able to reach her. 

 

Rio turns to her, the dull buzz coming from the pocket of her blazer, not loud enough to get their teacher’s attention but a clear signal to Rio, confirmation that it was Agatha texting her at the sight of her lilac colored phone case at the side of her desk before even unlocking her own phone. 

 

‘Ya, r u?’ 

 

Rio keeps her eyes forward, maybe an effort to keep up the illusion, maybe another attempt at hiding the full depths of her feelings. Agatha can’t read all of it right now, something complicated. 

 

‘u can’t freak out’

’but we have to talk after class’

’it’s about Evanora’

 

It feels strange using her mother’s government name like that, not that she’s in any way deeply connected to the placating connection of calling her ‘mom’ but she and Rio had always played with harsh nicknames using anything from ‘she-devil’ to ‘wicked gnome’. But that felt too trivial right now, condemning the gravity of it to a grating barb, it felt reductive, and maybe facing the whole truth of it was the start to making it end. 

 

‘Can’t u tell me right now?’ Rio answers, impatient. Agatha watches out of the corner of her eye as Rio shifts in her chair, fidgets with her pen. Maybe she should have waited to reveal the truth, maybe it was wrong to dangle the bloodied carrot in front of her face and make her wait for the whole story. 

 

Agatha bites her lip, she turns to Rio, trying to make the girl turn to her without a word. Brown eyes find blue like a magnet, the burning coffee of her irises set into something open yet sad, waiting for bad news, searching for the guillotine that Evanora would inevitably send shooting into Agatha’s neck, wondering what form it took as she sinks into the roaring ocean of Agatha’s eyes. 

 

Blue eyes turn back to her phone, a new attempt at finding the right words to explain. Her fingers hover over the keyboard, but they don’t spring into action, her mind coming up blank on where to start.

 

Before she can spiral back into the worry of it, or punish herself for not knowing, two new texts comes through. The gray bubbles not a figment of her imagination, but Rio’s words shining back at her.

 

’Fineeee I’ll wait…’ Agatha can hear the whine in Rio’s words even if not said out loud.

 

’But were getting ice cream’

 

—-

 

The pink spoon in Rio’s mouth is a distraction. 

 

Okay, maybe it’s just Rio’s mouth, but the plastic isn’t helping.

 

Rio isn’t exactly the neatest eater, especially when it’s just her and Agatha in Rio’s car, parked in an abandoned lot, 2 cups of ice cream, and the radio turned down from Rio’s preferred volume of ‘way too fucking loud’ (according to Agatha of course). 

 

It’s just them and some old R&B song Agatha doesn’t recognize. Agatha thinks to grab Rio’s phone off the center console, change it to something else, anything to put her focus elsewhere. 

 

The bit of chocolate on the corner of Rio’s mouth wins against the fear in her gut, and perhaps that’s its own battle to win, knowing that she didn’t have to think about her mother forever, that she could forget about Evanora in favor of remembering the girl in front of her.

 

Rio and her eyes that looked like fresh coffee grounds, the softness of her hands like she hadn’t spent half her life with a pencil in between her fingers, the way she could read Agatha like a book (something she loved as much as she absolutely hated), the way her tongue graced the plastic spoon like the mint chocolate chip flavor was something to be savored to the last drop.

 

Agatha was barely touching her own, a small cup of Butter Pecan, her own spoon busy stirring around the contents, rarely reaching her mouth. 

 

“You’re assaulting your ice cream?” Rio points her spoon at Agatha, her body turned  towards the passenger side, one of her shoes off, knee bent, her sock-clad foot pressed into the leather seat. “Does it taste weird?”

 

Agatha doesn't answer with words, simply holds up her cup to Rio as an offering, giving her the opportunity to taste. Rio takes the bait, dipping her spoon in without hesitation.

 

With the spoon back in Rio’s mouth, Agatha tries to focus on the question at hand, if Rio approves of her flavor choice, but she gets caught on pink lips, the way her cheeks hollow around the cold bite.

 

Rio scowls after a moment, spitting the pecan out of her mouth into her own empty cup like it truly offended her. 

 

“Nuts are gross”

 

”She really is a lesbian, ladies and gentlemen,” Agatha announces dramatically like they’re in front of a live studio audience.

 

”Who said I’m a lesbian?” Rio asks, still reeling from the taste, but never thrown by Agatha’s attempts at humor.

 

”Umm, your tongue told me earlier when it was in my mouth,” Agatha squints her eyes, “You remember, right?”

 

”I don’t think the bisexuals of the world would appreciate that assumption,” Rio adds, playing into the bit, as if it wasn’t just them privy to this conversation. She reaches forward with her spoon again, aiming to take another scoop of Agatha’s ice cream. 

 

But Agatha pulls it out of her reach, confusion clear on her face.

 

“You just said you didn’t like it.” 

 

“Maybe I’ll like it the second time.” Rio says like it makes perfect sense, obviously convinced by her own logic. 

 

“Fine,” Agatha brings it back within reach, “but let me warn you, it still has nuts.”

 

Rio goes in for her second taste, finding the same outcome, complete with the pecan hurled out of her mouth, and into the paper cup.

 

Agatha levels her with a look of ‘I told you so’ but there’s also a clear lack of patience, an attempt at hiding her amusement. Rio just smirks, shrugs.

 

”Spitting is kind of fun”

 

Agatha’s hand comes up to her own face, her fingers squeezing the bridge of her nose, shaking her head at her reality.

The taste of mint on her tongue plagues her like an afterthought, doing the things she told herself she wouldn’t.

Deuteronomy 28:6- Blessed shall you be when you come in, and blessed shall you be when you go out.

1 Thessalonians 3:12- And may the Lord make you increase and abound in love for one another and for all, as we do for you

It was the same way when Agatha had confessed to never watching SpongeBob when they were 14, how Rio forced her to binge the first five seasons on her Paramount plus account, claiming Agatha had to understand her references or they couldn’t possibly be friends.

Agatha nods.

1 Samuel 12:24- But be sure to fear the Lord and serve him faithfully with all your heart; consider what great things he has done for you.

She knew that it made Agatha feel weak. Instead, she observed, she sat patiently, witnessing Agatha bloom over years of delicate friendship, over years of untouched feelings. Maybe one day Agatha would feel comfortable in self celebration, and when that day comes, Rio will be waiting with the banners and the balloons, but for now she’s content to hold off, sink into what Agatha needs over what she knows she deserves.

Agatha remembers that silence isn’t war. Reminds herself that there is ease in not having to fill the space, that she can relax here, that she doesn’t have to live life in the margins waiting for her savior, always on guard for the next act of violence. 

 

All of her life had been written by her mother, coiled up and cold. Evanora had always decided what words made it into the story, the character she was painted as. Rio had been the first person to encourage her to rip out pages, to pick up her own pen. It had happened slowly, brown eyes weaseling into her psyche through weighted gestures, and silly jokes, but what really kept Agatha held up was the unconditional presence. Agatha let Rio see all the ugly, gave her the tweezers and flashlight to pick through it, and instead of power washing out the dirt, Rio had tangled herself into the roots, had made a home in all the things Agatha thought made her unworthy, whispered strength into all the cracks until they felt like stickers instead of scars.

And now was no different.

Here she was. Sat in Rio’s bed, allowing Rio to spread comfort through them both, the careful press of fingertips tracing against her palm, not running, not giving in to the desire to pull away from the unconditional affection that still felt foreign even if Rio had been offering it quietly for years.

Dinner isn’t ruined. If anything the salt of her tears offer more seasoning.

Genesis 3:15- And I will put enmity between you and the woman, and between your offspring and hers; he will crush your head, and you will strike his heel. 

 

Rio should be an FBI agent. At least Agatha thinks so. She could be infinitely meticulous about innocuous things, working on the same details of a painting for hours, remixing colors several times over to achieve the right shade. She’d organized her book shelf like a snobby librarian. She was able to compartmentalize well, separate hard stuff from the overarching positivity, knew when to focus, when to goof around. Look for the little details, but never forget the big picture.

 

Walking into school the next morning feels like a secret mission. A carefully calculated plan that Rio had concocted. When she woke up an hour earlier, Rio was sat up in bed, writing in her journal profusely, a list of possible courses to take, an analysis of potential scenarios, the pros and cons listed for each one. Agatha thought that if she let her stew any longer, she’d find Rio pasting pictures to the wall, using red string like she was trying to solve a murder, taping up all the evidence to see more clearly. 

 

They agreed to stick together as much as possible. That Rio would walk her to the two classes they didn’t share even if it made her late. Agatha was to text Rio immediately if she was summoned to the office again, and in the event that she couldn’t text her in front of Valentina, Rio had given her a note to slip to Jen, a request to text Rio ‘SOS’. Worst case scenario, Rio had been working on a pitch to convince Agatha to just walk out of school, avoid Evanora at all costs, stop the cycle even if it meant setting off the alarm from an emergency exit. 

 

Not knowing made her anxious, but it made it less harrowing to have a semblance of a plan, that Rio was doing the overthinking for her, seeing her put the effort in, the physical desire to validate her fears, it made her shiver. 

 

She was surprised that Evanora hadn’t called her, hadn’t demanded she returned last night in a text message, hadn’t sent out a search party. Agatha had no false beliefs that her mother wanted to keep her safe anymore, knew that all of it was a means of control. But a part of her shrivels at the way Evanora’s anger doesn’t seem passionate anymore either, that it didn’t rage loud enough to force her back into her grasp. 

 

They get to school on time, Rio purposely getting them there about 5 minutes early, just enough time for Agatha to get her books from her locker, no time to linger, no time to worry about things going wrong. 

 

Agatha takes a deep breath, reminding herself that Rio is beside her, she doesn’t need to be scared. It felt like crossing a bridge, the wood falling off beneath her feet, running as fast as she could to save herself from the impact of the water. But she isn’t running fast enough, making the decision to save herself, but knowing that the storm is still chasing her, that her mother wouldn’t simply give up, that there were more waves on the horizon. 

 

The new reality grates at her nerves, how each attempt at abuse felt harsher now, weighed heavier when she knew she wanted better, when she was finally pulling off her rose-colored glasses, resolving herself to face this without diminishing the impact. Truth be told, the slap in the office yesterday was far from the worst she’d ever endured, but it seared into her against the most hateful words Evanora had ever casted on her, it organized itself among memories of bruises that lasted weeks, the pain of a broken pinky finger that went untreated until Rio bent it straight, taped tightly to her ring ringer. 

 

Maybe because of the way her mother looked at her, a flash of unbridled anger, the way she had tangible evidence now that Agatha was a sinner, going to hell, too evil to save. Kissing Rio, loving Rio. Whatever Wanda had told her. It was something Evanora would never accept, a truth that swung harsher than anything Evanora saw as ungodly before. 

 

And still, Agatha’s gut reaction seeks to apologize, to placate her mother’s feelings, sink to her knees and beg for forgiveness, knowing that it’s the only way to keep her. It wouldn’t change Evanora’s mind, wouldn’t cause any less abuse, because Evanora didn’t pull her punches, didn’t stop until she saw blood. But it gnawed at Agatha’s guilt a little less, hoping God would hear her begging, that He would know she wasn’t evil, the pull towards reconciliation still etched into her soul.

 

It would be it’s own battle to convince herself that she had done nothing wrong, that she never deserved this, that it wasn’t her fault. 

 

For now, she’ll bite down the ‘sorry’ that lives on the tip of her tongue, she’ll breathe, she’ll look at Rio like a special agent, a bodyguard, an emotional support companion.

 

It’s Wednesday. She reminds herself. Two more days. And then the weekend. A safe place to hide. 

 

They make it through all of first period without any interesting interruptions, it’s enough time to refocus, to settle into the heaviness of the day, for her guard to fall slightly, relax into it. 

 

But seeing Wanda in the hallway between classes shatters the carefully placed security. 

 

Agatha had sort of forgotten. Crushed into a new reality where Evanora knew, where she was suddenly changing the rules, taking the abuse inside the school, offering Rio full transparency, and swimming in the pool of affection laid out for her. 

 

Wanda hadn’t been the biggest monster in her brain yesterday, overshadowed by the intensity of everything else. 

 

But the rage surges as soon as she sees the flash of her hair, the cold stare of green eyes. It’s freeing, remembering how anger feels as it courses through her. It crackles under the surface, but does not break, she clenches her teeth, holds tighter to her text book, but she does not move to fight. Her central nervous system still relearning how to navigate her fight or flight reaction, instead electing the freeze option, paralyzed by her rage here, the same way she is by her fear under Evanora’s violence. 

 

Perception shifts, the panic attack creeping up as Rio continues walking, Wanda walking in their direction, but not with them as her destination, simply passing in the hall, her head down. She tries to focus on her breathing, tries to speak, do something to get Rio’s attention, tell her to wait for her to catch her breath. It doesn’t work, the world shifting into slow motion, the colors feeling more crisp, the hallway feeling warmer than usual. 

 

She tries to claw her way out, strip herself of all the layers of trauma, remembers all the lives she has yet to experience. But everything feels so loud, too present, an overwhelming heightened observation like her body had forgotten to perform all of it’s involuntary processes in favor of using 100% of her brain to stop herself from collapsing.

 

Blue eyes stick to the veins on the back of Rio’s hand, the display of greenish blue lines free to see as she grips the front of Wanda’s shirt, pushes her backwards. They’re face to face now. Rio and Wanda. 

 

Wanda’s eyes read fear, widened and unsure, eyebrows curling in. But Rio’s anger is quiet, no ripple of screams or harsh demands, but brown eyes show determination. She keeps Wanda against the lockers, both hands firm against her shoulders, a grip that allows escape, but doesn’t lie about it’s intentions. 

 

Rio’s speaking into Wanda’s face, but Agatha can’t hear it. The chatter of the hallway, the cotton in her ears blocking it out. She feels like she’s in a fish bowl, condemned to never know the outside world. 

 

Her nervous system curls in on itself once more, a stark reaction to the way Rio’s jaw tightens, the way Wanda shrinks, the parallel of all the pain she’s felt painted in front of her with a new light, different actors in the same roles.

 

She’s not sure if it’s fight or flight, but her feet press her forward suddenly, a floating feeling at the way she glides over tile in a flourish. She doesn’t remember taking the steps, launched forward to Rio’s side like teleportation, like the movie was being shot from a different angle, a continuity error in the way she was closer now. 

 

A few other students flank them, a small commotion now, trying to separate the two girls, stop the dramatics of a high school fight. As Agatha joins them the rest of their peers seem to take notice, a crowd forming around them, an innate need to catch a glimpse of whatever was about to go down between Rio (someone who tended to get along with everyone) and Wanda (the most devout of them, seemingly able to rile Rio up). 

 

“Rio,” the crack in her voice barely reaches over the jeering of the crowd as she pushes through to be close enough to touch her. Rio’s shoulder is rigid under her fingertips, sharp and flexed, “Let her go.”

 

Rio doesn’t fight her on it, hesitates for about half a second, a flash of confusion at the way Agatha’s voice peaked in something she couldn’t read. It wasn’t fear. It was exhaustion. 

 

Rio’s hands leave Wanda’s shoulders. Agatha can see the muscles in her shoulders rest, holding intense eye contact with Wanda for an extra second, a silent warning that she was not offering her forgiveness, simply following Agatha’s wishes. 

 

Rio doesn’t look at Agatha, can’t face her. She turns and walks away. Agatha looks at Wanda now, flashes through all the emotions she’s supposed to feel, but she can’t bless it with any words, she hoped Wanda could understand what she herself didn’t know how to label. 

 

She follows after Rio, pushing through the crowd, leaving the swarm of teenage girls with no answers, no explanation, no show. Her feet trace the pattern of Rio’s footsteps, losing her in the sea of people, but knowing where she’s headed without thinking about it too hard. 

 

It’s cool outside. A light drizzle. Agatha shivers against the gust of Spring wind, her body still warm from the events that had just occurred inside. She knows the side door locks automatically from the inside when it closes, knows she’ll have to walk to the front to get back inside. 

 

A part of her never wants to return, contemplates dropping out with the last few months of her senior year left. Dreams up a life where she could couch surf, get a job, escape Evanora and all the hurt that came with being in her proximity.  

 

But her mind can’t stray for long, focused on finding Rio, on making this all okay. 

 

Rio’s form comes into view as she takes a few steps forward, she’s slouched forward, sitting on an old bench on the side of the school. They’d discovered it early in their Sophomore year and claimed it as their own. It was seldom used by anyone else, placed in a strange area, the section of school that existed first, before the several expansions to the building. The metal is rusting, the black paint chipping away. A small dedication, a plaque barely readable ‘In memory of’ and a name they can’t read, letters they can’t agree on. Overgrown grass around it, the view from it- gray sky and singing clouds.

 

In loving memory- a person meant to be remembered who they’d never know the name of.

 

It reminds her of idle conversations, laughing at the absurdity of their teachers, sharing snacks, hiding away here in each other’s company, never needing a reprieve from her favorite person. 

 

She stops a few feet away, unsure if Rio knows she’s there, wanting to commit the image to her memory. Rio here, trapped in thought, eyes trained on the gravel, biting at her lips nervously, her knee shaking.

 

”I wasn’t gonna hit her.” 

 

Rio’s voice holds some anger, but it swells in a cautious burst, trying her best to manage the feelings, pushing them into the conversation without any small talk, no easing in. 

 

And Agatha wants to reassure her, tell Rio that she knows she wouldn’t do that. But her brain isn’t being rational. She couldn’t allow that. Even if she knows Rio isn’t a violent person, even if the chance was resting at 0.005%, she needed it to be zero. 

 

“It wasn’t about that,” Agatha finally brings herself into view, sits next to Rio, studies the side of her face, brown eyes still refusing to meet blue. 

 

“I was just trying to protect you,” Rio squeaks in an attempt to defend herself, all touches of anger gone, a breath away from a sob. It feels like pleaful remorse, not an excuse. 

 

Agatha’s hand lands over Rio’s knee, an effort to soothe, quiet the nervous shaking. 

 

“I’m not mad,” Agatha shakes her head, her voice slow, honest. 

 

Rio doesn’t answer, but her breaths seem more steady after that, like she’s returning back to reality, silencing the demons in her own mind. 

 

Maybe this was a little more foreign for Agatha, figuring out how to comfort Rio, she wasn’t sure if she was doing a good job. But the thing that she cherished most about Rio was her presence, the fact that she was always there, unconditional. She thought at the very least, she could manage to do the same. 

 

They sit in the quiet for a moment, filing through the sound of light rain, the cold metal of the bench pressed into the back of her thighs, the warmth of Rio’s thigh under her hand, the smooth skin as she strokes it with her thumb unconsciously. The quiet contemplation in furrowed eyebrows, the way Rio stares forward, lost in the concrete. 

 

“Fuck Wanda,” Agatha grumbles, breaking Rio from her staring contest with the ground. She finds blue eyes, a complex swirl reflected back in the brown. 

 

“But mostly fuck Evanora,” she continues. 

 

She readjusts herself on the bench, moving closer, her free hand coming to wrap around Rio’s back, her head falling onto her shoulder. 

 

“I’m sorry if I scared you,” Rio apologizes, her voice hushed into the small space between them, “The last thing I want is for you to look at me and think I’m anything like your mother.”

 

Rio had finally said it out loud, the reason why it stung harder than they’d like to admit, the reason Agatha couldn’t let Rio punish Wanda.

 

If Rio hit Wanda, how was she any different than Evanora?

 

Wanda was a victim in this too. A carefully placed bomb by a master manipulator waiting to erupt. Evanora had preyed on Wanda, used her vulnerability against her, knew that Wanda was doing what she thought was right, even if it was hard to agree with. 

 

“You could never be like her,” Agatha whispers, sliding further into the embrace, wanting to kiss Rio. The consequences feeling small. 

 

Rio nods, her eyes still coated in a layer of sadness. 

 

“We’ve been fighting a lot lately,” Rio turns forward again, picking at a stray thread on Agatha’s sleeve, a confession of insecurity even if not expressed that way, Agatha can tell.

 

”Feels like figuring things out to me.”

 

”I’ve never felt closer to you,” Rio babbles, adding it like it's a valid form of evidence, a supporting piece to Agatha’s words.”So, I guess that’s a plus.” Like she’d forgotten why they had somehow gotten closer.

 

Agatha reminds her, pressing a soft kiss into Rio’s laugh line, loving every delicate nuance of her face, appreciating the closeness to her lips without sealing it completely. 

 

“If this is how you wanna fight for the rest of our lives, I would be so down for that.” Agatha doesn’t mean for it to sound like a promise. But the weight of it isn’t something that makes her recoil. Rio breaths out, something akin to a chuckle, a smirk that doesn’t reach all her features. She can’t bring herself to regret it.

 

“You really couldn’t find a better place to propose?” Rio jokes, pressing in some lightness. 

 

“It’s our bench,” Agatha defends herself as if Rio was actually calling her romance into question, “The venue is perfect.”

 

”Whoever this bench was dedicated to is probably rolling in her grave. Poor lady is screaming slurs from the beyond.”

 

”And how do we know it’s a woman?” Agatha asks, wondering when Rio had decided that, usually sharing their bench donor conspiracy theories with each other. 

 

“No one remembers men lovingly.”

 

It makes Agatha laugh, a quiet snort she can’t cover. Because Rio’s quips always fall free so easily. Words that find a home in Agatha’s heart, for all her attempts to make her laugh, for all the joy Rio pressed in right next to the tragedy. 

 

“What about your dad?”

 

Rio purses her lips, mulling it over, like she’d seriously forgotten his existence. 

 

“The exception that proves the rule,” she settles on after a moment, a quiet smile returning to her face, “Mami had to whip him into shape for years before she agreed to go out with him.”

 

”He told me it was love at first sight.” Agatha supplies, still trying to put the story together.

 

Rio shakes her head, scoffs, licks her lips as if to say ‘of course he said that’.

 

”Maybe for him,” Rio adds.

 

”I mean your mom is super hot”

 

Rio squints at her, wondering how they got here. 

 

“What? It’s true. You can’t be mad. You look just like her.” Agatha tries to defend herself, shaking Rio’s arm to get her to stop looking at her like that. 

 

“Anyway,” Rio pulls her arm out of her grasp, wrapping it around Agatha’s shoulders, keeping her close. “they were actually friends for years. Met through mutual friends. He asked her out once and she said no. He respected that, stayed her friend for like 2 years of her being engaged to someone else.”

 

”So, we could have had a world without a Rio Vidal?” Agatha mumbles, unsure if it's a joke. 

 

“I guess,” Rio chuckles.

 

”So, what changed?” Blue eyes look up to find brown, search her face for the answers. 

 

Rio takes a breath before recounting the rest, like she’d been there to experience it, hearing it so many times as a child, the love story of her parents, her own origin story. 

 

“Mami got really sick for a while, doctors couldn’t figure out what it was, but she was bedridden, always running a fever. And I guess my dad would show up to the hospital or her apartment with their friends. But then he started showing up alone, bringing her soup, replenishing her tissue supply, sitting with her for hours. She said she started to see him differently.” She finishes with a shrug.

 

”He took care of her,” Agatha whispers, something reminiscent.

 

”Hmm,” Rio hums, “Think it took like 2 more years for them to actually date though.”

 

”Being a loser runs in the family, I see,” Agatha tries to hold back the smile, unable to keep the amusement out of her eyes. 

 

Rio doesn’t seem offended, happy to be called a loser in this instance. 

 

“We’re just powerless against beautiful women,” She corrects the statement lightly, pressing a kiss into Agatha’s cheek. 

 

“Did they ever figure out what was going on with your mom?”

 

Rio shakes her head. Her face still tucked close into the side of Agatha’s face, her nose brushing against her cheek bone with the movement. “No. Maybe just God trying to bring them together.” 

 

A moment passes, the calmness settling over them, the tangent leaving space to process the morning.

 

”I’m sorry I didn’t plan ahead about Wanda,” Rio’s voice is quiet, still close to her ear.

 

”We can’t plan for everything.”

 

Agatha answers, a sting that reminds her of her own guilt, of the way she’d tried to wait for perfect moments when time continued spinning over all her delicate plans. She could never blame Rio, she knew her heart, the soft empathy that radiated out of her like a spell of protection. 

 

“We should get to class,” Rio opens her mouth again, another press of her lips to Agatha’s cheek, always the one trying to do the right thing even if she wanted to stay here forever. 

 

The sky seems to agree with her, the drizzle morphing into something heavier, the rain suddenly falling harder. 

 

“I’ll race you,” Rio whispers into her ear, smug and certain she has the upper hand. 

 

Rio pushes off the bench in a poised surge, grabbing her backpack off the ground and swinging it over her shoulder in the same second, moving as fast as she can.

 

Agatha doesn’t move yet, waits for Rio to take her first stride before rising to her feet.

 

Rio’s smirk is already there, sure she’s going to win, but before she can cement any space between them, Agatha grabs her by the backpack, pulls her backward.

 

It’s rough and startling, something Rio isn’t expecting as she falls into Agatha’s strength, her body turning to catch itself. 

 

But Agatha catches her instead. Molding into her, kissing her softly, their lips finding a slow rhythm as Agatha holds onto her tightly, doesn’t let her run. She feels Rio’s hands on her hips, knows the game is over, Agatha has won.

 

She waits for the rain to become a little heavier, the sound crushing into her ears, their hair and uniforms growing wet before she pulls away. She revels in the way she’s able to take Rio’s breath away, takes note of the desire in brown irises, before pushing her away swiftly and turning around, running full speed to the front entrance. 

 

“Hey,” Rio calls from behind her, trying to catch up, her heart racing from more than just the cardio, “That’s cheating.”

 

Agatha only laughs, pushes herself to run faster.

 

—-

 

Numbers 14:18- The Lord is long suffering and abundant in mercy, forgiving iniquity and transgression; but He by no means clears the guilty, visiting the iniquity of the fathers on the children to the third and fourth generation. 

 

Her skirt is damp. Her hair still sticking to her neck. 

 

They’ve been in English class for fifteen minutes, Sister Hart only shaking her head at them as they arrived late to class. 

 

The quiet shame from the nun was nothing in comparison to the empty seat in the front of the room, a desk usually occupied by Wanda Maximoff. 

 

Rio’s jaw is tight, an exterior she’s trying to portray as calm, but Agatha can read through it. The weight of it rips through her, the pain reflected in brown eyes, all because of her.

 

It almost feels like the devil on her shoulder laughing, telling her ‘I told you so,’ because she knew this would happen, knew that letting Rio in solved nothing, only brought Rio pain, showed her the full truth of what she was going through. And now it wasn’t Rio carrying the weight for her, it was Rio’s burden too. 

 

She hated it.

 

Hated seeing Rio sling back and forth between trying her best to keep it together and putting on a mask. It felt cruel. The way Agatha only seemed to be getting better to Rio’s detriment. It went back to the conversation they’d had by the swings that day at church, that change would come and they had no power to stop it. 

 

Rio turns her head to check on her, finds blue eyes in an instant. She wears a reassuring smile, something small but sincere, saving Agatha from all the scarce glory, offers her a gift in the way Rio can still force happiness onto her features. 

 

Rio’s eyes flick around her face, drag over the delicate curves. Agatha tries to erase all the evidence of her own fear, push away the tension in her own jaw, relax her eyebrows. 

 

Brown eyes squint for a moment, a new thought. She pulls the black hair tie off her wrist and offers it to Agatha without a word. 

 

It collapses the moment into a careful snapshot, a second in time where one friend could offer another a small favor. An enormous condition of their relationship being the unspoken instances of care. Agatha didn’t need to ask, Rio always showed up. Rio didn’t need to say she was happy, or sad, or scared, Agatha could always see it. 

 

Agatha takes it, ties her hair into a low ponytail, the cool air on her neck, making it easier to self-regulate, less overwhelmed by the soggy state of her clothes, trying to breathe. 

 

Because where the fuck is Wanda? 

 

She couldn’t bring herself to ask the follow-up questions. To wonder about exact consequences, to use the rest of her energy to worry. 

 

It seemed she’d passed the anxiety bug to Rio instead, could sense it in the way Rio’s knee bounced under her desk, the way she wasn’t doodling in her notebook, holding her pen too hard, zoning out. Brown eyes that kept tracing back to the same empty seat. 

 

Fuck. 

 

There was a part of Agatha that wanted to run. Her mother’s voice in her head reminding her that she isn’t special, that she brings evil wherever she goes, that Rio would be better off if she just left. It was crushing, knowing that she’d never wanted to run away to protect herself, that she’d always stayed with Evanora, prayed away the pain but never just left with a duffle bag and a dream. But now that it was hurting someone else, Rio, the only good she could trust, she found herself wanting to flee. 

 

She was ruining her. Corrupting her affectionate nature, pulling at threads that the Vidals had carefully woven for almost 18 years. It made her want to close the curtain, pretend this never happened, sink back into the life that had Agatha on the receiving end of the pain, and Rio at arms length.

 

Even if it meant never kissing her, never loving her. Maybe that was better than breaking her. 

 

The familiar rhythm of heels on tile stretches closer and closer until Valentina is standing in the threshold of the door. Her eyes trace from Sister Hart over the classroom of students, surveying, seeking someone in particular. 

 

It feels like deja vu. Only Rio is beside her and their vice principal’s eyes hold something more serious, a clear indication that the woman knows something. 

 

“Ms. Vidal,” Valentina speaks as Sister Hart pauses her lesson, her eyes holding a calculated press of anger, “Principal’s office. Now.”

 

They hadn’t planned for this either. Rio being the one summoned into Evanora’s dungeon.

 

Agatha tries not to spiral back into another panic attack, clenches her fists in her lap, her nails digging into her palms, doing her best to hold back the tears of frustration, her life feeling more and more like a never ending obstacle course. 

 

Rio doesn’t look at her at first. Simply nods at Valentina, before putting her notebook and pen into her bag, throwing it over her shoulder with ease. An attempt at displaying calm, it throws Agatha off for a moment, thinking she’d unknowingly trained Rio into being able to hide her emotions, the guilt of making Rio feel like she had to press down any romantic feelings for years, the way she’d given Rio access to her trauma, but never allowed her to help her out of it, only gave her the freedom to help her hide it. 

 

Rio’s voice comes through a moment later, a whisper just for Agatha, the squeak of it is anything but controlled, the crease of emotion clearly present. 

 

“It’s gonna be okay”

 

And then she walks away, follows Valentina like she’s on her way to the gallows, her head still held high in protest. 

 

It only takes 30 seconds for Agatha to give up on staying put, the shattering truth of Rio gone, the drowning course of Sister Hart’s voice pressing back in. She thinks to ask to use the restroom, make up some excuse to leave, find any reason to not be trapped here. But she never raises her hand, the words don't come. 

 

She grabs her things, shuffles her binder into her bag without regard for the noise it makes.

 

”Agatha,” Alice’s voice clips through the air, a sharp whisper from a few seats away, “You okay?”

 

She only meets the concern in Alice’s eyes for a fraction of a second, can’t meet the emotion without falling, knows that it’s too much to take other people’s pity, that she doesn’t deserve it. She shakes her head no, her eyes still cast down, before closing her bag, pushing up from her desk and stomping out of the classroom without hesitation.

 

”Ms. Harkness.” She can hear Sister Hart call after her, but it clings to her brain like an afterthought, a boomerang that she sends back, can’t grasp.

 

It weighs on all the shadows of expectation. The principal’s daughter causing a scene, leaving class without permission, making whatever was already going on worse. She couldn’t bring herself to care about what it meant, what her classmates would inevitably gossip about her, what Evanora would do to her when she found out, God’s disappointment. All she cared about right now was making sure Rio was okay.

 

She walks towards the main office, knowing she’s only about 2 minutes behind them. Her thoughts come in clear for the first time all day, contemplating her options. Running isn’t one of them. 

 

Agatha tries to gauge what might be happening behind those walls, the words of vitriol, if Evanora is using her fists. The rational part of her brain knows her mother still has a reputation to protect, that laying a finger on anyone but her daughter would be a consequential miscalculation, that Rio had parents that would fight for her. That even if Evanora was powerful and well connected, the Vidals still had the means to blemish her perfect image. 

 

Barging in wouldn’t help, Agatha decides. Save them both from the added pressure, especially when Agatha doesn’t know how her mother is spinning this. 

 

She waits instead, pacing in the corner, out of sight in the hallway a safe distance away. She keeps looking at her phone, trying to gauge the passage of time, the reflection of numbers only making her more anxious as she never turns away from the office, willing Rio to come out unharmed. 

 

Maybe Agatha is a witch.

 

Because Rio steps through the threshold a second later, a mix of something in her eyes as she turns to walk away, seemingly still in one piece. 

 

Rio doesn’t see Agatha, the girl out of view. Agatha opens her phone frantically, not wanting to yell Rio’s name, or chase after her, afraid of being seen in front of the office, afraid of alerting her mother of her presence.

 

’turn around’ she texts Rio.

 

She watches as the brunette fishes her own phone out of her pocket, reads the text before swinging her body around, her eyebrows raising like she’d just won a prize as her eyes fall on Agatha.

 

The relief seems to wash over them both, Rio jogging towards her like long lost lovers finally reunited. 

 

“Are you okay?” Agatha asks as both hands settle around Rio’s face, caressing her cheeks like she needs to feel her, know without a doubt that she’s real. 

 

Rio nods into her hands, presses their foreheads together for a moment, seeks out the connection just as harshly. Her hands latching onto Agatha’s wrists as they breathe in the same air.

 

”What did she do?” 

 

Rio’s hands let go, instigate some space, one moves to press out of Agatha’s grasp, the left interlacing their fingers, the right pulls a pink paper from her pocket. 

 

“We’ll I’m suspended for three days for ‘instigating a physical altercation on school property’,” Rio reads from the official document, rolling her eyes as a sigh leaves her mouth.

 

“Rio,” Agatha hums, trying to comfort her, trying to press away all the callous intrusions.

 

”It’s okay,” Rio squeezes her hand, “it’s not your fault.”

 

”Your parents.”

 

”I’m not worried about that right now.” 

 

Agatha looks at her for a moment, taking space to process the information, Evanora hadn’t touched her, hadn’t done any irreparable harm, three days, they could get through that. 

 

“She’s trying to separate us,” It leaks from Agatha’s mouth like a sad epiphany, an idea not worth celebrating.

She can’t.

 

”I can’t”

 

”Agatha. Please.”

 

Agatha couldn’t stand the way Rio’s voice broke, the solid swirl of tears waiting to fall, the loose hold she had left of her resolve. It broke her heart. 

 

She pulls her hand out of Rio’s grasp feeling the burn of the way they fit together so perfectly, the way touching Rio had always felt right. 

 

The weight of it is too heavy. She turns and walks away, a huff on her lips as she can no longer hold in the emotion, her feet feel heavy. But she knows Rio is following.

 

”Where are we going?” Rio asks, unwilling to believe that Agatha could leave her behind now. It stings again, knowing Rio has this image of her, that Agatha knows the ugly truth. 

 

This isn’t running away.

 

She knows it would only hurt Rio more. 

 

Still, she can’t answer out loud, just keeps walking forward to the front exit of the building, through the parking lot towards Rio’s car. 

 

Take me home. 

 

She thinks, but doesn’t say, her throat feeling coated in thorns, unable to open her mouth.

 

But Rio seems to understand. Turns the key in the ignition, shuffles a playlist called ‘sad boy hours’, and pulls out of the parking lot.

No one had ever seen her like this.

There’s a weighted silence that follows, blue eyes locked on brown ones, the foot of space between them pulsing with heated potential, a question that holds too much uncertainty, a question Agatha shouldn’t have thought to ask, the shattering self-doubt only present from the repetition of hatred stuffed under her skin from her mother. In the end, it would always be this. Agatha afraid to lose her, scared that she didn’t deserve Rio, that she was holding her back, that it would be easier to push her away, take the control back. 

 

It wasn’t her fault. It wasn’t her fault.

 

But it was time to end the cycle, find the paths of healing, stop subjecting herself, stop subjecting Rio to the wreckage. 

 

“I sit through the storm with you for the chance to see the sunlight.” Rio releases like a chant, a quiet truth. Like she’d be here to take on the rain with her, hold tight in hurricanes and earth quakes. Like they could build towards the clear skies, the single steps forward to be cherished along side the intended destination. 

 

For richer or for poorer, in sickness and in health. 

 

The chance. 

 

Just the possibility was worth it to Rio.

Rio’s eyes shift to the side, before tracing back. Contemplating. Hesitant to reveal the vulnerability. 

 

“It’s from the book of Rio,” She reveals, a half smirk at the way Agatha was slowly conceding, sheepish in the wake of sharing her own personal words, “A poem. Written for a girl.”

 

Agatha knew Rio wrote. A collection of poems she’d never shown her. A tiny notebook she carried in her backpack, black and leather, white lined pages that Agatha had never laid her eyes on. A section of Rio that remained secret until now. 

 

She doesn’t press on the new revelation, doesn’t point out the way they both could let down walls around each other, that it didn’t need to be qualified with placating observations.

 

“She seems pretty lucky to have you.” Agatha tries, pressing in the truth without saying it directly, “This girl you speak of.”

 

”I’m the lucky one,” Rio says and Agatha can tell she believes it, “she just doesn’t know it yet.” 

 

Agatha scoffs, thinking the day could never come when she realizes she’s out of Rio’s league. 

 

Rio turns to grab one of the water bottles, holds it out to Agatha like a peace offering. 

 

She takes it without hesitation, tired of pushing away. She sits on the bed, picking up the fallen grapes and tossing one at Rio, popping the other in her mouth. 

 

It hits Rio in the cheek before hitting the floor. Brown eyes blink rapidly, like she’s trying to catch up with what just happened. 

 

“I’m sorry,” Agatha chuckles. “Not about the grape. About being a brat.”

 

Rio sighs, sits down next to her. She takes her own bottle, uncaps it, takes a sip. 

 

“Hmm,” Rio hums, “You’re like a rejected sour patch kid. Sour, sweet, always right next to me.” 

 

Agatha smiles, turning her head to look at her, Rio turning too like a magnet. 

 

“Can I be a green one?” 

 

“Why?” Rio smiles, “Cuz you think green are my favorite?”

 

Agatha shrugs, smirks, smug. 

 

Rio smiles, pushes against Agatha’s shoulder with her own. Sighs something resigned, content in the return to their normal banter, a place far away from the worries of their lives. 

 

—-

 

Ephesians 4:26-27 -Be angry and do not sin; do not let the sun go down on your anger, and give no opportunity to the devil. 

 

Agatha doesn’t remember falling asleep, just remembers Rio tucking her in. They’d shared the bowl of grapes, stopped talking about the cascading clouds of life. Rio turned on the TV, but didn’t get all the way into bed with her, sat up next to her instead, doodling in a sketchbook. 

 

She didn’t plan on falling asleep, but the emotions brought on a new wave of exhaustion. Rio gave her a shirt to put on, the fact that she’d ripped her shirt off and spent the whole conversation in just her skirt and bra wasn’t lost on her. The fabric soft and comforting, the smell of Rio’s laundry detergent surrounding her. 

 

Maybe it was the quiet, the background noise of the TV along with Rio’s scribbling pencil. The steady warmth of Rio beside her, they weren’t entangled, but Rio’s knee was bent, pressing into her side, the barrier of Rio’s heavy comforter between them. The warmth, the safety, knowing they could disagree, that she could possess big emotions and Rio wasn’t kicking her out, wasn’t creating a situation they couldn’t grow from. 

 

When she opens her eyes, she’s not sure what time it is. Only a few hours later. Rio next to her, her posture shifted, hunched over her tiny notebook seemingly swapped out from her sketch book, her pen sliding across the page with ease. 

 

The TV’s playing something else now. An asmr video of someone doing a grocery haul. It’s still light outside, probably around 1 in the afternoon. 

 

She scans the side of Rio’s face, watching as her eyebrows scrunch in thought, her eyes tracing over the words as she writes them, her tongue poking into the inside of her cheek. She thinks about waking up next to Rio for the foreseeable future, not just for the next few months in her childhood bedroom. But for a long time, she imagined Rio older, wrinkles next to her eyes, growing fully into all her features, phases of different hairstyles. 

 

“Are we more Emily Dickinson or Edgar Allen Poe?” 

 

Rio shifts at the sound of Agatha’s voice, a little thrown by it, unaware she was awake, unaware she was being watched. Her pen comes to a stop. Brown eyes soft and steady.

 

She doesn’t answer Agatha’s question, shifts to grab a plate from the bedside table.

 

”I saved you half my grilled cheese,” Rio offers like it's effortless. 

 

Agatha sits up, takes the plate, presses a kiss to Rio’s cheek as her thank you.

 

Rio looks at her, makes sure she’s eating, tucks back into her book, shifted just enough to hide the contents, Agatha doesn’t push, doesn’t ask to read it, knows Rio will share if she wants to. 

 

“I’m sorry, again.” Agatha places in the air around a mouthful of bread and cheese, coating herself in the need to say it, still feeling bad about it.

 

“It’s okay,” Rio looks up for a half a second, “I forgive you,” her foot juts out, poking Agatha’s shin with her toes. 

 

“I don’t like making you sad.” 

 

“We don’t have to keep talking about it,” Rio tries, willing them to stop saying all the heavy things, so much already happening today. 

 

Agatha picks at the crust. 

 

“You just seem really sad lately.” Agatha muses, another attempt at pressing into the wound, “I don’t like being the thing making you sad.”

 

Rio chuckles. A response Agatha isn’t expecting. 

 

“That’s funny?”

 

Rio’s tongue swirls around her mouth, contemplating. 

 

“No. Sorry. I just- For a long time I thought protecting you meant shielding you from my bullshit.” Rio tries to explain. But Agatha is only more confused, unsure how that connects back. Rio seems to read the misunderstanding, she looks at Agatha waiting for the puzzle to click, but it doesn’t.

 

”I’m always sort of sad,” Rio continues, shrugging like it’s simply part of her reality, something she’d gotten used to, “I guess I’ve just been hiding it from you a little less lately. You’re not the only one who built walls to protect yourself.”

 

Rio’s voice is thoughtful, certain. A resolve she’s made with herself like a sordid temptation, lowering her walls slowly, not the way Agatha’s had crashed all at once. 

 

“I have depression.” Rio reveals like it’s small, not noteworthy. She turns towards the nightstand again, opens the drawer, pulls out a prescribed bottle of pills, holds it up like proof, shakes the contents enough to make a noise, “Just always felt like it was small in comparison to all the stuff you have going on.”

 

”Rio,” Agatha tries, looks at Rio like she wants to hold her, erase the parts that felt not extraordinary enough to voice out loud. Everything she knew about Rio was a thundering shutter, a loud laugh, a big smile, the most expressive eyes, a confidence that took up space, a spirit that demanded attention. This felt like the soft underbelly, a chance to see behind all the carefully laid scarves. She didn’t want to take it for granted.

 

Underneath the guilt, the gnawing fear that her own trauma got in the way of knowing this about Rio sooner, there was a solid field of elation, knowing that Rio felt safe enough to share it now, that they weren’t perfect at this, stumbling like baby giraffes, that they were allowed to make mistakes, allowed to be human. She knew Rio’s forgiveness was not freedom to make the same mistakes over and over, but a place to be held accountable. Knowing she would be there to kiss her wounds, but also remind her that their current life is not something to get comfortable in, to keep fighting for better. 

 

But, Rio takes her response differently.

 

”I know, I hide it well.” She sighs, “I just wanted you to know.”

 

Agatha nods. Takes Rio’s empty hand, brushes over her knuckles. 

 

And she’s overwhelmed. Not for the first time today. But it slings her through all the intense affection she feels for the girl in front of her, a cocoon of desire that warps around them like a solid hand. It holds her up against the pulling need to crumble.

 

Rio. Brave and vulnerable. Choosing to speak her truth. 

 

In all the attempts at throwing this away, telling herself that letting Rio in would only hurt them both. Maybe that was true. But Agatha still wanted to try, still wanted to tangle all their problems together, tie a firm knot, learn how to cope in the safety of Rio’s arms, be an anchor for all the sadness she found in brown eyes.

 

She presses forward, not caring about the empty plate tilting crumbs into the sheets. She links her arms around Rio’s neck. Hugs her as tightly as she can, not knowing any words to describe it. 

 

Agatha thinks of all the times Rio has comforted her. Thinks of the firm stroke of her thumb on her thigh, on her cheek, on her wrist, the quiet empathy in brown eyes. 

 

Rio taught her it wasn’t about the words. She didn’t need to find the perfect phasing or say the right thing.

 

She just needed to be there. And that she could do. 

 

A chance. 

 

Agatha could live with that.

Chapter 13

Chapter Notes

Ummmm surpriseeee…fastest update in a while. This one definitely less angst…sorry about last chapter lol were in our healing era let Agatha live

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Joshua 1:9- Have I not commanded you? Be strong and courageous. Do not be afraid; do not be discouraged, for the Lord your God will be with you wherever you go.

 

It was hot outside, Spring washing softly towards Summer heat. Global warming. Agatha could remember how much snow they’d gotten in her childhood. She wasn’t really allowed outside unsupervised, she couldn’t remember a time where being a kid was about playing or creating fairytale worlds. But she remembers liking the cold, admiring snow men made by other children, watching it melt over the next few days. In the last few years, Snow days had felt less common, snow fall seldom more than a couple of inches. 

 

And now it seemed like Spring was a passing glance, a flash of humidity and rain before petulant sunshine kicked in. Agatha tried not to think about the cycle of change, the way time passed and even as Winter turned to Spring and Spring turned to Summer it never happened quite the same. Agatha hated sweating, a blemish on her mother’s image if her daughter had pit stains in her church clothes. She hated the sticky overwhelm, her hair clinging to her neck, nausea creeping in more easily. 

 

But she could take the unbearable heat if it meant seeing Rio in shorts. 

 

The Vidals hadn’t taken the news of suspension well, at least at first. Rio did the explaining, Agatha did the pouting and apologizing, feeling like she’d corrupted the syndicated princess, taught her how to break the rules. 

 

But Mrs. Vidal seemed a little less disturbed by it with the knowledge that Rio was confronting Wanda in the name of revenge. It was kind of jarring that her mother seemed less concerned when given a clear motive, like she needed a reason for it to make sense. Rio’s father was elated to learn that no punches were actually thrown, seemingly scared of the potential strength of his own daughter, as if he wasn’t built like a line backer, as if his daughter wasn’t built like a string bean.

 

But being that they weren’t exactly Agatha’s legal guardians, they hadn’t forced her to go to school without Rio, had sort of assumed they’d be home together Thursday and Friday.

 

So instead of some unnecessary punishment, like sending Agatha home or confiscating Rio’s phone, her parents had left her a list of chores to do while not in school, a list that seemed plausible to complete between the two of them.

 

Rio was focused on cutting the lawn, an electric lawn mower roaring as she clenched the handle with both hands, an AirPod in her left ear, it’s counterpart in Agatha’s right. She’s got on clear protective glasses, a shield from the dirt and grass being kicked up towards her. Agatha tries not to stare at the black tank top, the neck line that falls lower than an average T-shirt, collarbones glowing under the early afternoon sunlight. But even worse are the light pink running shorts that are loose around her hips, the tie at the front working overtime in keeping them up, short enough to expose inner thighs, an expanse of skin that rarely gets to see the sun, a lot shorter than their uniform skirts. 

 

The heat of her body isn’t just from the high temperatures, a dull ache she can’t push away anymore.

 

Agatha swallows, focusing back on the task at hand, refilling the hummingbird feeder with sugar water. She places it back on its perch, begging her hands to stay steady, letting the weight of it settle into place. Moving onto the other feeder, she fills it with bird seed from a bag in the garage. The tasks seem small, but feel significant, like she’s providing something, not repaying the Vidal’s exactly, but adding something in, doing something out of desire rather than expectation. 

 

She pulls her phone out of her pocket, changing the song, perhaps an attempt at getting Rio’s attention simply because she wants it, not exactly having something to say, but missing the crisp burn of brown eyes.

 

SOMEBODY CALL 911 SHAWTY FIRE BURNING ON THE DANCE FLOOR

 

Sean Kingston’s voice suddenly infiltrates both their ears, Rio’s head turning at break neck speed, making eye contact as she mouths the lyrics intensely, wiggling her body in a goofy collapse of limbs that still somehow makes Agatha’s heart stutter. 

 

This fucking dumbass.

 

Agatha wanted to kiss her so fucking bad.

 

She puts her phone back into her pocket, a pair of jean shorts she’d stolen from Rio’s closet, before walking towards her without hesitation, clear minded enough to stay out of the path of the mower, but wanting to be next to her, needing to see the beads of sweat on Rio’s neck up close.  

 

They don’t speak, no pressure to exchange words against the surging pulse of the lawn mower. Instead Agatha’s arms snake around Rio’s stomach from behind, pull her in close enough to rest her chin on an exposed shoulder, feel the distinct warmth of sun kissed skin. Rio stops her wiggling, giving Agatha’s hold more chance to stick, finding cautious romance in the physical touch lived in the same moment of Fire Burning blaring in their ears. The hold isn’t enough to stop all of Rio’s movement, still walking forward, pushing the mower with Agatha matching the pace, clinging like a car being towed. 

 

Rio allows the contact, walking with more careful intention, not wanting to instigate any separation but still completing the task- at least until the song is over.

 

“You alright?” Rio voices, turning slightly as she flicks off the lawn mower, suddenly more interested in Agatha than finishing their chores. 

 

“Mmm,” Agatha hums into her skin, pressing a few light kisses along the side of her neck, content to feel the softness against her lips for the foreseeable future, she can feel Rio buzz under the contact, “Just missed you.”

 

It doesn’t make sense, missing her. They’d been together more than usual, even for just a couple of days, there wasn’t the normal time apart, like they were handcuffed together, only apart when one of them wanted to shower or had to pee. She’d like to say it was a surprise, like she thought spending every waking moment next to Rio might be a learning curve, but it felt so natural, something in her soul put at ease with the other girl close, her sleep feeling more recharging than usual with Rio’s arm wrapped around her in spite of the gnawing anxieties on the horizon. It felt simple, grounding. A new rhythm that they shifted into with ease.

 

It had only been two days, but it already felt like a new habit, a fulfilling ritual, an inevitability that would be two hearts beating to the same curated playlist. 

 

Rio turns fully then, presses slightly out of the loose hold, just enough to see Agatha’s face, her hands still draped around her hips, now from the front, her nose skimming under Rio’s ear before coming face to face. 

 

Rio’s hand comes up to brush a stray strand of hair out of her face, the pieces framing her face too short to get into the small bun, before claiming a spot against Agatha’s jaw.

 

The song playing through their ears now is a chirpy pop song from the early 2000s, a name Agatha can’t place, a one-hit wonder. But the lyrics, the beat, sink to the bottom of her priorities, the playful smile on Rio’s lips taking all her attention, fighting with the need to stare endlessly into coffee brown irises, slide further into the golden glint reflected in the bright sky. Rio’s lips only look more inviting as she wets them with her own tongue, mushes them together to complete the mindless tick, the oral fixation on full display, a constant need to move. 

 

Agatha contemplates putting it to good use, hoping to be on the receiving end of well-intentioned bites, has yet to fully know the capability of pink lips and skillful tongue. It feels like its only getting harder by the minute, pretending she doesn’t want all of Rio, fighting the parts of her brain that protest, wicked verses that remind her of sin, premarital sex, not to mention woman laying with woman. 

 

It feels like background noise, idle chatter from the studio audience, an echo of disgruntled customers. Contending with her own identity had always slammed back to this. It was easier to live with the reality of being a homosexual when she wasn’t acting on it, could convince herself this wasn’t wrong if she never acted on it.

 

And that had sort of sat on the back burner, something she hadn’t conflated with, convincing herself they’d never be in this position. But Agatha had kissed her, had wanted to kiss her so badly, steered by her passion in a way that didn’t leave room to question. 

 

Maybe it was just the insecurity talking, the desire to get this right, to please Rio in all the ways she didn’t know how. She tried to be rational, remind herself of Rio’s patience, that there would undoubtedly be a learning curve, but the inevitable stumbling already felt like a failure, a harsh place to judge herself for the slip-ups that were yet to happen. Perhaps it was easier this way, pressing it out like dough to be rolled, pushing on all the air bubbles of distinct trouble, labeling them as something else. 

 

A sin. 

 

“You okay?” Rio’s eyes scan over her face, sensing something Agatha isn’t fully presenting, but not putting in the effort to hide either. 

 

Agatha can feel the damp exterior of Rio’s tank top, the sear of warmth floating beneath, but it doesn’t burn her, doesn’t force her to retreat. Instead it lures her in further, an idle fire that burns slow and deliberate. A safe place to bury her seeds. 

 

Blue eyes shine with a sign of deep satisfaction, a quaking desire to confess. She nods instead, the swirling desires to keep Rio happy brushing firmly over her chest. Words don’t come but she leans forward filling the rest of Rio’s personal space.

 

Brown eyes snag on pink lips, no smirk, no quiet elation, just something disarmed, like Agatha’s proximity was starting to take hold, coax her closer to the edge. It didn’t feel like a battle anymore, a place where every kiss was a traitorous victory. It felt natural, something Agatha no longer felt guilty for wanting. And Rio wasn’t being smug about it, wasn’t teasing her, she was just falling in, basking in the sparkling progress.

 

Agatha kisses her, something firm and solid, out in the open on Rio’s front lawn, the hot air clinging to them, undeterred by the marks of sweat, the charged restraint in Rio’s hand staying put on Agatha’s face. 

 

“Baby,” Rio gasps into her mouth, like she’d suddenly remembered where they were, what they were doing, “someone might see.”

 

Agatha’s hold only tightens against her hips, shuts Rio up with her own mouth, tilts her head to bring her closer. She doesn’t have to say ‘I don’t care’ for Rio to know.

 

Because Rio was kissing her back, because Evanora already knew, because Rio’s parents were both at work, because no one else mattered. 

 

It felt like another rope being cut, like the weight of her expectations were slowly being trimmed away, weary leaves sheared off, steadily replaced by even growth. 

 

The moment doesn’t erase all the wicked pain, doesn’t solve the rubik's cube of self-doubt in her mind, but it heals a small tether, ties a new knot along the pathways in her brain that sew self-love, the neurons creating new patterns, making the emotions easier to find again later. Proverbs 30:5-6 - Every word of God proves true; he is a shield to those who take refuge in him. Do not add to his words, lest he rebuke you and you be found a liar. 

 

Church was an inevitability. 

 

Every Sunday for as long as she could remember. Sunday mornings were a dedicated tradition, a road she had no opportunity to turn away from. 

 

As a child, it felt like connection, protection. A place where she was safe from her mother’s cold words and unrelenting hands. A time where prayer still felt like a means for better.

 

For all Hail Mary’s, for all the Our Father’s, Agatha’s mother still hit her with shoes, still pushed her, still wound callous insults around her soul, still withheld basic necessities. 

 

Somewhere along the way it shifted, prayer made her feel powerless, like a slave to an unresolved story, a ritual she still completed for the sake of falling in line, another expectation she could not divert from if it meant securing her own safety.

 

For the Vidal’s it had always been about honoring the people that came before them, following in the beliefs of their parents and their grandparents. 

 

Rio’s parents were believers, had felt the protection of community, saw the ideals as guidelines to be moral people, didn’t use the gospel to cast judgement.

”Okay.” Agatha nods, pushing down the unraveling fear, using this as another step towards freedom, at the very least wanting to show Evanora that this was the last time she’d fall under her control, set the record straight. 

 

Maybe it was a little selfish, needing to spit in the face of her abuser, even if in a metaphorical small way, this ploy, whatever it would consist of, felt like the final act in this tragedy. 

 

Father Buchanan smiles again, his teeth glinting off the sharp lighting like he’d just saved a kitten from a tree, returned the pet to their rightful owner. Agatha let him hold the joy, a place where this could breathe and not spell hatred.
