Her mother never waited long to stop holding in the hatred, often spewing her callous corrections as soon as others were out of earshot. But now, the only sounds filling the unblemished insides of Evanora’s SUV were coming from the radio, the cycle of hymns playing quiet enough to be a subliminal ploy. 

 

Pulling into the driveway presses them into a reality where this was never out of the norm, like Agatha had been home all along, coming home from Sunday church as mother and daughter, as they had for as long as Agatha could remember. It sparks the ritual of memory, a cavernous regret, the truth that she’d be saying goodbye to all of this for good, that none of the little moments could be salvaged, even the ones that felt like reprieve, even the ones that felt neutral. Truthfully, Agatha never expected the reality of it to bleed around her strength, to feel like something she was losing. 

 

The same jostle of the car as it pulled over the pothole in the driveway, the way the porch light flickered on from the movement even in the daylight, the silver cross that hung on the door, the way she had to jiggle the key to open the screen door. Small things that no one else would know about a home that held her blood in it’s walls. The echoes of hallways that could spin the tales apart from the truth, the screams of pain, the scars of deceit and neglect. 

 

A cocoon of drafted thesis, a book to close and never read again. Agatha would walk away from here and never be able to trace the schemes again. 

 

“Sit. I’ll make you some tea.” 

 

Evanora’s voice is startling, the soured inflection absent, replaced by something sticky and sweet, a surprise, a promise. 

 

Agatha listens to her command, sits at the kitchen table in her usual spot, making sure not to mess up the placemat. She sticks to the thought that this is another act, another calculated ploy, dedicating herself to letting it pan out a bit further, just to pull at the thread, unravel the knot without getting tangled in it. 

 

This is not Evanora. 

 

At least not in true form.

 

The clarity in her eyes something forced. 

 

Agatha waits for the axe to drop. 

 

The kettle boils. Tea is served. A table spoon of honey. Mixed with care. 

 

Agatha watches the steam, waits for it to cool. Reads the Bible quote etched into the ceramic mug. 

 

“I tell you the truth, a time is coming and has now come when the dead will hear the voice of the Son of God and those who hear will live.” -John 5:25 

 

Evanora finally takes her seat. Her own mug steaming. 

 

“I’m so glad you’re home, sweetheart.” Evanora starts, eyes downcast on her own hands, a soft smile coating her features, “I knew you’d get tired of that girl and find your way back to the Lord.” 

 

Agatha clears her throat, the first attempt at using her own words, straying from the path her mother had always set for her to follow. 

 

“It’s okay, you’re home now. I accept your apology.”

 

”I’m not apologizing.” the words creak out, sounding more aggressive in her head, reveling in the way they’d at least found the air. 

 

Evanora’s face morphs, eyebrows scrunching in confusion. 

 

“Don’t you think an apology is necessary to get us back on track, sweetheart?” Evanora’s voice teeters closer to its usual tone, but doesn't quite break from the careful sweetness either. 

 

This doesn’t feel like her life. Maybe a sitcom version, twisted to show only the brightest colors. A side character, always hidden, always beaten down, thrust into the leading role. She can’t remember her lines, or the way she’s supposed to move. But the truth of her feelings bubble up from somewhere deep. A wave she can’t push back.

 

The anger kicks in like a collapsing building, the fire of it reaching her ears. Agatha is glad to already be seated, the quaking emotion feeling like a jolt she can’t contain. 

 

“You think you got me back that easy? You think I got a taste of freedom and want this back?” Agatha pleas, hating the way her voice sounds, broken. 

 

She wants to wield the anger, throw stones without emotion, but she isn’t her mother, the surge of frustration free for Evanora’s eyes to devour. 

 

“I think you should know your place, Agatha. I think you know the consequences of disobedience. I’ve taught you better than to run away from God. You treat your life as if it is not a blessing. You act like I haven’t sacrificed everything to make you holy. Yet all you’ve done is disrespect me.”

 

Each syllable presses against Agatha’s skull like a needle, her fingers pressed firmly into the arms of the chair, white knuckling to stop herself from ripping off her own skin. Lies. A crooked retelling, the disjointed perspective of a woman she’ll never understand. 

 

”Mother,” Agatha begs, finding the part of her that wants to believe her mother has a heart, can still speak to reason, “We are the only two people that know what’s truly happened in this house. I’m not a kid anymore. This isn’t right.”

 

The damn breaks, the crack in her voice running parallel to the tears that finally fall. It feels like a failure, a clear indication that Evanora is affecting her, it sinks in the ways they are different, Agatha actually capable of human emotion. It still stings, the curse of trauma that hasn’t left her bones, the way her mother’s cheeks remain dry, a sign that she has won.

 

”You are being foolish, child.” Evanora shakes her head, the full depth of her ire embedded in each word, no longer putting on the mask of aloof grace.  “Drink your tea.”

 

Dismissed.

 

Agatha’s hand moves on its own accord, a pattern of following orders that she can’t shake. Her fingers flex around the handle, a quiet voice in her mind that sings.

 

Maybe Evanora is right. A sip of tea will do some good, relax her senses for just a moment.

 

She looks into the steam, as she moves the mug towards her mouth.

 

Bubbles.

 

Agatha pushes up from the table, the mug slammed against the table. Standing now, needing to move away from the truth she’d seen with her own eyes. 

 

Poison. Fucking poison. 

 

“You-,” Agatha stains, unsure how to confront it out loud, her brain still catching up, she can feel the tears dripping down her face, the cool ache that pulls at the sweat on the back of her neck, the shaking in her hands, “You rather kill me, then let me be happy.”

 

”Happy?” Evanora scoffs, blowing at her own tea, still seemingly unbothered. “You’re confusing sin with love, darling.”

 

”You fucking hypocrite,” Agatha seethes, her fist slamming into the wood, the pain shooting up her arm, but it finally gets Evanora to stir, her eyes widening at the act of rage, a breaking point, untamed. “You’ve pretended abuse was love my entire life, spit in my face and acted like you were teaching me right from wrong with a wooden spoon to the head. And you have the fucking nerve to judge me.”

 

The fight in her ebbs out in sobs, drowning around the chorus of cries, still waiting for a reaction, needing to be acknowledged. 

 

“You have always been an ungrateful demon child,” Evanora finally rises from her own seat, standing close enough to scream into Agatha’s face, a fight that they’d never stood on even playing field for. “And I will not let you throw away all I’ve given you.”

 

Evanora’s hands grab onto Agatha’s biceps pushing her backwards, the grip around each arm harsh and unrelenting. It doesn’t leave much time for a reaction, the thud of her own head hitting the wall behind her brings her back to reality. 

 

Agatha feels her own hands struggling to gain freedom, an attempt at breaking out of the grasp, a new approach to the mess of this, the first time she’s fighting back, the last time she’ll have to. 

 

“You must feel the consequences of your sins. You must face God’s wrath.” Evanora pushes her sideways, Agatha falling to the ground, her hands barely able to brace her fall, her hip and knee struck against the hardwood, “It is time to return to him, Agatha.”

 

Agatha scrambles to her feet, perhaps flight still being a better response than freeze, she sprints towards the front of the house, an attempt at making it out of the front door.

 

Evanora’s full weight collides into her just as she reaches for the lock, her wrist mangled against the knob. Her mother stands above her again, a blurred image of her limitless determination, she finds the will to give in. 

 

In the space of her front door, one step away from freedom. 

 

She hears the slap more than she feels it, the echo popping off her eardrum, the cold whip against her tear stains. 

 

Agatha grabs at Evanora’s wrist, pulls her down by her forearm, a final attempt.

 

”You were born evil.” Her mother grits out as they crash onto the floor, swinging her fist in quick succession, making contact with the side of Agatha’s head from the odd angle. 

 

“And who fucking made me?” Agatha calls back, grabbing hold of the wailing fist, twisting the arm backwards.

 

It doesn’t bloom closure in the way she thought it would, her mother’s pain unsatisfying.  

 

Fighting back seems to only stir more anger, this middle aged woman finding all her strength in creating as much damage as possible, undeterred by her daughter’s new found ability to defend herself. 

 

In another attempt at quelling the fight, Evanora headbutts her in the face, the hard surface of her forehead, smacking into Agatha’s nose. She can feel the cool trickles of blood from her nostrils, the new sense of urgency sliding away.

 

In the wake of trying to protect herself, Agatha realizes how exhausting it is, that perhaps she’d saved herself the hassle by taking it for years without any barriers, every push back or attempt to escape seemingly giving Evanora more like a power sucking super villain.

 

The fight for power stalls at the sound of movement upstairs, a sharp thud followed by quick footsteps, a thundering pace that grows louder as the intruder descends the stairs. 

 

Rio. 

 

How the fuck-

 

“Sorry to crash the tea party, Miss H.” Rio’s pace doesn’t falter as she comes to stand in front of Evanora.

 

Agatha doesn’t see her face, but she can hear the piercing edge, the anger that bleeds into fear, the way it's pressed down into something controlled. A brave face for them both. 

 

The shock shared between mother and daughter is possibly the closest thing they’ve had to a bonding experience in years. 

 

“You!” Evanora’s anger shoots back out, standing up in an instant, meeting Rio face to face, “The harlot that ruined my daughter.”

 

”Now is that any way to talk to your future daughter in law,” Rio’s admonishes, something jovial in her tone, refusing to meet the harsh grit of Evanora’s words, “Very unbecoming of a holy woman like yourself, Miss H.”

 

”Get out!” Evanora spits, not entertained by this play.

 

Agatha finally finds the will to stand up, she reads the stiff stance of Rio’s posture, the curled fists, an attempt at preservation. She can’t meet her eyes, can’t face the vulnerability. The pressure on her head comes flooding in, a feeling that throws her off balance. Agatha doesn’t feel herself falling, just the cold sweat, the dizzying nausea, and Rio’s arms around her, keeping her up. 

 

“Hey,” Rio’s voice is different, pressed into her ear, her arms so solid, her tone so soft, “It’s gonna be okay.”

 

”Leave her!” Evanora spits, “She belongs with her mother.”

 

Agatha faintly registers Evanora clawing at her, Rio pulling her closer, cradling the back of her head. 

 

“You are not a mother,” Rio speaks, clear and free.

 

Agatha hears the sound first, the crisp slap to Rio’s face, feels the jerk of it in the wake of the sound. She pulls away without a conscious thought, turns her body towards the attack, moves herself between Evanora and Rio. 

 

“Don’t fucking touch her,” Agatha sobs, a yell that scratches at her throat, she makes herself the shield, the protector. 

 

“You’re are going to hell.” Evanora’s words come out in a heated whisper, a last chance at wielding what’s left as Rio moves them both, taking Agatha by the arm, still unsure of her stability, pulling her towards the door. The words are pressed into the air as if to shatter her child’s world. 

 

And a year ago that might have worked. A reminder of the veil so tightly tied around her eyes, the cautious whisper of the girl she used to be, the child who obeyed. 

 

“We’ll see you there.” Agatha scoffs, letting Rio pull her along.

 

The front door slams behind them. The hurried steps continue, a floating sense where Agatha knows she’s moving her own feet, but she isn’t exactly feeling it. 

 

“How the fuck did you get here?” Agatha pulls out of Rio’s grasp, steadying herself, still processing the fact that she'd been there to witness that, unsure of where she wants to be grateful and be mad. Maybe it was the lack of understanding, or the minor concussion, but it all felt like too much.

 

“Keep walking.” Rio orders, it isn’t mean, just a clear demand, her arm wrapping around Agatha again, a guide, an anchor. 

 

“Rio.”

 

“We’ll talk when we get out of here.”

 

And there. That was the clarity she needed. That Rio wasn’t mad. Or at least not mad enough to let this ruin them. That they would talk. There would be room for understanding. 

 

That Rio wasn’t ignoring her. That Rio wanted her safe. Far away from this before they figured out how to move on. 

 

Agatha kept walking. 

 

A shriek of tires against pavement only makes the pain in her head worse, an older model minivan swerving to a stop on their side of the street.

 

What now?

 

“Get in.” Billy’s voice spills from the driver’s seat. 

 

Rio opens the door, helps Agatha into the backseat without much fight, the adrenaline wearing off. 

 

“You two okay?” He asks, eyes scanning their faces in the rear view mirror. He pulls napkins out of the glove box, shoves them into Rio’s hands.

 

There isn’t a verbal answer. A poised silence. Billy trains his eyes back on the road. 

 

“I feel like we just robbed a bank.” He laughs nervously, tapping the steering wheel like they’re in a high speed chase, not going 25 in the suburbs.

 

“Thank you, Billy.” Rio supplies, genuine, but still a mechanism of getting him to shut up. Rio presses the crumpled under Agatha’s nose, holds firm to stop the blood from flowing all over her, keeps her steady. 

 

”How did Billy know to-? How did you get here, Rio?” Agatha tries again, her brain still not computing how they had driven to church together with her parents, how Rio had somehow teleported into her house. She lets Rio stay close, tend to her nose.

 

“I heard them talking to you at church,” Rio starts, choking on her own words, knowing Agatha would keep spiraling the longer she made her wait, “When I saw you agreed, I thought I’d tag along. I hopped in her trunk right before you got to the car, that woman should really learn to lock her doors.”

 

Rio heard everything? Or…

 

”Where-“

 

”I was in the bushes, listening. When I heard yelling I climbed into your window.” Rio is sort of sheepish about it, her eyes trained on the task at hand, but not directly into her eyes. 

 

Agatha can read the hurt, the pain in dark irises even if they never fully show themselves.

 

“And Billy?”

 

”uh, Rio texted me. ‘SOS’ and your address. Stole my mom’s van from the garage.” He shrugs, chancing a look back at them at a stop sign. “Speaking of. Where exactly am I supposed to be going now?” 

 

“Uhh,” Rio ponders out loud, obviously not planning this far ahead.

 

”ooo,” Billy chirps, suddenly excited, “Do you wanna come over? My parents aren’t home. And I kind of need to be back before they realize the car is missing.”

 

”Sure,” Agatha sighs, not knowing where else to go.

 

“I’m sorry if I overstepped,” Rio whispers, retracting her confidence, not knowing the full depth of the complicated emotions Agatha was feeling.

 

Agatha scoots closer to press firmly into her side, holds onto Rio’s wrist, keeps her close. Agatha doesn’t have the words yet, but she knows this is better than what she left behind. 

 

—-

 

Ruth 1:16- But Ruth replied, “Do not urge me to leave you or to turn back from you. Where you go I will go, and where you stay I will stay. Your people will be my people and your God my God.”

 

A calm wind tangles against the wind chime, the sounds of nature wrapping Agatha in a hold that keeps her thoughts from running grim. 

 

A blanket on her shoulders that doesn’t stop her from shivering. Her nervous system still quieting.

 

Billy’s backyard is pretty small. She can see the next 3 yards from the back deck, tucked into a corner seat. Her nose no longer bleeding but the area still feeling dry and raw.

 

Rio stands by the railing, leaned up against it, looking up at the clouds, Agatha can only see the side of her face. 

 

Billy brings out a snack board with sliced apples, mixed nuts, capri suns, doing his best to play the part of a good host. 

 

“I’ll be inside if you need anything.” He says awkwardly, drawing more attention to the silence, the delicate bubbling of processing before he disappears back inside. 

 

“Why’d you go with her?” Rio asks after a few more moments of cautious wind and no words, she doesn’t sound angry, halted static to the way she holds her body so taught. 

 

The windchime wrinkles the sound between them. A third person in their conversation. She lets the wind speak before opting for her own turn. 

 

“Closure maybe.” Agatha shrugs. “Give her a chance to come to her senses.”

 

Rio nods. 

 

“I never intended to stay there. Or not tell you where I was going.” Agatha tries to clarify. 

 

“I’m sorry.” She tacks on. Meaning it. Really fucking meaning it.

 

Rio turns to her, the sadness in her face trembling like a quiet surrender. A heartbreaking truth to the stories she’d only heard from Agatha’s mouth. It’s not like she didn’t believe her, but seeing Evanora in action was something different.

 

She steps forward into Agatha’s space, her hands on her face. Rio places a delicate kiss onto her hairline, stays close even after the graze of her lips. 

 

“I’m just glad you’re okay.” She whispers into her skin, a solid confession that floats over the broken in her voice. 

 

Agatha’s arms pull her closer around the waist, an awkward angle as she remains seated, but she pushes forward, her face pressed firmly into Rio’s chest, needing the tangible reminder of her existence, sighing at the reality of Rio’s heart beat pulsing against her ear. 

 

“I should have known better,” Agatha sobs into her, mad at herself for giving Evanora a chance to redeem herself, a hair of room to weasel her way back in, even if they’d escaped. 

 

Rio only holds her tighter, scratches at the nape of her neck. 

 

“You’re not wrong for wanting her to act like a mother.” Rio tries, her voice soft, a careful press of solid wishes, a truth she needs Agatha to hear, “I could never blame you for that.”

 

Agatha pulls back slightly, needing to see Rio’s face, wanting with everything in her to kiss her. She slides her hand over Rio’s collar bone, finds brown eyes that allow tears to fall too, an oath they’d both taken to feel their feelings out in the open. 

 

“I’m sorry I let her hit you,” Agatha’s voice breaks as her hand glides over her cheek, a stroke of her fingers over the same spot Evanora had assaulted. 

 

Rio’s fingers lace around her wrist, shaking her head. 

 

“Stop apologizing for her.”

 

Agatha nods.

 

Tilting her head up to further enter her space, pushing up to slide forward to connect their lips. Rio doesn’t hesitate to meet her half way, a calming sigh that slides from Rio’s mouth into hers, a searing breath that reminds them both of the passion that only spoke in their silence. A place to return to, a comfort in the soaring flame. 

 

“Am I hurting your nose?” Rio whispers into her, a spilled out moment of making sure.

 

”Shut up and let me kiss you.”

 

Agatha can feel the upturn of RIo’s lips against her, the temptation of a smirk hiding in the clash of lips, the droplet of amusement in the bucket of doom, something to cling to, knowing tomorrow has the room to be better.

Chapter 16

Chapter Notes

IMMMM ALIVEEE
…sorry its been quite a bit since my last update
Life is…idk anymore…but I’ve been trying to figure out this chapter for what feels like forever just glad I finally got through it

See the end of the chapter for more notes

James 1:2- Consider it pure joy, my brothers and sisters, whenever you face trials of many kinds

 

By the time Rio is turning her key in the door, the afternoon heat has set in. The sting of sweat nips at the back of Agatha’s neck, a dense fear of awaiting gloom. She isn’t sure what they’ll find inside, the tides that will turn from their presence, the unfurling explanation of events. 

 

The unknown has always been an easy thing to stress over, but the pattern of acceptance was starting to rewire Agatha’s brain, the angel on her shoulder coaxing her out of a renewed panic attack.

 

It’s just Rio’s parents. They care about her. They love her.

 

Rio’s mother is at the door as it opens, fussing over them, taking them into her arms, looking over them to confirm they’re both okay, caressing Rio’s cheek, squeezing Agatha’s shoulder. She curses under her breath in Spanish as she moves. 

 

“Where’s Papa?” Rio breathes, finally able to find words. 

 

“He went back to the church about an hour ago, he thought maybe you’d go back there.” Mrs. Vidal sighs, “I’ve been calling you nonstop where have you two been?” the timber in her voice growing, teetering back towards anger now knowing they were safe.

 

”Mami,” Rio grabs her by the shoulders, “Let me call Papa and tell him to come home, okay?” She tries to calm her, somehow striking back as the voice of reason. 

 

“Mierda, Chispita, I’m not thinking straight.” 

 

“Here,” Agatha steps in, taking her hands, “Let’s sit down.” They step towards the couch as Rio pulls out her phone, taking a seat together on the sofa. 

 

Mrs. Vidal pulls Agatha into her, a safe connection, a maternal warmth that sinks through the layers of skin, she caresses Agatha’s hair, looks at her with gentle worry, still overcome by their previous absence. 

 

“Yes, Papa, we’re safe.” Rio says into her phone, Agatha swears she can hear her father’s relieved sigh even with the phone held up to Rio’s ear. 

 

They sit in silence while they wait for his return, the TV playing reruns of family feud, Agatha content to stay in the proximity of Mrs. Vidal. 

 

Rio meets him at the door as he arrives, letting him pull her into him, the cocoon of his body holding her like a shield.

 

”Aye, Rio. We were so worried.” His voice aches between anguish and fear, the reality that his daughter had vanished for hours without a word.

 

They sit in the living room. Her father in his designated chair, Rio perched on the armrest, Agatha and Mrs. Vidal still sat on the other section of couch.

 

They don’t rehash it all, just mark the occasion as a continuation of abuse, Rio does most of the talking, places the responsibility on herself for not telling them where they were going, allows Agatha the room to add in necessary details.

 

It feels like a dust cloud, something lethargic in freeing the words from the cage in her chest. Agatha sort of understands why people go to therapy. 

 

“I’m sorry for dragging Rio into this.” Agatha offers, earnestly, feeling for the first time the care of a family, knowing the pain of losing it.

 

”You didn’t drag me into anything.” Rio shakes her head, brown eyes welling slightly, “I followed, that was my choice.”

 

“She’s always been protective, Agatha,” Mr. Vidal recalls wistfully, seemingly less on edge after knowing where they were, that Rio had followed in an attempt to keep Agatha safe. “None of us are going to change that.” He adds with resigned acceptance.

 

They don’t talk about the poison, or the wicked intentions, an unspoken choice in the way Rio’s eyes darken, Agatha swallows harshly, a sense of worry that doesn’t need to reach her parent’s ears. 

 

Regardless, they don’t let Agatha hold the blame, a reassurance with gentle words, the way Rio’s mother never loses the grip on her hand. 

 

“I called CPS.” Mrs. Vidal confesses, her head in her hands, needing to get the truth out before it consumed her.

 

”Mami,” Rio scolds, angry but unsurprised.

 

”She wanted to call 911, too,” Her father chimes, “You should be glad I convinced her to wait a few more hours.”

 

”It’s okay,” Agatha sighs, “I’ll deal with it.”

 

”They said they have to investigate the report, they might try to speak to you about everything, but hopefully it will help.”

 

”I’m just waiting to be 18.” Agatha explains, resigned to the reality that she knows how this will play out, Evanora using her power to get out of any consequences, “there’s no point in being placed in foster care or getting emancipated when I’m going to be a legal adult in 3 months.”

 

”I’m sorry.” Mrs. Vidal whispers, “I wasn’t trying to make this harder.”

 

”I know.”

 

It sings to all the times that Evanora had never apologized for things with evil intent, that Rio’s mother had so innately offered her love and care, that she was apologizing when she was only trying to help, it weighed heavy on the truth, a reminder that she’d walked away, but there was nothing there to lose, that leaving Evanora only meant walking closer towards this. The intention of people who valued her health, her feelings, who wanted her to thrive. 

 

Part of it still feels like a fairytale, a lost dream that she can’t touch, sliding away as she tries to grasp its edges, but Rio’s eyes feel solid, the unwavering press of support. A reminder that stepping into the unknown is scary, but she doesn’t have to do it alone, tethered instead to the people who are willing to catch her if she falls. 

 

“Sooo,” Rio adjusts herself on the arm of the chair, the conversation coming to a natural end, she teeters on finding the right words, a moment of silence that could last forever. “The gay thing?”

 

To anyone else, Rio isn’t moved by the new conversation, unafraid of the chance at rejection, but Agatha can hear the ache in the mid tone of her voice, knows the anxious movement of her fingers.

 

”We kind of figured,” Mrs. Vidal shrugs, smiles, all warmth and patience, like she would have waited forever for her daughter to be ready to say it out loud. 

 

Rio’s head swings to face her father, gauges his reaction too, takes in the way he nods, chuckles at the way Rio seems genuinely surprised.

 

”But I was so good at hiding it!” Rio shrieks, exasperated. 

 

The high pitched lilt stirs a laugh from Agatha as well, a curtain of happiness that shields her from the harsh tricks of the light. 

 

“Have you seen the way you look at her?” Mr. Vidal chimes in, nodding his head towards Agatha as he directs the question at his daughter, “We’re not blind.”

 

”Woah,” Rio hops up, fully standing now, ready to get to the bottom of this, “What if Agatha wasn’t into me? You totally blew up my spot with that.” 

 

“Oh, so you two are together?” Mrs. Vidal laughs, getting the exact confirmation they needed. 

 

“Dude,” Agatha admonishes, “You just fell into their trap.”

 

”I’m dumb,” Rio face palms, realizing too late that she’d probably just sabotaged the chances of Agatha continuing to sleep in her room. 

 

“You’re not dumb, Chispita. Just a useless lesbian.” Her father teases without hesitation.

 

”Where did you learn that?” Rio’s head snaps back up, “Mami, take his phone. He’s not allowed on the internet anymore.”

 

Surprisingly, there isn’t a conversation about Agatha sleeping in the guest room. No teasing statements about using protection, just a sharp look of support, a kiss to Rio’s forehead, a hug that makes Agatha feel like she might shatter. 

 

They order food, never setting the table, keeping the comfort of the living room. Rio fills cups with juice, Agatha grabs forks. 

 

Rio looks at her softly when they’re alone in the kitchen, almost spills. It’s a swirl of concern, no regret, just something steady and blooming, witnessing the resilience in the way they were both still standing in the wake of unspeakable events, sharing a moment that was just them again.

 

Circling like orbiting planets, never too far away, always due to crash back together. 

 

“Let me take one before you drop something, clumsy” Agatha teases, a breath of something that feels normal, Agatha being nice to be mean.

 

”Agatha,” Rio smiles sadly, a course of trying to hold it together after her front row seat to the show, still processing, a burden that would take time to sort through, her hand clenched around the plastic cup, her fingers standing in for the harsh grasp on her resolve. 

 

“Give me the cup, Rio.” Agatha coaxes it out of her hand gently, presses a kiss to her cheek, waits for the resounding exhale. 

 

Rio tucks between Agatha and her mother on the couch, they all wordlessly eat, someone turns on The Parent Trap, a movie they’d all seen a million times. Agatha tries to offer silent connection, their thighs touching, Rio’s elbow resting against her ribs as she eats.

 

It’s a sturdy comfort. The warm food in her hands, placed there as an unquestioned necessity. The ease of company, the seamless wheel of care always turning. The gentle quiet of no expectations to say the right thing, to fall in line.

 

For the first time in a long time, existence felt more like a choice, a careful path that opened up, direction unclear.

 

The story altered by her own hand. 

 

It was scary, not having the next chapter seared into the Earth by God’s hand, by Evanora’s guidance, but it felt like power, a sense she’d learned to like, power in her words, in her voice. 

 

The truth of it surged through Agatha like a crystalline current, a torch of lilac fire. A taste of something she wanted more of. 

 

Rio’s room starts to feel like a safe haven. Less than a week of this and she’s already sleeping much better. Maybe it’s the security of Rio next to her, the warmth and continuity. “What ya reading?” She asks as she moves to take her coat off, noticing the cup of coffee already on her side of the table, smirking at the seamless way they cared for each other without having to speak it, the cap slightly off to let it cool, the 2 packs of sugar left beside it.

Rio smiled at the way Agatha didn’t move to put down the book, the fact that Agatha was still chronically not online and had no idea what Billy had gotten her into.

 

”C’mon darling, supper is getting cold,” Rio jokes in an old-timey accent, pushing Agatha’s food towards her, the words landing even if both her bagel and juice were already intentionally cold. Rio grabs the orange juice, opening it for her without a second thought.

 

Agatha closes the book after a moment, saving her place. Rio had always joked that Agatha must be a serial killer, never using a bookmark, never dog-earring the page, simply remembering the page number and never forgetting it. 

 

Rio watches as Agatha takes off her glasses, placing them in the front of her shirt, before ripping open the wrapping of her bagel, basking in the way she was still taken with simple joys, perhaps conditioned to not take small things for granted, and while Rio had no questions about the ugly truth of where those habits were born from, it didn’t stop her from admiring the way Agatha took her time, accessed and calculated, make sure of what she wanted before she enjoyed it. 

 

It made it feel even more remarkable when she’d realized that she herself was one of the things Agatha had chosen, that they’d built this life together, cautious and not always confident, what always remained was the choice to do it together.

 

Agatha sighs at the first bite of her bagel, an order she’d perfected and never strayed from, an onion bagel with cream cheese and lox, and god forbid, never toasted, a splurge for smoked salmon with today’s inflation that Rio never hesitated on, well worth it to make Agatha happy, even if she needed a mint after. 

 

“Stop staring at me,” Agatha says between bites, kicking Rio lightly under the table.

 

”I’m not,” Rio almost chokes on her own bagel, an everything bagel toasted with veggie cream cheese, “I’m just- admiring.”

 

Agatha rolls her eyes, but it’s more out of amusement than frustration, the way Rio still looked like a fawning cartoon character, actual heart eyes reflected in brown irises for her. After years of unfiltered love, the shattering care of Rio’s attention hadn’t waned, but Agatha had become more comfortable under its weight.

 

It no longer felt like big shoes to fill, a person Rio thought she loved, but didn’t know the whole of. It no longer scared her, because this had finally started to feel like breathing, like she wasn’t climbing out of a trap of self-hatred anymore, this wasn’t a place to hide, a place to run from. Rio’s gaze is where she came to rest, where she came to thrive. The home they had built existed outside of the walls of their apartment, an ease that held across state lines, with oceans between them, a knowing that held all her grievances with life and still chose to keep going. 

 

Rio remembers a promise she made Agatha when they were 17. 

 

A promise that she couldn’t foresee the future, that there was no way to know who they’d be 10, 20 years from now, if they’d grow together or apart.

 

A promise that a chance at better was enough for her, that she’d stick around through the moments that felt like stabbing edges, the lashing out, the nightmares, the pain of lapsing habits. That she was willing to use their love as a jumping off point for all the potential offshoots of hope. That the chance at better was worth every attempt even if at times it felt hopeless. 

 

The outcome was better than either could have ever imagined.

 

She’s just glad they took that chance.

 

Rio’s heart swells as she walks home in the cold, fighting a smile that makes her look like a goofball. She’ll wait impatiently in the apartment for Agatha to finish work, pass the time letting Scratchy chase her around the apartment, texting Billy to stop teaching Agatha about books that will take up all her time, setting the thermostat warmer.

 

It's a good problem to have, waiting for the woman she loves, even if she just saw her. A testament to fate, the flames lit a long time ago, that still burn. 

 

Rio thinks about God, about the things she’d lost and gained. The power of those teachings reflected in love, the power she sees in Agatha now. She thinks about destiny, being made with someone else in mind. 

 

She tucks herself against the couch, Scratchy tired from running around, curled against her thigh as she opens her laptop. 

 

“Can you help me pick one out?” Rio pats gently behind his ears, scrolling through tabs for engagement rings. 

 

When Rio sends some screen shots of potential rings to her parents (Scratchy not exactly a great helper), she laughs at her father’s immediate response.

 

‘it’s about fucking time’

 

Chapter End Notes

Ummmmm I think my brain sort of didn’t allow me to start writing this for a while because that means the story is over…but i also wanted to do them justice and put time and care into where they ended up. I hope i was able to give them the ending that they and you the reader deserve. But I’m glad we got to the end. Thank you to anyone who has read even a sentence of this fic, I’m glad we can all escape from the crazy of the world in these lesbian witches.

PS. I made some fan art for this chapter, if u wanna check it out it will be on my tumblr…

PPS its canon in this fic that Evanora got hit by a car like 2 years after they graduated high school and died a painful death…She of course donated all her money to the church…but Rio and Agatha threw a little party…complete with balloons and a cake…that being said i did not want to write that in and take away from the pure joy
